Based on the shiurim of HaGaon HaRav Yitzchak Berkovits shlit"a

p. 1Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Hilchos Bishul

1. What Constitutes Bishul

The Issur Doraisa: What Gets Cooked?

The Melacha of bishul (Av Melacha: cooking/baking - 'haofeh') covers any significant transformation of food or material through heat.

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Rambam (plain reading / R' Akiva Eiger)

No chiyuv doraisa for cooking food that is edible raw - only for food that is inedible raw

Halacha does NOT follow this reading

Mishnah Berurah's reading of Rambam

Chayav even for raw-edible food, if the cooking improves it. Only excluded if there is no improvement at all

Still a minority position

Tosefos, Kol Bo, Riva, Ohr Zarua

Assur midoraisa to cook raw food even if edible beforehand - no distinction

This is the accepted halacha

Halacha L'Maaseh

Assur midoraisa to cook any food that is edible raw. If cooking makes food worse, may only be assur miderabanan.

p. 2Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Yad Soledes Bo (YSB) - The Temperature Threshold

Bishul only takes effect at or above the temperature of Yad soledes bo. Below this temperature there is no Torah prohibition. One may not rely on one's own hand to test this - the assessment is subjective and may differ from Talmudic times.

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Must be concerned from 43°C / ~109°F

Most stringent

Rav Bentsion Abba Shaul

Must be concerned from 40°C / ~104°F

Most stringent

Rav Shlomo Zalman Auerbach

YSB begins at 45°C / ~113°F (based on goose blood measurement)

Most lenient of the three

Practical Rule:

Treat anything above 40°C (104°F) as potentially YSB. You cannot test with your hand.

Common benchmark: food that you cannot hold in your closed hand without discomfort is at or above YSB.

Maachal Ben Drussai (MB'D) - The 'Begun Cooking' Threshold

A person is chayav for bishul once the food reaches the equivalent of one-third cooked (Rashi) or one-half cooked (Rambam) - the point at which a person would eat the food only in a time of great need (b'shaas hadchak).

p. 3Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Practical implication: food that has reached MB'D on Shabbos cannot be further cooked on Shabbos even to complete the cooking - it has already triggered the issur.

Leaving Food Near Fire Where It Could Reach YSB

ScenarioHalacha

Leaving uncooked liquid in a place where it can eventually reach YSB (even if intent is to remove it first)

FORBIDDEN miderabanan - gezeira that one may forget and it will reach YSB (SA 318:14, Rash)

Leaving uncooked liquid in a place where it could NEVER reach YSB

PERMITTED

Leaving uncooked solid food where it could reach MB'D

FORBIDDEN miderabanan - same gezeira applies (Rama 318:14)

2. Ein Bishul Achar Bishul - No Recooking of Cooked Food

The Core Rule

Once food has been fully cooked, there is no issur doraisa to cook it again in the same medium. This is the principle of 'Ein bishul achar bishul' (EBA'B).

p. 4Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Dvar Yavesh (Dry Solid Food) - Simple Case

Food Type / ScenarioHalacha

Dry, fully cooked solid food - reheating on Shabbos

PERMITTED midoraisa - EBA'B applies. Effect of cooking never disappears from dry food.

Dry, fully cooked solid food - placing near the fire where it will get hot but NOT roast

PERMITTED (Chazon Ish: the Re'eim's concern about tsli only applies when food actually gains taam tsli)

Dry solid food - placed on hotplate and will become roasted/toasted (taam tsli)

Assur - this is tsli achar bishul; the change in texture is significant

Dvar Lach (Liquid / Cooked Liquid) - Bishul Achar Bishul

Liquids are fundamentally different: if a cooked liquid cools down, the question is whether the effect of cooking 'disappears,' triggering a new issur bishul when reheated.

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Rashi

There IS bishul achar bishul with liquid - once liquid goes below YSB, it is assur to reheat it above YSB, even if still warm

Strictest position

Rashba (and Rambam per Chazon Ish)

NO bishul achar bishul with liquid - even cold cooked liquid may be reheated freely

Leniency not accepted as minhag

Rabbeinu Yerucham

Bishul achar bishul only applies when the liquid is 'mistamek veyafeh lo' (improves while cooking). If it is 'mistamek verah lo' (gets worse, e.g. boiling away), may reheat.

Rav Ovadia Yosef is lenient

Rama (SA 318:15)

Lenient (like Rashba) until liquid is 'nistanen legamrei' - fully cooled down. Once fully cooled, forbidden.

The accepted Ashkenazi practice

Shulchan Aruch HaRav

'Nistanen legamrei' = when most people would not eat it at this temperature (even if still slightly warm)

Stricter than Chazon Ish

Chazon Ish / Rav Moshe / Rav Wosner

'Nistanen legamrei' = actual room temperature; any warmth at all means it is mutar to reheat

Lenient

Rav Berkovits

Rules like Shulchan Aruch HaRav. Also: the Rama's prohibition on fully cooled liquid is a Minhag/chumra, not issur doraisa (following Chazon Ish).

Key practical consequence: more room to combine leniencies

p. 5–6Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Practical Summary - Reheating Liquids (Ashkenaz):

Hot soup / tea / coffee that is still hot (above eating temperature): PERMITTED to reheat.

Warm soup that is below eating temperature: FORBIDDEN (Shulchan Aruch HaRav / Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits).

Soup that has completely cooled to room temperature: FORBIDDEN - all agree (though Rav Berkovits: it is a chumra, not doraisa).

Sefardim: follow Mechaber who holds like Rashi - once below YSB it is assur.

Reheating Solids That Have Liquid / Gravy

ScenarioHalacha

Dry solid food with congealed gravy still clinging to it

Need not remove - moisture clinging to solid is not considered 'liquid.' May reheat.

Solid food sitting in a puddle of gravy - puddle visible

Must remove the gravy puddle first; then may reheat the solid (Ashkenaz). Rav Ovadia: lenient if solids are majority.

Congealed fat (solid at room temp, e.g. schmaltz) - reheating

PERMITTED - considered a dvar yavesh (Mechaber, most Acharonim). Melts onto a solid: mutar. Melts into empty plate: Molid problem.

Congealed gravy (liquid at room temp) - reheating

FORBIDDEN - it is essentially a dvar lach even while congealed

Butter on a hot potato or food

PERMITTED (Rav Moshe) - butter is solid at room temperature, and it melts into the food rather than forming a puddle

Ketchup placed on hot food

Rav Moshe: PERMITTED (two chumras need not both be applied). Rav Elyashiv: PERMITTED (ketchup is a dvar yavesh).

p. 7Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Molid - Changing the Form of a Solid

A separate issur derabanan: causing a solid to turn into a liquid form (e.g. melting ice into an empty cup, melting butter onto an empty plate). This is Molid - creating a 'new' form.

ScenarioHalacha

Melting ice or butter into an empty cup or plate

FORBIDDEN - Molid (issur derabanan)

Melting ice into a cup of water (melts into existing liquid)

PERMITTED - not considered Molid since it dissolves into the existing liquid

Melting butter onto a hot piece of food

PERMITTED - absorbed into the solid food, not forming a puddle (Rav Moshe)

p. 8Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

3. Bishul Achar Tsli / Tsli Achar Bishul

Background: Types of Cooking

Bishul = cooking in liquid. Tsli = roasting over open fire. Afiyah = baking in oven (treated like tsli). Deep-frying = bishul. Shallow-frying = tsli.

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Re'eim (Hagahos Maimones)

There IS bishul achar tsli - assur to cook something previously baked/roasted. Even in a Kli sheini (bread), since bread is kalei habishul.

Ashkenaz is strict for this

Ravya (Mordechai)

NO bishul achar tsli - may cook something previously baked.

Mechaber (318:5)

Brings Re'eim as 'yesh mi she'omer' and Ravya as 'yesh matirin' - ikar follows Ravya, but advisable to be strict

Sefardim: machlokes; Ben Ish Chai and Rav Abba Shaul strict; Rav Ovadia lenient

Rama

Strict for Re'eim - Ashkenazim do not cook previously baked food. Even Kli sheini forbidden for bread (kalei habishul).

Standard Ashkenaz practice

Chazon Ish

Re'eim only forbids when there is actual 'taam tsli' (flavor of roasting). Merely warming cooked food by fire does not create taam tsli.

Key leniency for hotplate/blech

p. 9Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Practical Applications - Bishul Achar Tsli

ScenarioHalacha

Putting bread into a hot Kli sheini (e.g. bowl of soup)

FORBIDDEN (Rama / Re'eim - bread is kalei habishul). Solution: make the bowl a Kli shlishi.

Soup nuts / croutons that were DEEP fried - into hot soup

PERMITTED - deep frying = bishul, so they are 'bishul.' No bishul achar bishul with dry food.

Soup nuts / croutons that were BAKED (not deep fried) - into hot soup (Kli sheini)

Potentially FORBIDDEN - bishul achar afiyah (same as tsli)

Reheating fully cooked food on hotplate/blech - food gets hot but does NOT get roasted

PERMITTED (Chazon Ish: no taam tsli = no issur)

Instant coffee into a Kli sheini

Generally PERMITTED - most hold the drying process after cooking is not tsli, and the original bishul remains in effect. Rav Moshe lenient to put in Kli sheini (personally strict for Kli shlishi only).

Instant coffee into a Kli rishon

Stricter - Mishnah Berurah holds the drying process may be tsli. Significant doubt. Avoid l'chatchila.

Previously salted or pickled food - then cooking it in liquid

FORBIDDEN even per Ravya - salting/pickling is not in the category of bishul doraisa, so bishul achar pickling does apply (Pri Megadim)

Food cooked, then baked, then you want to cook it again

Pri Megadim: permitted (original bishul never nullified). Biur Halacha: seems to disagree.

p. 10–11Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

4. Stirring (Meriha) and Removing Food with a Spoon (Hotsaah B'Kaf)

Stirring

ScenarioHalacha

Stirring food on the fire that is NOT fully cooked

FORBIDDEN midoraisa - stirring speeds up cooking (SA 318:18)

Stirring food that is NOT fully cooked and OFF the fire

At minimum assur miderabanan; possibly doraisa (Tiferes Shmuel). Be strict.

Stirring fully cooked food ON the fire

Kol Bo: assur midoraisa (small uncooked bits may still be present). Tiferes Shmuel: assur miderabanan. Lemaaseh: do not stir.

Stirring fully cooked food OFF the fire

Mutar m'ikar hadin (SA). Ideally be strict (Rama). Mishnah Berurah: mutar for Hotsaah b'kaf, may be strict for stirring.

p. 12Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Hotsaah B'Kaf (Removing Food with a Spoon)

ScenarioHalacha

Taking food with a spoon from a pot ON the fire - food NOT fully cooked

FORBIDDEN - possibly doraisa. Same as stirring.

Taking food with spoon from pot OFF the fire - food NOT fully cooked

Assur (Mechaber 318:18). Be strict.

Taking food with spoon from pot ON the fire - food fully cooked (e.g. cholent)

L'chatchila: do not do so (Rama). B'dieved or l'tsorech: Chazon Ish lenient. Rav Ovadia: lenient. Ben Ish Chai / Rav Abba Shaul: strict unless l'tsorech mitzva.

Taking food with spoon from pot OFF the fire - food fully cooked

PERMITTED (Mishnah Berurah)

Removing individual pieces of dry fully cooked chicken from a tray ON the fire

PERMITTED - not a tavshil; no concern of small uncooked bits being mixed in

Clear soup - removing from pot ON fire

PERMITTED - same as above; no mixed uncooked bits

Putting lid on a pot of FULLY COOKED food that is ON the fire

Rav Moshe: assur miderabanan (gezeira). Most Poskim: permitted. Do not do l'chatchila but lenient b'dieved.

p. 13Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

5. Kli Rishon, Kli Sheini, and Kli Shlishi

Definitions and Status

Kli Rishon (KR): The vessel in which food was cooked on the fire. Its walls retain heat and can continue to cook food even off the fire - its cooking status is DORAISA even off the fire.

Irui Kli Rishon: Pouring from a KR onto food. Cooks a klipa (outer layer) of dry food - treated as Kli sheini for most purposes. Into liquid: see below.

Kli Sheini (KS): A vessel into which hot food/liquid has been poured from a KR. Its walls have cooled the liquid - does not cook midoraisa (in most cases). Raw food may be placed in it (with exceptions - see below).

Kli Shlishi (KSH): A vessel into which food has been poured from a KS. Generally no concern at all. Rav Auerbach: kalei habishul forbidden even in a KSH (midoraisa). Rav Moshe / Chazon Ish / Rav Berkovits: permitted.

Kli Rishon - Off the Fire: Does It Still Cook?

Halacha:

A Kli Rishon that is off the fire can still cook midoraisa as long as it is above YSB.

Therefore: do not add raw uncooked ingredients to a Kli Rishon even off the fire if it is YSB.

Irui Kli Rishon Into Liquids

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Tosefos

Irui kli rishon onto cold liquid is assur if the resulting combination is above YSB. Permitted only if end result is below YSB.

This is the accepted halacha (Biur Halacha)

Ran (+ Rashba, Rambam, Tur)

Irui kli rishon onto cold liquid is always mutar - the hot liquid loses cooking power once it enters the new vessel (becomes KS)

Many Rishonim hold this; Biur Halacha: be strict l'chatchila for Tosefos

Mechaber (318:12)

Rules leniently like the Ran - mutar to pour from KR onto cold water with no distinction

Halacha

L'chatchila be strict for Tosefos - assur to pour from KR onto cold liquid if end result is YSB. Bdi'eved: mutar (rely on Rishonim who are lenient).

p. 14Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
ScenarioHalacha

Pouring hot soup from pot (KR) into a cold bowl of soup - end result above YSB

FORBIDDEN l'chatchila (Tosefos / Biur Halacha). Bdi'eved: permitted.

Pouring hot water from a KR into a cold cup - end result below YSB

PERMITTED - all agree

Adding large amount of cold water into a boiling KR - end result below YSB

PERMITTED - do in one pour (Chayei Adam)

Hot water from urn tube entering the urn when water level drops

Permitted b'dieved - psik reisha de'lo nicha leih, at worst miderabanan (Rav Moshe)

p. 15Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

What May and May Not Be Put in a Kli Sheini

Basic rule (Mishnah Shabbos): Mutar to put raw food in a Kli Sheini. Numerous exceptions apply:

Food / ItemStatus in Kli Sheini

Raw meat / vegetables (general, not kalei habishul)

Magen Avraham / Mishnah Berurah: FORBIDDEN (safek kalei habishul - we don't know which foods cook easily). Chazon Ish / Rav Abba Shaul: PERMITTED. Rav Berkovits: follows Mishnah Berurah.

Water (uncooked)

PERMITTED - Gemara explicitly permits

Oil (uncooked)

PERMITTED - explicitly permitted by Gemara

Spices - whole spices

PERMITTED - explicitly permitted. Rav Auerbach: FORBIDDEN for GROUND spices. Rav Moshe: permitted even ground. Rav Berkovits: follows Rav Auerbach (ground spices forbidden).

Salt (uncooked) - Kli Sheini

PERMITTED. One who refrains is 'worthy of blessing' (Tosefos, Rama). Mutar even in KR off the fire.

Salt - into Kli Rishon (off fire)

PERMITTED m'ikar hadin (Mechaber). Ideally be strict (Rama). If salt was previously cooked: mutar, but Mishnah Berurah: l'chatchila avoid KR off fire.

Sugar

Same as salt - but sugar has been cooked (processed), so totally mutar in KS and no chumra for KR off fire.

Bread / soft baked foods - into Kli Sheini

FORBIDDEN (Re'eim: kalei habishul + bishul achar afiyah). Rama follows this. Solution: use a Kli Shlishi.

Bread - into Kli Shlishi

PERMITTED (Rav Moshe, Chazon Ish, Rav Berkovits). Even Rav Auerbach's concern re: kalei habishul in KSH does not apply to bread - combination with lenient opinions on bishul achar afiyah.

Eggs (raw or undercooked)

FORBIDDEN in KS - considered kalei habishul

Teabag or tea leaves

FORBIDDEN in KS (kalei habishul). Status in KSH: Rav Moshe and Chazon Ish: PERMITTED. Rav Auerbach: FORBIDDEN midoraisa. Rav Berkovits: follows Rav Moshe - permitted in KSH. Rav Kanievsky: permitted.

Ground coffee (Turkish) - uncooked

FORBIDDEN in KS (kalei habishul)

Instant coffee - previously cooked

PERMITTED in KS (Rav Moshe) - previously cooked. Rav Moshe personally: only in KSH.

Cocoa / ground powdered food

Rav Moshe: PERMITTED in KS (category of spices). Rav Auerbach: FORBIDDEN (ground).

Lemon slice - into hot liquid in KS

Mishnah Berurah: FORBIDDEN (safek kalei habishul). Chazon Ish: PERMITTED. Rav Berkovits: follows Mishnah Berurah. Note: most Poskim forbid squeezing lemon into tea but permit placing a slice.

Onion - into KS

Rav Moshe: doubtful - should not put into KS (may be kalei habishul). Forbidden per Mishnah Berurah.

Cold previously cooked liquid (e.g. cold soup into hot bowl)

PERMITTED - EBA'B applies; bishul achar bishul of cooled liquid is only a chumra, not doraisa (Mishnah Berurah 318:23)

p. 16–18Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Yad Nichveis Bo - Boiling Hot Kli Sheini

If a Kli Sheini is so hot that one's hand would get burnt (yad nichveis bo), there is a machlokes whether it can cook raw food midoraisa.

ScenarioHalacha

Adding cold uncooked water into a boiling Kli Sheini (yad nichveis bo)

Chayei Adam (cited in Mishnah Berurah): FORBIDDEN - treated as a stringency. Radbaz: permitted. Rav Berkovits: do not combine with other leniencies.

Cold previously cooked liquid into boiling hot Kli Sheini

Two chumras combined - Rav Berkovits: not lenient even so.

How long until Kli Sheini is no longer 'yad nichveis bo'?

Rav Wosner: a few seconds is sufficient

p. 19Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

6. Dvar Gush and the Ladle

Dvar Gush - Status of a Hot Piece of Solid Food

When a hot solid piece of food (dvar gush) is removed from a Kli Rishon and placed in a Kli Sheini - does it remain a Kli Rishon (and can it cook other food) or does it become a Kli Sheini?

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Mechaber and Rama (YD 105:3)

Dvar gush becomes a Kli Sheini once placed in a Kli Sheini - just like liquid

Sefardim follow this - a piece transferred to two vessels is a Kli Shlishi

Maharshal / Shach

Dvar gush retains Kli Rishon status as long as it is YSB, regardless of how many vessels it passes through. Exception: if surrounded by gravy, becomes a Kli Sheini.

Magen Avraham / Mishnah Berurah (Hilchos Shabbos)

In Hilchos Shabbos: treat hot dvar gush as Kli Rishon as long as it is YSB - a stringency.

Ashkenaz practice in Hilchos Shabbos

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Dvar gush being Kli Rishon is a chumra; may combine with other leniencies to be lenient

Key for complex cases

Shach - gravy exception

If food is surrounded by at least half its height in gravy, it becomes a Kli Sheini. Rav Elyashiv: must be fully covered. Rav Berkovits: half is sufficient.

p. 20Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

The Ladle

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Maharil

A ladle placed briefly in a Kli Rishon becomes a Kli Sheini (its walls cool the liquid)

Taz

A ladle placed briefly in a Kli Rishon remains a Kli Rishon

All agree

If the ladle was left in the Kli Rishon for a long time, it becomes a Kli Rishon

Chazon Ish / Rav Berkovits

Machlokes Maharil/Taz only applies when Kli Rishon is on the fire. If off the fire, all agree ladle is a Kli Sheini.

Important practical leniency

Mishnah Berurah (simple reading)

Machlokes applies even when Kli Rishon is off the fire

p. 21Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Practical Cases - Dvar Gush and Ladle

ScenarioHalacha

Hot piece of meat placed next to a salad

Mishnah Berurah: meat is KR - assur midoraisa. Mechaber/Rama: at worst KS. Rav Auerbach / Rav Berkovits: lenient (psik reisha de'lo nicha leih + mekalkel). Rav Elyashiv / Rav Wosner: strict.

Putting salt on a hot piece of meat on your plate (plate = KS or KSH)

If meat was transferred via ladle (making plate a KSH) and there is no gravy: may be lenient - two chumras (dvar gush + salt) need not both apply. If meat is in gravy (half covered): Kli Sheini - room for leniency. Rav Berkovits: be strict but can be lenient with two chumras.

Putting bread in a bowl of soup - pot was on fire, soup poured directly

Bowl is KS - FORBIDDEN to put bread (Rama). Pour soup from KR into a second bowl to make it KSH.

Putting bread in a bowl of soup - soup was ladled with ladle NOT left in pot long

If pot was off fire: ladle is KS (Chazon Ish / Rav Berkovits) - bowl is KSH - PERMITTED. If pot was on fire: machlokes Maharil/Taz; Maharil + machlokes on bishul achar afiyah = combined leniency sufficient.

Putting bread in a bowl of soup - ladle was left in pot a long time

Ladle is KR (all agree). Bowl is KS. FORBIDDEN (Rama) - bread is kalei habishul.

Cholent with significant gravy transferred to a plate via ladle

Pieces surrounded by gravy = KS (Shach). Plate is KSH. PERMITTED for most additions.

Picking up a piece of food with a FORK

Fork has no walls - does NOT make food into a KS. Food remains KR if it was KR.

Picking up a piece of food with a SPOON/LADLE (briefly in pot off fire)

Ladle = KS (Chazon Ish). Food placed in plate = KSH. More room for leniency.

p. 22–23Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

7. Cooking in the Sun (Toldos Chama) and Other Heat Sources

Heat Source / ScenarioHalacha

Cooking directly in the sun (e.g. egg in direct sunlight)

PERMITTED - the sun itself is not a form of fire (SA 318:3)

Cooking using an object heated by the sun (Toldos Chama - e.g. kerchief heated in sun)

FORBIDDEN miderabanan - gezeira to protect from Toldos Ohr (objects heated by fire)

Cooking using Toldos Ohr - objects heated by fire (e.g. a hot pot next to the fire)

FORBIDDEN - same as cooking on fire itself

Placing food on a hotplate/blech already on from before Shabbos (no issur chazara)

PERMITTED - the blech itself was heated before Shabbos. Issue of bishul depends on food state.

Placing a new metal blech on a fire on Shabbos

PERMITTED - halacha does not follow Chazon Ish that heating metal to YSB is issur. Mishnah Berurah: only issur if metal actually softens.

p. 24Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

8. Special Practical Cases - Rav Moshe's Teshuvos

Practical CaseRuling

Ketchup on hot meat (ketchup is cold, previously cooked)

PERMITTED (Rav Moshe): ketchup is a dvar lach (doesn't hold shape) but reheating a cold dvar lach is only a chumra, and hot dvar gush cooking = another chumra; two chumras need not both apply. Rav Elyashiv: ketchup is a solid - permitted anyway.

Butter on hot food in a Kli Sheini (butter previously pasteurized to YSB = 'cooked')

PERMITTED (Rav Moshe) - butter is dvar yavesh; pasteurization = bishul; EBA'B applies.

Dry food with small amount of liquid - reheating

Cannot be lenient unless solid is majority and liquid is minority. Rav Ovadia: lenient if solids are majority. Most Ashkenazi Poskim: remove visible gravy. Rav Moshe: lenient only in great need.

Teabag in Kli Shlishi

PERMITTED (Rav Moshe, Chazon Ish, Rav Kanievsky). Rav Auerbach: FORBIDDEN midoraisa. The color/taste change occurs even in cold water - it is not being 'cooked.'

Instant coffee in Kli Sheini

PERMITTED (Rav Moshe) - considered previously cooked. Rav Moshe personally uses Kli Shlishi only.

Uncooked salt in Kli Shlishi

PERMITTED - nothing cooks in KSH; salt is also lenient m'ikar hadin (Rav Moshe)

Onion or lemon in Kli Sheini

Rav Moshe: IN DOUBT - do not add (may be safek kalei habishul). Chazon Ish: lenient. Note: placing a lemon slice in tea is different from squeezing - slicing is generally mutar per most Poskim.

Cocoa / powdered food in Kli Sheini

Rav Moshe: PERMITTED (treated as spices). Rav Auerbach: FORBIDDEN (ground = different status).

Pouring from KR into cup with cold previously cooked droplets

Rav Moshe: PERMITTED (psik reisha de'lo nicha leih + reheating cold dvar lach is only a chumra)

Pouring from KR into cup with UNCOOKED cold droplets

Rav Moshe: FORBIDDEN l'chatchila. Bdi'eved: permitted (rely on lenient Rishonim). Rav Ovadia: lenient l'chatchila.

p. 25–26Hilchos Bishul — Cooking

Quick Summary: Core Principles

The 10 Most Important Rules of Hilchos Bishul:

  1. BISHUL APPLIES TO ALL FOOD: Assur midoraisa to cook any food - even if edible raw - if cooking improves it.
  2. YSB THRESHOLD: Treat anything above 40°C as potentially YSB. Cannot test with your hand.
  3. EIN BISHUL ACHAR BISHUL - DRY FOOD: Once dry food is fully cooked, may reheat freely (no EBA'B).
  4. EIN BISHUL ACHAR BISHUL - LIQUID: Once liquid cools to below eating temperature, forbidden to reheat (Ashkenaz: Shulchan Aruch HaRav / Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits). Remove from heat if it dropped below this point.
  5. BISHUL ACHAR TSLI: Ashkenazim: do not cook previously baked/roasted food. Kli Sheini or Kli Rishon - forbidden for bread. Solution: use Kli Shlishi.
  6. KLI RISHON OFF FIRE: Still cooks midoraisa if YSB. Do not add raw food.
  7. KLI SHEINI: Mutar to put water, oil, salt, whole spices. Forbidden: bread, eggs, tea (kalei habishul), ground spices (Rav Auerbach / Rav Berkovits), most other raw foods (Magen Avraham / Mishnah Berurah).
  8. KLI SHLISHI: Generally permitted for everything. Exceptions: teabag (Rav Auerbach), but Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits lenient.
  9. DVAR GUSH: Treat hot pieces of food as Kli Rishon (Mishnah Berurah / Ashkenaz stringency). Exception: surrounded by gravy (half covered) = Kli Sheini. Combine with ladle = Kli Shlishi in plate.
  10. LADLE: If pot was off fire - ladle is always Kli Sheini; plate = Kli Shlishi (Chazon Ish / Rav Berkovits). This makes most Shabbos table scenarios more manageable.
p. 27Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Hilchos Shabbos

Hatmana, Shehiya, and Chazara

1. Hatmana - Insulating a Pot

Hatmana is the Rabbinic prohibition of surrounding a pot to retain or add heat. There are two categories: (a) Dvar hamosif hevel - a covering that actively adds its own heat; (b) Dvar she'eino mosif hevel - a covering that merely retains heat.

Basic Rules - When Is Hatmana Permitted?

ScenarioHalacha

Dvar hamosif hevel (adds heat) - Erev Shabbos

FORBIDDEN - even on Erev Shabbos. Gezeira lest one insulate with live embers (remetz) and come to stoke on Shabbos.

Dvar hamosif hevel - during Bein Hashmashos

FORBIDDEN (per Mechaber / Rashi's girsa). Permitted only per Rif/Rambam's girsa - rejected by most Rishonim.

Dvar hamosif hevel - on Shabbos itself

FORBIDDEN

Dvar she'eino mosif hevel - Erev Shabbos

PERMITTED

Dvar she'eino mosif hevel - during Bein Hashmashos

PERMITTED - food is still hot so no concern of stoking

Dvar she'eino mosif hevel - on Shabbos

FORBIDDEN - gezeira lest one see food cooled and come to reheat it (Rashi)

p. 28Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

What Is a Dvar Hamosif Hevel?

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Rashi

Remetz (ash with live embers) = mosif hevel - it is currently generating heat

Standard girsa accepted by Mechaber / most Rishonim

Rambam / Rif

Remetz = eino mosif hevel - though hot now, it is dying down and cannot sustain heat

Different girsa; creates different practical conclusions. Rejected by Maggid Mishneh and most Rishonim.

Eino Mosif Hevel on Top of Mosif Hevel (e.g. towels on a pot sitting on a platta)

When a dvar she'eino mosif hevel (towel/blanket) covers a pot that sits on a dvar hamosif hevel (platta/fire), is the covering treated as mosif hevel?

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Ri (first approach)

Only a problem if it is possible to surround the pot with the heat source below (e.g. refuse). A platta cannot wrap around the pot - permitted.

Key leniency: covering pot with towels on a platta is permitted

Ri (second approach)

Permitted as long as the covering material does not physically touch the pot

Requires gap between towel and pot

Rabbeinu Baruch

If the heat source below is 'dying out' (not sustaining heat), it is eino mosif hevel - an oven without coals, or a cooling element, is not mosif hevel

Platta: since it sustains heat, it IS mosif hevel per this view

Rosh

Permitted only if the material does not touch the pot - even in an oven without coals

Stricter than Ri's first approach

Mishnah Berurah

L'chatchila be strict for the Rosh - covering must not touch the pot. No need to rebuke one who follows Ri (lenient).

Standard Ashkenazi practice

Mechaber / Chazon Ish

Even touching coals on one side = hatmana (strict on definition of hatmana)

But Rav Abba Shaul: platta/blech is different since you cannot surround pot with it

p. 29Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

How Much of the Pot Must Be Covered? (Definition of Hatmana)

ScenarioHalacha

Dvar hamosif hevel - touching one side of pot

Mechaber / Chazon Ish: FORBIDDEN (even one side). Rama: PERMITTED - hatmana requires all four sides.

Dvar hamosif hevel - three sides of pot

Rav Auerbach: FORBIDDEN even per Rama. Rav Moshe Feinstein: only four sides = hatmana (lenient). Rav Berkovits: follows Rav Feinstein.

Dvar she'eino mosif hevel - partial coverage

All agree: only forbidden if all sides covered.

p. 30Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Crockpot and Practical Applications

ScenarioHalacha

Crockpot (covers 3 sides of inner pot)

Rav Feinstein / Rav Berkovits: PERMITTED - hatmana only applies to all four sides. Rav Auerbach: FORBIDDEN (3 sides = hatmana per Rama). Solution: place foil under inner pot so sides of foil extend up over outer pot (creating hefsek/gap), or raise pot above inner surface.

Covering food with aluminum foil on a blech/platta

Most Poskim (Rav Auerbach, Rav Elyashiv): PERMITTED if intent is not to keep hot (e.g., prevent burning). Rav Feinstein: FORBIDDEN if intent is to heat. Intent matters. Double-layer foil: at least one layer should not fully cover.

Baby bottle fully submerged in hot water (Kli of hot water)

FORBIDDEN - hot water is a dvar mosif hevel; surrounding something cold in it = hatmana. Must ensure part of bottle is above water level.

Putting food inside other food (e.g. kishke in cholent)

Rav Auerbach: lenient (intent = prevent falling apart). Rav Elyashiv / Rav Wosner: make holes in foil so it becomes 'one tavshil.' Rav Berkovits: minhag is lenient.

Thermos (pouring hot water in)

PERMITTED (Rav Feinstein) - Kli sheini; covering lid is not hatmana since intent is not for heat. Chazon Ish: insulated Kli itself is not hatmana.

p. 31Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Leniencies - When Is Hatmana Permitted Even on Shabbos?

ScenarioHalacha

Pot was covered before Shabbos and cover fell off on Shabbos

PERMITTED to replace cover (even deliberately remove and replace). Chazal only forbade initiating hatmana on Shabbos.

Adding additional cover on Shabbos (even hotter than original)

PERMITTED - as long as food is fully cooked

Switching to a different cover on Shabbos

PERMITTED - even if new cover is better at retaining heat

Food not fully cooked - replacing cover

FORBIDDEN - Mechaber. The added insulation contributes to cooking. (Magen Avraham: only if pot is on fire. Beis Meir: always forbidden. Rav Berkovits: follows Beis Meir.)

Covering something cold with dvar she'eino mosif hevel

PERMITTED (Rambam / Mechaber) - even if intent is to keep warm or remove chill. Rashi: only permitted if intent is to prevent heating.

Covering a Kli sheini with dvar she'eino mosif hevel

PERMITTED (Rambam / Mechaber). Rashi: only if intent is to cool down.

p. 32Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Hatmana and Shehiya - Do the Leniencies of Shehiya Apply to Hatmana?

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Rabbeinu Tam

NO - stoking is more effective when pot is fully covered; Chazal were stricter about hatmana. Forbidden even if food is raw or fully cooked.

Accepted halacha (Mechaber)

Rabbeinu Shmuel

YES - hatmana follows shehiya: permitted if food is raw (kidra chaysa) or Mb'd (Chanania)

Rama: lenient opinion; no need to rebuke where this is the minhag; forbidden elsewhere

Lenient opinion in Rama (257:1)

Hatmana permitted if intent is to eat the food the next day

Only b'dieved; do not become accustomed to relying on this

2. Shehiya - Leaving Food on the Fire

Shehiya is the Rabbinic prohibition of leaving food on an open fire as Shabbos begins, lest one come to stoke the fire on Shabbos (shema yechateh). Two ways around it exist: grufa (removing coals) and ketuma (covering coals with ash).

The Core Machlokes: Chachamim vs. Chanania

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Chanania

Permitted to leave food on open fire if it has reached Maachal Ben Drussai (Mb'd) by the time Shabbos enters. No concern of stoking once the food is at Mb'd.

Mb'd = 1/3 cooked (Rashi); 1/2 cooked (Rambam). Minhag follows Chanania.

Chachamim

Forbidden to leave food on open fire even if Mb'd. Only permitted if food is fully cooked AND mistamek v'rah lo (getting worse). [Per Rav and Shmuel's reading.]

Rif / Rambam follow this. Mechaber brings as primary opinion.

Rosh

Agrees with Chachamim in principle but concludes minhag was like Chanania. 'Yisrael should be left to keep their minhagim.'

Machlokes between MB and Chazon Ish on what the Rosh meant.

Mishnah Berurah

The minhag of leniency (Chanania) is not ideal; one should l'chatchila be strict like Chachamim.

In a makom tsorech, rely on Chanania.

Chazon Ish

The Rosh's leniency is fully lechatchila - the minhag is legitimate and connected to oneg Shabbos.

Rav Berkovits: rules like Mishnah Berurah.

p. 33Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

HALACHA L'MAASEH - Shehiya: Ashkenazim: Minhag is like Chanania (lenient). Ideally reach Mb'd by shkia. In makom tsorech, rely on Chanania even without grufa/ketuma. Rav Berkovits: l'chatchila do grufa/ketuma. | Sefardim: Also have minhag to follow Chanania.

p. 34Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Status of Modern Cooking Utensils

ScenarioHalacha

Platta (hot plate, no knobs)

Most Poskim: considered garuf v'katum - may leave any food on it as Shabbos enters. Rav Elyashiv: NOT garuf v'katum; must cover with thick layer of foil (or two thin layers). Rav Berkovits: follows majority - platta is garuf v'katum.

Gas stovetop (with knobs)

NOT garuf v'katum - raising gas is like adding wood. To make katum: cover the flame AND the knobs (Rav Feinstein). Rav Aaron Kotler: cover knobs only. Standard practice: use a blech.

Blech covering stovetop

Blech = garuf v'katum - may leave food on stovetop. Ensure blech covers the knobs too. If knobs not covered, cover them separately.

Electric oven

To make katum: place metal box inside covering elements, OR cover elements with foil. Also cover the buttons/knobs. Rav Berkovits rules this way.

Crockpot / slow cooker

Treated like open fire for shehiya. To use: food must be Mb'd by Shabbos (Chanania), OR perform equivalent of ketuma on the dial.

Urn / hot water urn

Treated like open fire for shehiya. Most urns have no way to raise the heat - status may be like garuf v'katum. Ask a posek for your specific model.

p. 35Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Grufa and Ketuma - Definitions

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Ran

Grufa = moving coals to one side (serves as heker - reminder not to stoke). Purpose of grufa/ketuma is as a psychological reminder.

Halacha follows Rambam.

Rambam

Grufa = removing ALL coals entirely. This shows complete diversion of attention from cooking.

Therefore: tanur remains forbidden after grufa - sparks still remain.

Rashba

Grufa requires removing all coals; tanur is forbidden as a lo plug (blanket decree regardless of sparks).

Different reasoning from Rambam for same practical outcome.

Kutma v'Huvara - If the Covered Coals Reignite

ScenarioHalacha

Coals covered with ash (ketuma) but fire rose up and burned off the ash on its own

PERMITTED - original act of ketuma/gilui daas still stands. Rav Auerbach: this only works if fire returned by itself. If the person raised the flame after covering, the ketuma is nullified.

Person covered the knobs but then turned them before Shabbos

FORBIDDEN - the ketuma is nullified by using the knobs. Must re-cover.

Lowering flame while blech/foil is on (vs. raising)

Seems permitted to lower. Raising = problem. Rav Berkovits: be strict l'chatchila but b'dieved lenient if raised.

p. 36Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Kidra Chaysa - Leaving Raw Food on the Fire

When the entire pot is raw as Shabbos enters and one intends to eat it the next day - all opinions agree shehiya is permitted.

ScenarioHalacha

When must food still be raw?

Mishnah Berurah / Rav Auerbach: by shekia. Rav Nissim Karelitz: by the time the person brings in Shabbos. In communities that accept Shabbos early, Rav Auerbach is unsure.

Definition of 'raw' - has food reached YSB?

Chazon Ish: raw = not yet YSB. Rav Abba Shaul: can still be considered raw even after YSB until food begins to soften. Rav Berkovits: follows Rav Abba Shaul.

When must the food be ready to use the heter?

Mishnah Berurah: only if food will not be ready until after the normal time people finish their night meal. Rav Elyashiv: must be several hours after shkia. Chazon Ish: permitted even if ready while people are still eating.

Pot on a high flame - could be ready before morning if raised higher

Rav Auerbach / Rav Elyashiv: heter only applies if the pot cannot be cooked early even on highest flame. Rav Wosner: permitted regardless. Rav Nissim Karelitz: if raw meat in pot, always permitted.

Chaticha chaya - adding a raw piece to a partially cooked pot

Raw piece must take a long time to cook (e.g. meat, not vegetables). Serves as a heker that one won't think about food until next day. Adding a raw vegetable: insufficient unless pot is very large (Rav Nissim Karelitz).

p. 37Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Leaving Fruit, Water, and Other Items on the Fire

ScenarioHalacha

Apples or fruit edible when raw - on open fire

PERMITTED (Tosefos / Mechaber). Edible raw = already 'better than Mb'd.' Note: Chazon Ish explains this only works when fruit is directly on coals (stoking would burn them).

Cold water on open fire

FORBIDDEN even though water is drinkable cold (Gemara). Similar to onions - not edible enough raw to override the gezeira.

Large pot of cold water - will only be ready next day

Chazon Ish: permitted via kidra chaysa. There is no concern of stoking since it will take so long to heat.

Tach b'tit - sealing oven with cement (or equivalent)

If oven is sealed so opening would damage food - shehiya permitted regardless of state of food. Chazon Ish: locking oven door = tach b'tit. Orchos Shabbos: strong tape on buttons = tach b'tit. Rav Berkovits rules both these ways.

p. 38Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Roasting (Tsli) and Shehiya - Differences from Bishul

ScenarioHalacha

Meat of a kid or chicken in oven (sealed or not)

PERMITTED - stoking would burn the tender meat, removing the concern. (Rambam / Mechaber: even on open fire. Other Rishonim / Rama: only in oven, not open fire.)

Meat of a ram / ox - oven NOT sealed

FORBIDDEN (all opinions)

Meat of a ram / ox - oven sealed with cement

PERMITTED - sealed oven prevents stoking

Meat / food directly on coals (not in oven)

Must reach Mb'd before Shabbos - all agree. Stoking would burn the food, but food must already be significantly started.

Whole goat/chicken vs. cut up

Whole bird: treated like ram/ox (wind won't damage as much). Cut up: treated like kid/chicken (more susceptible to burning from stoking).

3. Chazara - Returning a Pot to the Fire

Chazara is the prohibition of returning a pot to a fire on Shabbos. It is stricter than shehiya - it requires grufa u'ketuma even according to Chanania. Beis Hillel permits chazara with conditions; Beis Shammai forbids it entirely. Halacha follows Beis Hillel.

Conditions Required for Chazara (Tanai Chazara)

Three possible conditions are discussed in the Gemara: (1) Odan beyado - pot remained in his hand; (2) Daato lehachzir - intended to return it when he took it off; (3) Lo hiniach al gabei karka - did not put the pot on the ground.

p. 39Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara
AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Rach (Rabbeinu Chananel)

BOTH odan beyado AND daato lehachzir required. Putting pot on the ground = forbidden even with daato lehachzir.

Strictest opinion. Strict on all unanswered Gemara questions.

Rambam

Only condition: pot was NOT put on the ground. No requirement of odan beyado or daato lehachzir.

Most lenient of the major opinions.

Sefer HaTerumah

Permitted as long as not on ground. Even if on ground: permitted if had daato lehachzir.

More lenient than Rambam on ground case

Mechaber

Rules like Rambam - only condition is not putting on ground

Sefardic standard

Rama

Rules like Rach - requires both odan beyado AND daato lehachzir

Ashkenazic standard. Does not explicitly address hanging/bed cases - may be lenient.

Biur Halacha

L'chatchila: be strict for Rach. In makom tsorech: lenient if one condition fulfilled. If one had daato lehachzir but put on ground: ask a rav.

Standard Ashkenazi ruling

Yerushalmi (brought by Ran)

If pot was on fire when Shabbos began, no conditions required to return it on Shabbos (even after being removed on Shabbos)

Rama: minhag to rely on this but good to be strict. Used in combination with other leniencies.

p. 40Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Practical Applications of Tanai Chazara

ScenarioHalacha

Pot placed on counter (not ground) - held onto it (odan beyado)

PERMITTED. Counter is not karka. Note: tilt pot or keep hand on it to maintain odan beyado status.

Pot placed on counter without holding - had daato lehachzir

Makom tsorech: PERMITTED (one condition fulfilled = sufficient b'makom tsorech). Rav Berkovits: lenient.

Pot placed on ground with daato lehachzir

Orchos Shabbos: strict, consult a rav. Rav Berkovits: lenient b'shaas hadchak (combine with Yerushalmi). Note: fridge = karka; counter = not karka (majority of Poskim).

Pot placed on ground with no conditions

Orchos Shabbos: strict. Rav Berkovits: lenient only b'shaas hadchak with combination of Yerushalmi (if pot was on fire when Shabbos began).

Wrong pot removed by mistake / someone else removed it

Rav Auerbach: lenient (treated as daato lehachzir - owner never intended removal). Rav Shach / Rav Elyashiv: strict. Rav Berkovits: follows Rav Auerbach.

Power cut on Shabbos - moving pot to another fire/platta

Rav Auerbach: permitted - considered daato lehachzir (never intended removal). Rav Elyashiv: strict (no explicit intent). Rav Berkovits: lenient.

Pot placed on unplugged platta before Shabbos (thought it was on)

If pot was on fire first and transferred: Rav Auerbach lenient (view as returning from original fire). If pot was cold when placed on unplugged platta: FORBIDDEN even if food was originally cooked.

p. 41Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Additional Conditions for Chazara

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Mechaber (basic rule)

Food must be hot (above YSB for liquids) when returned. Not about chazara - about bishul achar bishul.

Dry food: may be permitted even below YSB (Magen Avraham)

Bach

If food went below YSB - forbidden to return, even dry food. Original cooking process nullified.

Stricter position

Magen Avraham

If food cooled completely (nistanen legamrei), forbidden miderabanan to return even dry food.

Does not require YSB - just 'some warmth'

Gra

No temperature condition for chazara - if other tanai chazara fulfilled, may return even if fully cold.

Biur Halacha: seems to favor Gra

Rav Feinstein / Rav Berkovits

Be strict for Magen Avraham: only return if food has some warmth. In makom tsorech: lenient (follow Gra).

Rama (253:5)

Cannot return food that is nistanen legamrei (fully cooled)

p. 42Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Liquid food (with gravy etc.): must be above YSB to return (Mechaber) or have some warmth (Rama). Dry food: must have some warmth (Magen Avraham / Rav Feinstein). In makom tsorech for dry food: Gra

is lenient even if fully cooled.

Chazara on Erev Shabbos (Close to Shabbos)

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Rashi / Ran / Rambam

No issur chazara on Erev Shabbos - prohibition only applies on Shabbos itself

Mechaber follows this

Tosefos / Rosh / Smag

Forbidden to place pot on fire so close to Shabbos that, if the food were cold, it could not heat up before Shabbos. Applies even to currently hot food.

They disagree on how cooked food must be: see below

Rosh

Issur chazara on Erev Shabbos only if food is FULLY COOKED (since then there's no bishul concern to override the chazara concern)

Tosefos

Issur applies once food has reached Mb'd

Smag

Issur always applies unless food is totally raw (lo plug)

Rama

Minhag is lenient, but good to be strict when there is no great need

Mishnah Berurah: like Rosh - only fully cooked triggers the issur. Adds chumra of Smag.

p. 43Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Workaround (Rav Auerbach): First put pot on high flame (where food will be ready by Shabbos), then lower the flame. Chazon Ish / Rav Kanievsky: not needed - since one could raise the flame, the issur doesn't apply even on a low flame.

Pina Meicham L'Meicham - Transferring Food to Another Pot

ScenarioHalacha

Transferring food to a cold pot and placing that new pot on the fire

Rach: FORBIDDEN (signals end of cooking process). Rambam / Sefer HaTerumah: PERMITTED. Magen Avraham: strict. Mishnah Berurah: LENIENT.

Hot water from urn poured into a cup then into pot on platta/blech

Rav Auerbach: PERMITTED. (Different case - returning to a different utensil than the one it came from.)

p. 44Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Hefsek Kedeira - Pot on Pot Arrangements

ScenarioHalacha

Placing cooked pot directly on top of another pot full of food (on the fire)

PERMITTED without any tanai chazara (Ran / Mechaber) - not the normal manner of cooking (ein derech bishul)

Placing food pot on top of an EMPTY pot on the fire

Permitted with tanai chazara - empty pot = garuf v'katum but still looks like it's on a fire

Upside-down pot on top of a blech/platta

Rav Elyashiv: strict (garuf v'katum only, tanai chazara required). Rav Auerbach: lenient (treat as full pot). Rav Berkovits: minhag is lenient; praiseworthy to be strict.

p. 45Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Status of Platta and Blech for Chazara

AuthorityPositionNotes / Key Point

Rav Elyashiv

Platta = like open fire; must cover with thick/double foil to make garuf v'katum; then may return with tanai chazara

Most strict

Shemiras Shabbos K'hilchasa

Platta = garuf v'katum even without foil (not normal to cook on platta = like a reminder)

Rav Ovadia Yosef

Platta = like radiator; may put food on without any tanai chazara

Most lenient

Rav Berkovits

L'chatchila: cover platta with foil to make garuf v'katum. B'dieved: can rely on Rav Ovadia. Blech = garuf v'katum (most Poskim). Chazon Ish: blech = open fire, forbidden to return without upside-down pot.

Standard Ashkenazi practical ruling

p. 46Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara

Quick Summary: Core Rules at a Glance

#RuleKey Point

1

Dvar hamosif hevel

FORBIDDEN Erev Shabbos, Bein Hashmashos, and Shabbos. No exceptions.

2

Dvar she'eino mosif hevel

Permitted Erev Shabbos and Bein Hashmashos. Forbidden on Shabbos itself (unless already covered before Shabbos).

3

Covering/insulating pot already covered before Shabbos

Permitted to replace, switch, or add a cover even on Shabbos - as long as food is fully cooked.

4

Shehiya - minhag

Both Ashkenazim and Sefardim follow Chanania: leave food on fire if it reached Mb'd (1/3–1/2 cooked) by shekia. L'chatchila: perform grufa/ketuma.

5

Platta = garuf v'katum

Most Poskim: platta is garuf v'katum; may leave any food. Rav Berkovits: l'chatchila cover with foil. Rav Elyashiv: must cover.

6

Blech on stovetop

Blech = garuf v'katum. Must also cover knobs.

7

Chazara requires grufa/ketuma

Cannot return a pot to an open fire without grufa/ketuma - even with all other conditions met.

8

Tanai chazara (Ashkenaz)

Requires: (a) not put on ground, (b) odan beyado, (c) daato lehachzir. In makom tsorech: one condition is sufficient. Rav Berkovits: lenient with combinations.

9

Pot put on ground with daato lehachzir

Shaas hadchak: consult a rav (Orchos Shabbos) or be lenient combining Yerushalmi (Rav Berkovits).

10

Food must have some warmth for chazara

Fully cold dry food: b'makom tsorech permitted (Gra). Liquid: must be YSB (Mechaber). Ashkenaz: any warmth is sufficient.

p. 47–48Maaseh Shabbos

Hilchos Maaseh Shabbos

The penalty applied to food/objects that result from a forbidden Melacha on Shabbos

1. The Three-Way Machlokes HaTanaim

Core Dispute (Bava Kamma 71a)

TannaB'ShogegB'MeizidLevel of Issur

Rebbe Meir (most lenient)

Permitted immediately (even for the sinner)

Forbidden for sinner and all others until after Shabbos

Always only Miderabanan

Rebbe Yehuda (middle)

Forbidden for everyone until after Shabbos

Forbidden to the sinner forever; permitted to others after Shabbos

Always only Miderabanan

Rebbe Yochanan HaSandlar (strictest)

Forbidden to sinner forever; forbidden to others until after Shabbos

Forbidden to everyone forever

B'Meizid = Midoraisa B'Shogeg = Miderabanan

2. The Reason for Maaseh Shabbos - Machlokes Rashi / Tosefos

AuthorityReasonPractical Consequence

Rashi (Chullin 15a)

Person must not benefit from the fruits of his sin

Must wait Kedai Sheyaasu after Shabbos (the time it took to cook on Shabbos)

Rashi (Kesubos / Gittin)

Penalty to prevent sinning in the future

Machlokes in Rashi between two Gemaras; Tosefos holds all Gemaras agree it's a penalty

Tosefos (Chullin 16a, Kesubos 34)

Penalty to prevent sinning - NOT to withhold benefit per se

No Kedai Sheyaasu for regular bishul (waiting would add no meaningful deterrence). Kedai Sheyaasu DOES apply to Amira L'Akum because that issur is taken lightly.

⚑ Halacha L'Maaseh: Rambam, Rosh, and Mechaber rule like Tosefos - no Kedai Sheyaasu after Shabbos for regular bishul. The Rama is silent = agrees.

⚑ Halacha L'Maaseh: Rambam, Rosh, and Mechaber rule like Tosefos - no Kedai Sheyaasu after Shabbos for regular bishul. The Rama is silent = agrees.

⚑ Halacha L'Maaseh: Rambam, Rosh, and Mechaber rule like Tosefos - no Kedai Sheyaasu after Shabbos for regular bishul. The Rama is silent = agrees.

p. 49Maaseh Shabbos

3. Halacha L'Maaseh - Which Tanna Do We Follow?

AuthorityRulingNotes

Rif, Rambam, Rosh, Ran, Ramban

Halacha like Rebbe Yehuda

Standard Rishonim position

Tosefos

Halacha like Rebbe Meir

Based on Stam Mishna in Terumos following R' Meir

Baal HaMeor

In public: tell people to be strict like Rebbe Yehuda. In private: can rule like Rebbe Meir.

Practical compromise

Mechaber (SA 318:1)

Like Rebbe Yehuda - B'shogeg: forbidden until after Shabbos. B'meizid: forever for sinner, until after Shabbos for others.

Standard Sefardi practice

Gra

Like Rebbe Meir

Based on Stam Mishna argument

Mishnah Berurah (318:7)

Basic: like Rebbe Yehuda. B'shaas hadchak (time of need): may rely on Gra (like Rebbe Meir).

Only for b'shogeg - NOT for b'meizid

⚑ Sefardim: strict like Mechaber. Yalkut Yosef: great need = may rely on Gra. Ben Ish Chai: even great need, cannot be lenient.

⚑ Sefardim: strict like Mechaber. Yalkut Yosef: great need = may rely on Gra. Ben Ish Chai: even great need, cannot be lenient.

⚑ Sefardim: strict like Mechaber. Yalkut Yosef: great need = may rely on Gra. Ben Ish Chai: even great need, cannot be lenient.

⚑ Ashkenazim: follow MB - basic rule like Rebbe Yehuda, b'shaas hadchak rely on Gra.

4. Defining Shogeg and Meizid - Categories

CategoryStatusNotes

Forgets it is Shabbos / forgets this Melacha is forbidden

SHOGEG

Standard case - penalties apply but b'shaas hadchak may rely on Gra (Ashkenaz)

Omer Mutar - thinks the action is permitted

SHOGEG (Tosefos, Ramban, Magen Avraham, MB)

Includes if a Rav incorrectly ruled it is permitted. Rambam (by implication): treated as Meizid.

Tinok Shenishba - raised without Torah

SHOGEG (Rav and Shmuel; Rambam) or ONNES (Rebbe Yochanan / Reish Lakish)

Practical: most secular Jews = shogeg. Rav Elyashiv: if exposed to observant Jews = meizid. Chazon Ish / Rav Berkovits: lenient.

Grew up observant but left observance

MEIZID

Even if left at young age

Misasek - performed an action without realizing it constituted a Melacha

Machlokes: treated as SHOGEG (Minchas Baruch, Rav Elyashiv, Rav Berkovits) or lenient (Rav SZ Auerbach)

e.g. closing door not knowing a deer was inside (trapping). Most examples involve non-food Melachos.

Onnes - sin was fully beyond one's control

No penalty at all

Rarest category

6. Maaseh Shabbos for Issurei Derabanan

Tanna / AuthorityPosition on DerabananNotes

Rebbe Yehuda (per Gra / Rambam)

LENIENT for b'shogeg derabanan - no penalty

Rambam: one who toivels vessels on Shabbos b'shogeg (derabanan) - may use immediately. Supported by Gra.

Rebbe Meir (per Gra)

Also LENIENT for derabanan b'shogeg

Gra understands other Gemaras to show Rebbe Meir is lenient here too

Pri Megadim

No difference between doraisa and derabanan - penalty applies to both

Proof: Gemara re Shehiya didn't use 'derabanan leniency' as a reason - implies derabanan carries penalty too

Biur Halacha

Rejects Pri Megadim's proof. Rules: derabanan b'shogeg = NO penalty (like Gra / Rambam)

Regarding b'meizid in a derabanan: Rambam implies the sinner may eat after Shabbos (unlike doraisa b'meizid where he's forbidden forever)

7. Special Penalties - Shehiya, Hatmana, and Chazara

Shehiya (leaving food on fire as Shabbos begins in a forbidden way)

ScenarioWho Sinned / HowHalacha

Food less than MB'D when Shabbos begins

B'Shogeg

FORBIDDEN on Shabbos. Rif / Mechaber: if food was fully cooked, permitted b'dieved. Permitted immediately after Shabbos.

Food less than MB'D when Shabbos begins

B'Meizid

FORBIDDEN on Shabbos. Forbidden until after Shabbos + Kedai Sheyaasu. (Rambam: KS only for meizid. Hagahos Ashri / MB: KS even for shogeg.)

Special reason for Shehiya gezeira even b'shogeg

-

Shehiya is a passive transgression, taken lightly - so Chazal feared: person may do it b'meizid and claim b'shogeg. (Shema yaarim.)

⚑ Is the food forbidden for others too? Hagahos Mordechai (per Rebbe Meir): only for sinner. Tur, Gra, Magen Avraham, Mishnah Berurah: forbidden for everyone.

⚑ Is the food forbidden for others too? Hagahos Mordechai (per Rebbe Meir): only for sinner. Tur, Gra, Magen Avraham, Mishnah Berurah: forbidden for everyone.

⚑ Is the food forbidden for others too? Hagahos Mordechai (per Rebbe Meir): only for sinner. Tur, Gra, Magen Avraham, Mishnah Berurah: forbidden for everyone.

p. 55Maaseh Shabbos

8. Planting a Seed on Shabbos - Why the Stricter Penalty?

The Mishna (Terumos 2:3): if one plants a seed on Shabbos b'meizid - must uproot it forever (per Rebbe Meir). Per Rebbe Yehuda: even b'shogeg must uproot. This is stricter than bishul. The Acharonim offer four explanations:

AuthorityReason for Strict PenaltyImplication for Other Melachos

Tosefos Yom Tov + Tiferes Yisrael

When possible to reverse the Melacha, one must do so. Cooking cannot be reversed; planting can.

Any reversible Melacha (e.g. building) must also be undone

Mishna Rishonah

Penalty must prevent the sinner from achieving his intent. For cooking: intent is that day - forbidding on Shabbos suffices. For planting: intent is future growth - only uprooting prevents achievement.

Building (for future use) = must destroy. Clothing / paintings = must destroy.

Kehillas Yaakov (Steipler)

Unique to planting: growth continues after Shabbos due to the Shabbos Melacha, so benefit continues perpetually.

Building: no ongoing post-Shabbos effect - no need to destroy.

Biur Halacha

Penalty can only work when the benefit is available on Shabbos itself. Planted seed: no benefit on Shabbos - so Chazal forbade benefit forever.

Building completed on Shabbos: benefit is on Shabbos - no need to destroy.

⚑ Practical: If Jews build a house on Shabbos - most Acharonim hold forbidden to live there ever. Painting / clothing made on Shabbos by a meizid = forbidden to buy. Shogeg + shaas hadchak: may be lenient with kedai sheyaasu.

⚑ Practical: If Jews build a house on Shabbos - most Acharonim hold forbidden to live there ever. Painting / clothing made on Shabbos by a meizid = forbidden to buy. Shogeg + shaas hadchak: may be lenient with kedai sheyaasu.

⚑ Practical: If Jews build a house on Shabbos - most Acharonim hold forbidden to live there ever. Painting / clothing made on Shabbos by a meizid = forbidden to buy. Shogeg + shaas hadchak: may be lenient with kedai sheyaasu.

p. 56Maaseh Shabbos

9. What Exactly Is Forbidden by Maaseh Shabbos?

IssueHalachaNotes

Selling forbidden food - monetary benefit

Permitted to sell it (Mishnah Berurah). May benefit from the sale.

Kaf HaChaim disagrees: may only sell at its raw (pre-Melacha) price - not the cooked price.

Absorptions (blios) from forbidden food - the pot

If food is forbidden on Shabbos: pot is also forbidden on Shabbos. If food is forbidden forever: pot is forbidden forever until kashered.

If food is permitted after Shabbos, pot is also permitted.

Feeding animals with forbidden food

Forbidden - normal use of food

Sound / radio / electricity - is it 'cheftza'?

Har Tzvi: no Maaseh Shabbos on sound (intangible). Minchas Yitzchak, Rav SZ Auerbach: Maaseh Shabbos does apply to sound.

When secular Jews run radio for Jews: kedai sheyaasu applies regardless.

Immersing in Mikva heated by a Jew

Rav Moshe Feinstein: permitted in shaas hadchak - 'Mitzvos lav nehenos nitnu' (physical benefit from Mitzva is incidental)

Light turned on b'issur - staying in room

May stay in room. May NOT directly use the light (e.g. read by it if it was too dark before).

Rav Nissim Karelitz: same principle for AC - may stay but do not go there specifically for AC benefit.

Electricity in Israel (powered by secular Jews)

Major machlokes: Rav Auerbach: basically permitted (cholim excuse). Rav Elyashiv / Chazon Ish / Rav Berkovits: forbidden. Chazon Ish: also a Chillul Hashem.

Consensus: ideally use a generator. Cannot resolve here - ask a Rav.

10. Maaseh Shabbos When There Is a Machlokes Whether the Act Was Forbidden

ScenarioPri MegadimMishnah Berurah (Ruling)

Machlokes whether the action was forbidden at all

Eishel Avraham: lenient - Maaseh Shabbos is derabanan, and safek derabanan = lekula. Food permitted immediately.

Rules like lenient Pri Megadim: if there is a machlokes and lenient opinion is significant (not daas yachid), food is permitted immediately.

Specific case: cooked cold liquid that had been previously cooked (mistamek verah lo) - machlokes whether forbidden

Mishbetsos Zahav: strict - Maaseh Shabbos is davar sheyesh lo matirin (will be permitted later), so we are strict even in safek.

Apparent contradiction in Pri Megadim. MB follows lenient opinion.

⚑ Practical takeaway (MB): If a significant Rishon or Acharon holds the act was permitted, there is no Maaseh Shabbos and the food may be eaten immediately.

⚑ Practical takeaway (MB): If a significant Rishon or Acharon holds the act was permitted, there is no Maaseh Shabbos and the food may be eaten immediately.

⚑ Practical takeaway (MB): If a significant Rishon or Acharon holds the act was permitted, there is no Maaseh Shabbos and the food may be eaten immediately.

12. Maaseh Shabbos for Non-Cooking Melachos - Carrying, Building, Photos

Melacha / ScenarioIs There Maaseh Shabbos?Notes

Carrying in Reshus Harabim (doraisa)

Machlokes: Tosefos: yes, same as bishul. Rabbeinu Yonah / Rambam: NO - no change was made to the object. Ramban: if returned to original place, no Maaseh Shabbos.

Chayei Adam / Biur Halacha: may rely on Rabbeinu Yonah only for shogeg + issur derabanan. But in shaas hadchak: lenient even for doraisa.

Carrying in Carmelis (derabanan)

Most places today = Carmelis (derabanan). May be lenient in shaas hadchak.

Secular Jew bringing gift on Shabbos: still forbidden on Shabbos + kedai sheyaasu (since he did it for Jews).

Object removed from techum, then returned

Permitted - three reasons: (1) Tosefos: only Issurei derabanan here. (2) Rabbeinu Yonah: no change to object. (3) Ramban: no net benefit from forbidden act.

Photo or video taken on Shabbos by non-observant Jew

If taken for non-Jews: permitted after Shabbos. If taken for Jews: Rav Berkovits - kedai sheyaasu = forever (event cannot be recaptured).

Unique because post-Shabbos recreation is impossible

Door opened with magnetic key b'issur

Rav Moshe: forbidden to walk through. Rav Auerbach / Rav Elyashiv: permitted (Melacha was done on key, not door).

Knot made on Shabbos b'issur

Forbidden to use. But if clothing can be worn without the knot: permitted (Rav Nissim Karelitz).

Stain cleaned b'issur (all Poskim agree it's forbidden)

Forbidden to wear garment if one would not have worn it with the stain
