Amira L'Akum

Amira L'Akum

Amira L'Akum

p. 62Amira L'Akum

1. Foundations

Status of the Prohibition

Amira l'akum is an issur miderabanan according to the consensus of the Rishonim. The verse in Shemos 12:16 is used merely as an asmachta (Ramban).

Three Reasons

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rashi (Avoda Zara 15a)

Daber Davar - speaking about melacha on Shabbos is itself prohibited (from Yeshaya)

Only triggered by explicit speech on Shabbos itself

Rashi (Shabbos 153a)

Shlichus - non-Jew acts as the Jew's agent; treated as if the Jew did it himself

Applies when non-Jew acts as the Jew's agent

Rambam (Shabbos 6:1)

Shabbos will become 'light in one's eyes' if Jews freely ask non-Jews to do melacha

Basis for Rav Moshe's prohibition of time-switches

p. 63Amira L'Akum

Practical Differences Between the Three Reasons

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Asking non-Jew on Erev Shabbos to do melacha on Shabbos

FORBIDDEN - Shlichus and Rambam apply; Daber Davar does not (not yet Shabbos)

Hinting to non-Jew on Shabbos (no explicit words of melacha)

FORBIDDEN - Shlichus and Rambam apply; Daber Davar does not (no speech)

Asking non-Jew on Shabbos to do melacha for a mitzva

Generally FORBIDDEN - Shlichus and Rambam still apply (see Section 3 for nuances)

Asking non-Jew on Shabbos to do melacha after Shabbos ends

FORBIDDEN only due to Daber Davar - speaking melacha on Shabbos; Shlichus doesn't apply since melacha not done on Shabbos

Bottom Line:

The halacha is l'chumra for all three reasons. All the above scenarios are forbidden unless a specific heter applies.

p. 64Amira L'Akum

2. Asking vs. Causing - For Whom Is the Melacha Done?

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Non-Jew does melacha for himself, with his own property

PERMITTED - Jew may benefit

Non-Jew does melacha for himself but with the Jew's property or food

FORBIDDEN (Shach; SA 307)

Non-Jew does melacha for the Jew's direct benefit

FORBIDDEN

Asking non-Jew to cook his own food

PERMITTED - never included in the gezeira

Non-Jew provides a service for a Jew and writes something for his own records

PERMITTED (assuming no other issues)

Telling non-Jew to put out a fire in his own house (even to protect your house)

PERMITTED - Shulchan Aruch HaRav

Causing a non-Jewish driver to stop so you can cross the street

Rav Karelitz: FORBIDDEN (asking non-Jew to do melacha for Jew's benefit). Rav Berkovits: LENIENT.

p. 65Amira L'Akum

3. Amira L'Akum for the Sake of a Mitzva

Issur Doraisa for a Mitzva - Opinions

AuthorityPositionNotes

Baal HaIttur

Permitted - amira l'akum is a lav she'ein bo maaseh; the Jew does no physical act

Extended to any mitzva (e.g. lighting candles for Shabbos seudah)

Most Rishonim (Rif, Rambam, Ramban)

Forbidden for melacha doraisa even for a mitzva

Mechaber

Forbidden - does not rely on Baal HaIttur at all

Rama

Cites minhag to be lenient; rules one should be strict unless great need

Many were accustomed to ask non-Jews to light candles for seudah

Shelah / Mishnah Berurah

Strict - not even in time of great need

Mishnah Berurah (special case)

Lenient to ask non-Jew to fix broken Eiruv on Shabbos

To prevent the masses from inadvertently sinning (rabbim)

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Lenient for a mitzva d'rabbim (e.g. lights in a shul so the tzibbur can daven/learn)

Rav Elyashiv

Strict - even for mitzva d'rabbim

p. 66Amira L'Akum

Issur Derabanan for a Mitzva - Shvus D'Shvus

The key heter: asking a non-Jew (itself a shvus) to do an issur derabanan (also a shvus) = shvus d'shvus, which Chazal treated more leniently.

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rambam (Shabbos 6:9)

Permitted to ask non-Jew to do issur derabanan for any mitzva, great need, or miksas choli

The main relied-upon position

Ramban

Only permitted for the sake of bris milah - not other mitzvos

Mechaber (SA 307:5)

Rules like the Rambam - permitted for mitzva, great need, or miksas choli

Practical halacha follows this

Practical Halacha:

Asking a non-Jew to do an issur derabanan is permitted for a mitzva, in a time of great need, or for miksas choli (Rambam / Mechaber).

For a melacha doraisa - generally strict, except: (a) fixing an Eiruv (Mishnah Berurah), (b) mitzva d'rabbim (Rav Moshe).

p. 67Amira L'Akum

4. Amira L'Amira and Melacha with a Shinui

Amira L'Amira - Asking a Non-Jew to Tell Another Non-Jew

AuthorityPositionNotes

Chavos Yair

Totally permitted - even for melacha doraisa

Avodas Hagershoni

Forbidden

Rav Shlomo Kluger

Treated as shvus d'shvus - lenient in case of loss

Mishnah Berurah

Lenient only in time of great loss; may not derive positive benefit from melacha

May benefit if light turned off; may not if turned on

p. 68Amira L'Akum

Melacha Doraisa with a Shinui - for a Mitzva

A melacha doraisa done in an unusual way (shinui) becomes an issur derabanan. May one then ask a non-Jew? This would be shvus d'shvus.

AuthorityPositionNotes

Pri Megadim

Doubtful - possibly permitted as shvus d'shvus for a mitzva

Mishnah Berurah (340:3)

Lenient - permits asking non-Jew to cut nails with a shinui for woman who needs to toivel Shabbos night

Classic case: forgot to cut nails before Shabbos

Rav Elyashiv

Only permitted where the shinui actually diminishes the quality of the melacha (writing with left hand, cutting nails)

Would NOT allow turning on light with elbow - effectiveness unchanged

Rav S.Z. Auerbach

Tends toward leniency

p. 69Amira L'Akum

5. Hinting (Remizah) to a Non-Jew

Three Categories of Hints

AuthorityPositionNotes

Type 1: Direct mention of melacha ('Whoever puts out this fire will not lose out')

FORBIDDEN - except the special case of fire or sudden damage (Mishna Shabbos 121a)

Gemara limits this heter strictly to fire/sudden damage

Type 2: Code-word command (e.g. 'clean your nose' = trim the wick)

Rama: FORBIDDEN. Bach/Taz: Lenient. Magen Avraham: FORBIDDEN.

Mishnah Berurah rules like Rama / Magen Avraham - forbidden

Type 3: Indirect comment, no melacha mentioned, no command (e.g. 'It is light in this room')

PERMITTED - no direct command, melacha not mentioned

Magen Avraham and Mishnah Berurah permit this

p. 70Amira L'Akum

Practical Cases

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

After Shabbos: 'Why didn't you turn off the light last Shabbos?'

PERMITTED (Mechaber 307:2 - Smag and Sefer HaTerumah)

Hinting on Shabbos to do melacha on Shabbos

FORBIDDEN (Rama 307:22)

Hinting on Shabbos to do melacha after Shabbos

PERMITTED (Rama)

Calling a non-Jew to come - in a case of potential damage (without specifying why)

PERMITTED (Rosh) - no worse than the fire case

Calling a non-Jew to come - time of need (e.g. to turn off light for sleep)

Minhag is to be LENIENT

Calling a non-Jew where he will know exactly which melacha to do upon arrival

FORBIDDEN unless there is potential damage (Pri Megadim)

Important Note:

Even when hinting is permitted, the Jew must be able to benefit from the resulting melacha.

If the non-Jew does a positive melacha for the Jew (e.g. turns on a light in a dark room), the Jew may not benefit regardless - so hinting achieves nothing.

Hinting is effective only where benefit would in any case be permitted: e.g. turning off a light, or adding light to an already-lit room.

p. 71Amira L'Akum

6. Benefiting from a Non-Jew's Melacha

Positive vs. Negative Benefit

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Non-Jew does melacha for himself - Jew benefits

PERMITTED (Mishna Shabbos 122a)

Non-Jew turns on light in dark room for the Jew

FORBIDDEN - positive benefit for the Jew

Non-Jew turns off light for the Jew

PERMITTED - removal of nuisance is not 'positive benefit' (Tosefos)

Non-Jew lights a second candle while first candle still burns

PERMITTED while first candle is lit; FORBIDDEN once it goes out (SA 276:4)

Non-Jew adds oil to an existing candle

May benefit from the original oil only; forbidden from the added oil (SA 276:4)

p. 72Amira L'Akum

When the Non-Jew Is Paid

AuthorityPosition

Ran

Paid non-Jew is always considered to act for himself - permitted to benefit in all cases

Hagahos Ashri

Forbidden to benefit from any positive melacha even if non-Jew is paid

Shibbolei Haleket

Middle position: permitted for non-immediate benefit (making a vessel); forbidden for immediate benefit (lighting candle)

Mechaber (252:4)

Rules like the Ran - permitted when non-Jew is paid

Rama (252:4)

Rules like Hagahos Ashri - forbidden; lenient only if Jew has no other item

Must a Jew Protest a Non-Jew's Melacha?

AuthorityPositionNotes

Hagahos Mordechai

Must protest

Applies when non-Jew does melacha with Jew's property or adds new benefit

Magen Avraham

Must protest when: (1) non-Jew adds new benefit, OR (2) non-Jew uses Jew's own property

If Jew protests and non-Jew ignores: may benefit (Bach, Mishnah Berurah)

Chayei Adam / Rav Moshe

Need not protest if non-Jew only adds to existing benefit or removes benefit - even in Jew's home

Rav Elyashiv

Strict - must protest in all cases

Minhag

Lenient - need not protest unless non-Jew adds a brand-new benefit (turning on light in dark room)

p. 73Amira L'Akum

Practical Rule:

Non-Jew turns on light in dark room for a Jew - Jew MUST protest.

Non-Jew turns off a light, or adds light where there is already some light - minhag is no protest required.

If the Jew protested and non-Jew ignored him - Jew may benefit.

p. 74Amira L'Akum

7. When the Jew Could Have Done It Himself (Rabbeinu Tam)

The Machlokes

Rabbeinu Tam: If the Jew could have obtained the benefit himself without the non-Jew's melacha, it is permitted to benefit even when the non-Jew did it for the Jew. (Example: a man can drink from the well himself - so when the non-Jew draws water for him, it is permitted.)

Ri, Rosh, Ran, Rambam: Forbidden regardless - benefiting from a non-Jew's melacha done for a Jew is always forbidden.

Halacha L'Maaseh

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Non-Jew carries food through a reshus harabim for the Jew

FORBIDDEN - basic halacha follows the Ri

Non-Jew carries food through a carmelis (issur derabanan) - significant Shabbos need

B'dieved: permitted to benefit. In time of great need: may even ask l'chatchila (Mishnah Berurah)

Non-Jew carries food through a carmelis - no particular need

FORBIDDEN

Asking non-Jew to move muktza that is in the way (Jew could move it via tiltul min hatzad)

PERMITTED - Jew could have moved it himself via tiltul min hatzad (Rama 276:3)

Asking non-Jew to move muktza to protect the muktza

FORBIDDEN - Jew could not have moved it himself for that purpose

Asking non-Jew to clean floors / wash dishes (could be done without melacha, non-Jew uses hot water for convenience)

PERMITTED - non-Jew uses hot water for his own ease; treated as acting for himself (Kaf HaChaim)

p. 75Amira L'Akum

8. Gezeira: Shema Yarbeh Bishvilo

The Rule

Even when a non-Jew does melacha for himself, Chazal forbade a Jew from benefiting when there is concern that the non-Jew will add to the melacha for the Jew's sake - if the non-Jew knows the Jew.

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Non-Jew cuts grass for his animal - does NOT know the Jew

PERMITTED

Non-Jew cuts grass for his animal - KNOWS the Jew

FORBIDDEN on Shabbos; PERMITTED immediately after Shabbos (no need to wait kedai sheyaasu)

Non-Jew lights a candle for himself - knows the Jew

PERMITTED - ner l'echad ner l'meah; one candle serves all, no concern he will add more

Non-Jew cooks food for himself - knows the Jew; Jew was present

FORBIDDEN (Beis Yosef; Mishnah Berurah)

Non-Jew cooks food - Jew was NOT present; non-Jew didn't know Jew needed it

Magen Avraham: PERMITTED. Mishnah Berurah: FORBIDDEN b'ikkar; lenient like Taz in time of need.

p. 76Amira L'Akum

Case of Doubt: Was It Done for the Jew?

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rav (per Rashi)

Strict - forbidden in any case of doubt until after Shabbos + kedai sheyaasu

Shmuel (per Rashi)

Lenient in normal case of doubt - item is forbidden only as safek muktza on Shabbos itself

Mechaber (325:7)

Brings both opinions; strict position is primary

Mishnah Berurah

Strict; lenient only l'tzorech mitzva - may benefit immediately after Shabbos

p. 77Amira L'Akum

9. Benefiting from Issur Derabanan - Scope of the Penalty

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Non-Jew does issur doraisa for a Jew

FORBIDDEN for ALL Jews to benefit - not just the specific Jew it was done for

Non-Jew does issur derabanan for a Jew (e.g. carries item from outside the techum)

Forbidden for THAT JEW only until after Shabbos. Other Jews may benefit IMMEDIATELY.

When may that specific Jew benefit after Shabbos?

Mechaber: after kedai sheyaasu. Some: immediately. Mishnah Berurah rules strictly - must wait kedai sheyaasu.

Non-Jew makes a coffin or digs a grave publicly for a Jew

FORBIDDEN FOREVER for that Jew (Rambam, SA 325:14)

Same - for other Jews

Forbidden only kedai sheyaasu

Non-Jew builds a house publicly for a Jew in a fully forbidden way

Magen Avraham: Forbidden forever. Taz: Only burial is treated this way. Mishnah Berurah: Lenient in time of need.

p. 78Amira L'Akum

10. Psik Reisha, Extreme Weather, and Time-Switches

Amira L'Akum of a Psik Reisha

AuthorityPositionNotes

Terumas HaDeshen

Permitted to ask a non-Jew to do a psik reisha of a melacha (even de'nichah leih)

Case: non-Jewish maid places cold pot near furnace which is later stoked

Gra

Forbidden - even psik reisha de'lo nichah leih; disagrees with Terumas HaDeshen entirely

Rama (253:5)

Relies on Terumas HaDeshen for amira l'akum of a psik reisha

Mishnah Berurah: amira l'akum is more lenient since Jew does no positive act

Mishnah Berurah

Lenient for psik reisha de'lo nichah leih in case of Shabbos need

Extreme Weather

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Very cold - may one ask non-Jew to light fire or turn on heater?

YES - in very cold weather everyone is considered a choleh (SA 276:5)

Not very cold - may one ask non-Jew to light fire?

Only for children; if no children present, no heter

Very hot - may one ask non-Jew to turn on air conditioning?

Minchas Yitzchak: Cannot compare to cold. However: since A/C is only issur derabanan, permitted in significant discomfort or for mitzva need (e.g. davening)

p. 79Amira L'Akum

Time-Switches

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Forbidden - same rationale as Rambam's reason for amira l'akum: Shabbos will become light in one's eyes

All other Poskim

Permitted

Minhag

Universally accepted practice is to use time-switches

p. 80Amira L'Akum

Summary: Key Practical Principles

Core Rules at a Glance:

  1. Amira l'akum is assur miderabanan - all three reasons (Daber Davar, Shlichus, Rambam) apply l'chumra.
  2. Asking a non-Jew to do an issur derabanan is permitted for a mitzva, great need, or miksas choli (Rambam / Mechaber - SA 307:5).
  3. Asking for a melacha doraisa for a mitzva: generally strict. Exceptions: fixing an Eiruv (Mishnah Berurah); mitzva d'rabbim (Rav Moshe).
  4. Benefiting from non-Jew's melacha: positive benefit forbidden; removing a nuisance (negative benefit) permitted.
  5. Adding light to an already-lit room: permitted. Turning on light in a dark room: forbidden.
  6. When non-Jew is paid: Mechaber lenient, Rama strict.
  7. Hinting: only indirect comments with no command and no mention of melacha are permitted.
  8. Amira l'amira (asking non-Jew to tell another non-Jew): lenient only in great loss; no positive benefit.
  9. Time-switches: permitted - all Poskim except Rav Moshe.
  10. Psik reisha: Rama is lenient for amira l'akum; Mishnah Berurah lenient for de'lo nichah leih in Shabbos need.
p. 81Amira L'Yisrael

Amira L'Yisrael

1. Asking a Fellow Jew to Do Melacha - Erev / Motsei Shabbos

The Core Question

May a Jew who has already accepted Shabbos ask a fellow Jew who has not yet done so to perform melacha for him? And the reverse: may one who has not yet taken out Shabbos ask one who already has?

Opinions

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rashba (SA 263:17)

Permitted - since the second Jew has not yet accepted Shabbos, there is nothing wrong with the request. No issue of Daber Davar because the melacha is entirely permitted for the one being asked.

Mechaber rules like the Rashba

Ran

Disputes the Rashba's proof; seems to argue l'halacha

Darchei Moshe: the Ran may not disagree l'halacha, only raised a question

Rama (263:17)

Permits asking and using the resulting melacha; applies the same kal v'chomer to Motsei Shabbos

Mishnah Berurah rules like Mechaber and Rama

Levush

Strict regarding Motsei Shabbos - Kedusha of Shabbos continues until one personally takes it out

Levush: permitted once Birchas Hamazon is recited even without Havdala

Mishnah Berurah

Rules like Mechaber and Rama in both directions

p. 82Amira L'Yisrael

Practical Cases - Erev and Motsei Shabbos

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Jew who accepted Shabbos early asks a Jew who has not yet done so to do melacha

PERMITTED (Rashba, Mechaber, Rama, Mishnah Berurah)

Jew who has not yet taken out Shabbos asks a Jew who already has to do melacha for him

PERMITTED (Rama) - minhag and Mishnah Berurah rule this way

Jew accepted Shabbos early out of halachic concern (e.g. concern it may actually be Shabbos)

FORBIDDEN - similar to one keeping second day of Yom Kippur; he fears the other Jew is doing an issur

Jew who accepted Shabbos early (l'hiddur, not from halachic concern) asks another to do melacha

PERMITTED (standard case of the Rashba)

Person strict for Rabbeinu Tam's zman (m'ikar hadin) - may he ask someone who is not?

FORBIDDEN (Rav Wosner)

Person strict for Rabbeinu Tam's zman only as a chumra - may he ask someone who is not?

Rav Wosner: In doubt. Rav Berkovits: Lenient (follows Rav Auerbach's reasoning)

p. 83Amira L'Yisrael

Parent Asking Child (of Any Age) on Erev Shabbos

The Torah states 'you and your son shall rest' - it is an issur midoraisa for a parent to ask a child to do melacha for him on Shabbos.

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Parent accepted Shabbos; child has not - parent asks child to do melacha

Chavos Yair: FORBIDDEN - the issur of 'atah u'vincha' applies. Rav Wosner: LENIENT - child is not yet in Shabbos.

p. 84Amira L'Yisrael

2. Asking a Jew Who Holds a Lenient Opinion

The Core Issue

May a Jew who follows a strict ruling ask a Jew who follows a lenient ruling to do the melacha for him? Two potential problems: (1) Daber Davar - asking someone to do what you hold is forbidden. (2) Lifnei Iver - placing a stumbling block before another Jew.

Rav Auerbach's Ruling (Minchas Shlomo 2:35)

If a Jew is strict only because of his Rabbi's ruling or community minhag - not because he personally concluded the halacha is strict - he does not believe the other person is doing an issur. Therefore there is no Lifnei Iver and no Daber Davar, and he may ask the lenient Jew to do the melacha.

If the Jew personally investigated the sugya and concluded l'halacha that the strict view is correct, he may NOT ask the lenient Jew - he considers the other to be doing an issur.

Practical Cases

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Sefardi (follows Mechaber: forbidden to reheat warm liquid) asks Ashkenazi (follows Rama: permitted) to reheat liquid

Rav Auerbach: PERMITTED if Sefardi has not personally investigated and holds it as issur - he just follows his Rav. Rav Berkovits rules this way.

Jew personally holds the strict view after learning the sugya - asks lenient Jew to do melacha

FORBIDDEN - he believes the other is doing an issur (Rav Auerbach; Rav Wosner strict in any case)

Jew strict for Rabbeinu Tam only as his Rav's ruling - asks someone not keeping Rabbeinu Tam to do melacha before Rabbeinu Tam's zman

Rav Auerbach / Rav Berkovits: PERMITTED. Rav Wosner: FORBIDDEN.

p. 85Amira L'Yisrael

Bottom Line:

Rav Berkovits rules like Rav Auerbach: if one is strict only due to minhag or one's Rav, one may ask a lenient Jew.

Most other Poskim (including Rav Wosner) are strict.

3. Ben Chutz L'Aretz Asking an Israeli Jew on Yom Tov Sheini

The Question

A Jew from chutz l'aretz visiting Israel keeps two days of Yom Tov; Israelis keep one. May he ask an Israeli Jew to do melacha for him on the second day?

Opinions

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rav Moshe Feinstein (Igros Moshe OC 3:74, 4:107)

Generally FORBIDDEN - treats it like amira l'akum (the laws of amira l'yisrael parallel amira l'akum here). Also a safek in a davar she'yesh lo matirin - must be strict.

Exception: Israeli workers in his factory in Israel - permitted (this was allowed even in the time of Chazal when the doubt was real)

Rav Auerbach

Lenient in a time of great need

Rav Elyashiv

Lenient for a mitzva need; most Poskim disagree

Rav Berkovits

Follows Rav Moshe - same halachos as amira l'akum. Therefore: issur derabanan permitted for need or mitzva; issur doraisa generally forbidden.

Many Yom Tov issurim are only miderabanan (e.g. electricity, turning on lights - only issur of molid)

p. 86Amira L'Yisrael
ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Ben chutz l'aretz asks Israeli Jew to do melacha doraisa on second day Yom Tov

FORBIDDEN (Rav Moshe; Rav Berkovits)

Ben chutz l'aretz asks Israeli Jew to do issur derabanan on second day Yom Tov (e.g. turn on light) - for a need or mitzva

PERMITTED - follows the rules of amira l'akum: shvus d'shvus for mitzva/need (Rav Berkovits)

Ben chutz l'aretz has Israeli workers in his factory - second day Yom Tov

PERMITTED (Rav Moshe - was permitted even when the doubt was real in Chazal's time)

p. 87Amira L'Yisrael

4. Business on Shabbos and Schar Shabbos

Doing Business on Shabbos

It is assur miderabanan to conduct business on Shabbos - a gezeira to prevent a Jew from coming to write on Shabbos. Borrowing and lending items is permitted.

Rebbe Akiva Eiger: Forbidden to make an acquisition on Erev Shabbos that takes effect on Shabbos (e.g. mechiras chametz when Erev Pesach falls on Shabbos). Ksav Sofer and Maharam Shick agree; Maharsham disagrees. Poskim are generally concerned for Rebbe Akiva Eiger's view.

The Drinks Machine / Online Business - Two Issues

AuthorityPositionNotes

Orchos Shabbos

Lenient re: Rebbe Akiva Eiger - he only forbade an explicit condition that acquisition takes place on Shabbos; a machine involves no such words or act. Logic applies to online business too (but consult a posek for specific situations).

Minchas Yitzchak

Lenient with four conditions: (1) machine not on Jew's property; (2) not publicly known to be the Jew's; (3) owner intends to transfer ownership to buyer on Erev Shabbos; (4) owner intends not to acquire payment until after Shabbos.

Rav Wosner

FORBIDDEN - constitutes Schar Shabbos

p. 88Amira L'Yisrael

Schar Shabbos - Earning Money on Shabbos

It is rabbinically forbidden to be paid specifically for work done only on Shabbos (a gezeira to protect other business prohibitions). Paying a non-Jewish worker for Shabbos work is permitted - the issur applies to the one being paid.

The Three Heterim for Schar Shabbos

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Havlaah - worker is hired for the week (not Shabbos alone); pay for Shabbos is 'absorbed' into the weekly wage

PERMITTED - the most common heter. Also applies to a Baal Korei paid for his weekly preparation + leining.

Matanah - employer designates the payment as a gift, not wages (worker must genuinely accept this)

PERMITTED - used for babysitters who work only on Shabbos. Note: morally questionable to rely on this routinely.

L'tzorech Mitzva - Chazzan, Baal Korei, etc.

Mechaber 306:5 brings two opinions. Mishnah Berurah: one who relies on leniency 'will not see blessing from his work on Shabbos.'

p. 89Amira L'Yisrael

Interest on Bank Accounts

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rav Auerbach

Schar Shabbos does NOT apply to interest payments - permitted

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Schar Shabbos DOES apply in principle. However: interest is calculated daily (day = morning to night), while Shabbos runs night to day - so each day's payment is partially Erev Shabbos and partially Shabbos (havlaah). Practically: only an issue when Shabbos is sandwiched between two days of Yom Tov.

In that case: give the disputed day's accrual anonymously to tzedaka

p. 90Amira L'Yisrael

5. Amira L'Kattan - Asking a Child to Do Melacha

Background: Is Beis Din Obligated to Stop a Child from Sinning?

There is a machlokes Amoraim (Yevamos 113b-114a) whether Beis Din must prevent a child from doing an issur doraisa. All agree: Beis Din need NOT prevent a child from doing an issur derabanan.

AuthorityPosition

Rashba

Beis Din is NOT obligated to prevent a child from doing issurei doraisa

Tosefos

Every adult is obligated to stop a child above the age of chinuch from sinning (doraisa and derabanan)

Rambam

Adults are not obligated; only the father is obligated to stop his own child (because of chinuch)

Mechaber (343:1)

Rules like the Rambam - adults not obligated to stop other people's children

Rama (343:1)

Brings Tosefos - adults are obligated for children above chinuch age

Chayei Adam / Mishnah Berurah

Everyone obligated for issur doraisa; only father obligated for issur derabanan

p. 91Amira L'Yisrael

Causing a Child to Do an Issur Doraisa

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Actively causing a child of any age to do an issur doraisa

FORBIDDEN - two issurim: general prohibition + 'Atah u'vincha' (specific to Shabbos, from the Torah's verse)

Putting a very young child near a light switch knowing he may turn it on

Some Poskim lenient (not a direct command). Many Gedolim strongly oppose this leniency - only use in rare, significant need.

Causing a Child to Do an Issur Derabanan

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rambam / Mechaber

FORBIDDEN to cause a child to do an issur derabanan in all circumstances

Rashba / Ran

Permitted if it is for the BENEFIT OF THE CHILD

Rebbe Akiva Eiger (cited in Biur Halacha)

Permits asking child to carry a siddur through a carmelis (issur derabanan) if the child uses the siddur - father may then use it too

Biur Halacha implies one may rely on this

Shulchan Aruch HaRav

Rashba only meant to forbid on a FIXED basis; on an occasional basis even asking for the adult's benefit is permitted

Mishnah Berurah does not seem to accept this leniency

p. 92Amira L'Yisrael

Practical Cases - Amira L'Kattan

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Asking child to do issur derabanan for the child's own benefit

PERMITTED (Rashba, relied upon l'maaseh)

Asking child to do issur derabanan for the adult's benefit - occasional basis, time of need / mitzva

May rely on Shulchan Aruch HaRav in a time of need

Asking child to do issur derabanan for the adult's benefit - fixed/regular basis

FORBIDDEN (all opinions)

Asking child to do issur doraisa in any case

FORBIDDEN (all opinions)

Child sinning for himself - child below age of chinuch

No adult is obligated to stop him (all agree)

Child sinning for himself - child above age of chinuch

Father obligated. Other adults: Mechaber - not obligated; Rama/Tosefos - obligated for doraisa; Mishnah Berurah: obligated for doraisa only.

Child doing melacha that benefits an adult (adult did not ask) - adult must stop him

YES - Mishnah Berurah: treated as if adult asked, even without a request

Asking child to do a psik reisha melacha (child does not realize melacha is occurring)

PERMITTED (Rav Auerbach, Rav Karelitz, Rav Scheinberg) - e.g. asking young child to open fridge if child doesn't know light goes on

p. 93Amira L'Yisrael

Key Distinctions at a Glance:

Issur doraisa - forbidden to cause a child in all cases. No exceptions.

Issur derabanan - forbidden per Mechaber; permitted for child's own benefit per Rashba (relied upon in time of need).

Psik reisha where child is unaware - permitted (Rav Auerbach et al.).

The obligation to stop a sinning child rests primarily on the father; other adults obligated for doraisa (Mishnah Berurah).

Summary: Key Practical Principles

Core Rules at a Glance:

  1. Erev Shabbos: One who accepted Shabbos may ask one who has not to do melacha - permitted (Rashba, Mechaber, Rama).
  2. Motsei Shabbos: One who has not yet taken out Shabbos may ask one who has - permitted (Rama; Levush is strict).
  3. Exception: If the person is strict due to halachic concern that it is actually Shabbos/Yom Tov - FORBIDDEN.
  4. Following a different posek: If strict only due to minhag/Rav (not personal conviction) - may ask a lenient Jew (Rav Auerbach / Rav Berkovits).
  5. Ben chutz l'aretz in Israel on Yom Tov Sheini: Issur doraisa - forbidden. Issur derabanan for need/mitzva - permitted (Rav Berkovits, following Rav Moshe).
  6. Schar Shabbos: Forbidden to be paid for Shabbos-only work. Heterim: havlaah (most common), matanah, possibly l'tzorech mitzva.
  7. Interest: Rav Auerbach - no issur. Rav Moshe - issur in principle; practically only an issue when Shabbos is sandwiched by two Yom Tov days.
  8. Causing a child to do issur doraisa - forbidden in all cases.
  9. Causing a child to do issur derabanan for child's benefit - permitted (Rashba; relied upon).
  10. Psik reisha via a child who is unaware - permitted (Rav Auerbach et al.).
p. 94Kavannah U'Maaseh

Kavannah U'Maaseh

1. Missasek

Missasek: A person intends to do one action but accidentally does a different forbidden action. He did not plan to do the forbidden act at all. Distinct from shogeg (knew the act, not the issur).

Two Types (Tosefos, Sanhedrin 62b)

TypeStatus

Missasek She'naaseh Machshavto His intent was partially fulfilled (e.g. reached for this vegetable - grabbed the same vegetable, but it was attached)

Rav: patur from korban only; still transgresses issur doraisa (Rebbe Akiva Eiger) Nesivos / Rav Chaim Soloveitchik: not issur doraisa

Missasek She'lo Naaseh Machshavto His intent was not fulfilled at all (e.g. cut a completely different vegetable)

Patur from korban AND from issur doraisa Still assur miderabanan (Rebbe Akiva Eiger)

Source for Exemption

SourceApplies To

Verse: 'It must become known to him' (Vayikra 4:23)

She'naaseh Machshavto - exempts from korban only

Meleches Machsheves (intent required)

She'lo Naaseh Machshavto - exempts from issur doraisa entirely

p. 95Kavannah U'Maaseh

Practical Applications: (1) Obligated to stop someone else about to do a melacha b'missasek (e.g., opening a fridge not knowing the light is on). (2) Take precautions - check pockets before Shabbos to avoid carrying b'missasek (Shulchan Aruch 252:7).

2. Dvar She'eino Miskavein & Psik Reisha

Dvar She'eino Miskavein: A permitted act that may (but not necessarily will) cause a forbidden act. Machlokes Tanaim - halacha follows Rebbe Shimon (permitted).

CategoryDefinitionStatus

Dvar She'eino Miskavein

Permitted act that may cause a forbidden result (not certain)

MUTAR - halacha follows Rebbe Shimon (SA 337:1)

Psik Reisha De'nichah Leih

Permitted act that will certainly cause a forbidden result; person is glad for the result

ASSUR MIDORAISA

Psik Reisha De'lo Nichah Leih

Certainly causes forbidden result; person does NOT care

Assur miderabanan (Tosefos / Mechaber). Aruch: mutar. When combined with other leniencies, may be permitted.

p. 96Kavannah U'Maaseh

Rebbe Yehuda vs. Rebbe Shimon

OpinionPosition

Rebbe Yehuda

Dvar she'eino miskavein: assur midoraisa in rest of Torah; assur miderabanan on Shabbos (Tosefos - because of Meleches Machsheves)

Rebbe Shimon (halacha)

Mutar in all of Torah - act is not considered transgression at all

Practical Cases

CaseHalacha L'Maaseh

Walking on grass (may be torn up)

MUTAR - dvar she'eino miskavein

Gently brushing teeth (gums may bleed)

MUTAR - dvar she'eino miskavein

Washing hands over own lawn (will water it)

ASSUR midoraisa - psik reisha de'nichah leih (he wants his lawn watered)

Turning on hot tap (heats boiler water)

Most Poskim: psik reisha de'nichah leih - ASSUR midoraisa. Rav Ovadia / Rav Abbah Shaul: de'lo nichah leih - only miderabanan.

Running on tall grass (will be torn)

Assur miderabanan - psik reisha de'lo nichah leih

Brushing hair with hard brush (will uproot hair)

Assur miderabanan - psik reisha de'lo nichah leih

Stepping on ants while walking

Assur miderabanan - psik reisha de'lo nichah leih

p. 97Kavannah U'Maaseh

3. Safek Psik Reisha

Safek Psik Reisha: An act that will definitely cause a melacha IF the conditions are present - but it is uncertain whether those conditions exist (e.g., closing a lid not knowing if a fly is inside).

AuthorityPositionScope

Taz

Permitted - treated as dvar she'eino miskavein

Even issur doraisa

Biur Halacha

Forbidden for issur doraisa. Permitted for issur derabanan (safek derabanan = lenient)

Splits by doraisa/derabanan

Shevisas HaShabbos

On Shabbos: always permitted (no Meleches Machsheves). In rest of Torah: forbidden for issur doraisa

Shabbos: always lenient

Rav S.Z. Auerbach / Rav Berkovits

Rule like Shevisas HaShabbos

Standard ruling

Rebbe Akiva Eiger / Rama (YD)

Strict - forbidden

Even issur derabanan?

p. 98Kavannah U'Maaseh

Practical Cases

CaseHalacha L'Maaseh

Closing lid when flies may be inside (issur derabanan - trapping flies)

PERMITTED - Taz and Mishnah Berurah agree (only derabanan)

Closing door when deer may be inside (issur doraisa - trapping deer)

Taz: PERMITTED. Mishnah Berurah: FORBIDDEN. Rav Berkovits: PERMITTED.

Opening fridge when unsure if light is on (issur doraisa)

Taz: PERMITTED. Rav Auerbach / Rav Berkovits: PERMITTED. Minchas Yitzchak: FORBIDDEN.

4. Melacha She'ein Sricha Legufa

Melacha She'ein Sricha Legufa: Person intends to do the melacha, but not for the same purpose it was done in the Mishkan / not for a constructive benefit. Machlokes Rishonim on the definition and status.

Definition - Two Opinions

RashiTosefos

Done merely to remove something from one's way, not to accomplish a positive goal

Done for a different purpose than the melacha served in the Mishkan

p. 99Kavannah U'Maaseh
AuthorityStatus of Melacha She'ein Sricha LegufaNotes

Rambam (rules like Rebbe Yehuda)

ASSUR MIDORAISA

Rach / Mechaber (rules like Rebbe Shimon)

Assur miderabanan

Halacha follows this

Rebbe Shimon (Tanna)

Patur; assur miderabanan

Not chayav for korban; does not fulfill Meleches Machsheves

Special stringency: Melacha she'ein sricha legufa, even though only miderabanan, is treated MORE strictly than ordinary issurei derabanan - e.g., one may not ask a non-Jew to do it even for a mitzva or great need (Mishnah Berurah 278:3).

Cutting Nails - Melacha She'sricha or She'ein Sricha?

AuthorityPosition

Tosefos / Magen Avraham

Cutting nails = she'ein sricha legufa - assur miderabanan only

Ramban / Rivash

Cutting nails = she'sricha legufa - ASSUR MIDORAISA (leaves behind improved body)

Mishnah Berurah (340:1)

Rules like Ramban/Rivash - ASSUR MIDORAISA

p. 100Kavannah U'Maaseh

Key Practical Cases

CaseHalacha L'Maaseh

Turning off a light (kibui)

She'ein sricha legufa - assur miderabanan. But does NOT have same leniencies as other derabanan.

Extinguishing glowing metal for public safety

PERMITTED - miderabanan + she'ein sricha legufa

Extinguishing glowing wood for public safety

PERMITTED (Mechaber follows Rebbe Shimon / Rach - miderabanan)

Trapping dangerous animal (snake)

PERMITTED for all - even Rambam - no sakanas nefashos required

p. 101Kavannah U'Maaseh

5. Gramma

Gramma: An indirect act where a melacha occurs as a downstream consequence of the person's action, not directly. The Tannaim debate which acts qualify as gramma.

AuthorityPositionLimit

Rav Shimon Ben Nannis / Rabbanan (halacha)

Gram kibui (indirect extinguishing) - PERMITTED

Rama: only in case of loss/damage

Rav Yosi

Gram kibui - FORBIDDEN

Rabbeinu Tam (strict opinion in Tosefos)

Only gramma with interim stage (fire cracks vessel → water extinguishes) is gramma. Wall of water around fire = direct act.

Lenient opinion in Tosefos

Even wall of water around fire = gramma - permitted

Mechaber (265:4)

Lenient opinion: permits water under oil if not intending to extinguish

Rama (334:22)

Permits all gram kibui - but only in case of loss

Standard ruling

p. 102Kavannah U'Maaseh

Opening Doors (Gramma 2)

CaseHalacha L'Maaseh

Opening door opposite candle - strong wind blowing

FORBIDDEN - direct act of extinguishing (psik reisha)

Opening door opposite candle - no wind

Rama: PERMITTED. Magen Avraham / Mishnah Berurah: FORBIDDEN (gezeira)

Opening door opposite furnace - strong unusual wind

FORBIDDEN - psik reisha of havara

Opening door opposite furnace - regular wind

FORBIDDEN - gezeira lest one do so with strong wind (Abaye / Mechaber 277:2)

Opening door opposite furnace - no wind

PERMITTED

Closing door opposite candle (fire burns longer)

PERMITTED - menias hamonaya (removes obstacle to extinguishing, not kindling)

Menias Hamonaya: Removing a factor that would extinguish a fire (thereby keeping it burning longer) is NOT considered an act of havara - it is permitted. Rav Auerbach: extending a time-switch is comparable (permitted). Rav Elyashiv / Rav Moshe: forbidden (direct act).

p. 103Kavannah U'Maaseh

Rosh vs. Rach - Gramma with Intent / Psik Reisha

RoshRach

Gramma is NEVER chayav midoraisa, even with intent (except zoreh, where gramma is the normal method). Gramma + psik reisha: may be totally permitted.

Gramma WITH INTENT to do melacha = direct act - CHAYAV midoraisa. Gramma + psik reisha (even without intent) = direct act - CHAYAV midoraisa.

Opening Fridge Door (Motor Not Running)

AuthorityRuling

Har Tzvi / Rav Auerbach

PERMITTED - gramma + psik reisha (follows Rosh/Avnei Nezer); no special need required

Minchas Yitzchak / Rav Moshe Feinstein

FORBIDDEN when motor is not running (follows Rach). PERMITTED when motor is running.

p. 104Kavannah U'Maaseh

6. Shinui

Shinui: Performing a melacha in an unusual way. Most types of genuine shinui reduce the melacha from issur doraisa to assur miderabanan.

What Makes Something a Shinui?

RuleExample

Melacha done normally everywhere = not a shinui

Writing with right hand (for right-hander)

Melacha done unusually everywhere = shinui

Writing with left hand (for right-hander)

Done unusually in one place because of unique circumstances (e.g., spinning directly from goat - only experts can) = NOT a shinui for those experts

Women who spun for the Mishkan

Done unusually in one place by choice (not circumstance) = shinui even for locals (batla daatan etsel kol adam)

Carrying on head in Hutsal - still a shinui

Done unusually by one family = always a shinui

Squeezing pomegranates

Specific Shinui Rulings

ActionStatus

Carrying heavy items on one's head

Assur midoraisa - not a shinui (Rambam: only light items = shinui)

Carrying light items on one's head

Assur miderabanan - shinui

Writing with weaker hand (right-hander writes left)

Assur miderabanan - shinui

Erasing with weaker hand

ASSUR MIDORAISA - not a shinui (Avnei Nezer: erasing works equally with either hand)

Pressing a button with weaker hand

ASSUR MIDORAISA - not a shinui

Ambidextrous person writing with either hand

Assur midoraisa - no shinui

p. 105Kavannah U'Maaseh

When Is It Permitted to Do a Melacha with a Shinui?

SituationRuling

Kavod ha'brios (human dignity)

PERMITTED - e.g., tearing toilet paper with elbows, or leaving in water to tear when flushed

Time of great loss (Magen Avraham)

Permitted (but Mishnah Berurah does not cite this - questionable)

Choleh she'ein bo sakana (issur derabanan only)

PERMITTED with shinui - e.g., turning on dud shemesh tap

Life-threatening situation (pikuach nefesh)

Do melacha normally if needed; use shinui only if no loss of effectiveness or speed

Signing name for vital operation on Shabbos

Prefer to sign with weaker hand - reduces to miderabanan

p. 106Kavannah U'Maaseh

7. Mekalkel

Mekalkel: Performing a melacha in a purely destructive way - with no constructive purpose. Such an act is assur miderabanan, not midoraisa.

ActionStatus

Purely destructive act (tearing clothing to discard it; destroying an object to throw it away)

Assur miderabanan - mekalkel

Destructive act in order to fix/rebuild in the SAME place (soser al menas livnos - tearing to sew up, erasing to write over)

ASSUR MIDORAISA - not mekalkel

Tearing clothing out of anger or mourning (kria)

ASSUR MIDORAISA - not mekalkel (Gemara 105b; halacha follows this)

Erasing for a constructive purpose other than writing over (e.g., to remove evidence)

Machlokes: Ritva - miderabanan (mekalkel). Pri Megadim / Mishnah Berurah - midoraisa. Halacha: ASSUR MIDORAISA.

Dismantling to rebuild in a DIFFERENT place (Rebbe Yossi's extra condition)

Patur according to Rebbe Yossi; Halacha does not follow this strictly

Mekalkel applies to ALL melachos, not only tearing and erasing (Rashi). Any positive purpose is sufficient to make an act midoraisa - does not need to be specifically 'al menas litfor / lichtov' (Biur Halacha 340).

p. 107Kavannah U'Maaseh

8. Dvar She'eino Miskayem

Dvar She'eino Miskayem: A melacha whose effect does not last a sufficient amount of time. Usually assur miderabanan; for certain melachos (tying, tearing) even permitted.

How Long Must the Effect Last?

AuthorityStandard

Rambam

Must last until end of Shabbos to be considered miskayem

Rashi (implication)

Must last permanently (or at least much longer than Shabbos)

Nuances

RuleExample

If it is normal for a substance to produce temporary results, it is NOT considered eino miskayem - still chayav

Writing with pencil (normally temporary) - chayav. Writing in sand - patur (not normal).

Effect permanent in itself, made temporary by external factor - Rambam: not eino miskayem (chayav). Tosefos: eino miskayem (patur).

Writing on flesh - erased by sweat. Rambam: chayav. Tosefos: patur.

Person intends to undo the melacha's effect himself - Tosefos: eino miskayem (patur / permitted). Rambam: disagrees.

Braiding hair intending to unbraid - Tosefos: permitted. Rambam: chayav.

Knot: not intended to last permanently - Avnei Nezer: eino miskayem, NOT even assur miderabanan

Tying a knot intending to untie before 24 hours - PERMITTED

p. 108Kavannah U'Maaseh

Practical Examples

ActionStatus

Applying rouge / nail polish (tzovaya)

Assur miderabanan - eino miskayem

Writing on fogged window / dusty table (koseiv)

Assur miderabanan - eino miskayem

Building a temporary structure, spreading sheet between chairs (boneh)

Assur miderabanan - eino miskayem

Tying a temporary knot (intending to untie within 24 hrs)

PERMITTED - eino miskayem (Avnei Nezer)

Disposable diaper: taping ends (tofer)

PERMITTED - clearly eino miskayem (few hours)

Making a snowman (boneh)

Assur miderabanan - eino miskayem

p. 109Kavannah U'Maaseh

9. Shnayim She'asu

Shnayim She'asu: Two people together perform a melacha. Halacha follows R Yehuda and R Shimon in their areas of agreement (Mishna 92b).

SituationWho is Chayav?Notes

Both could have done it alone

Neither - both PATUR (but assur miderabanan)

Rebbe Meir: both chayav; halacha rejects this

Neither could have done it alone

Both CHAYAV

Each needed the other to complete the melacha

One could do it alone; one could not

The one who COULD do it alone is CHAYAV; the other is patur

The weaker one is a mere 'mesayaya'

One performs akira, other performs hanacha (carrying)

Both PATUR from korban; both assur miderabanan

Agreed by all Tanaim (93a)

Mesayaya - One Who Assists

AuthorityPosition

Taz (YD 198)

Mesayaya = ASSUR MIDORAISA - even holding out one's hand for a non-Jew to cut nails constitutes assisting

Shach / Rama / Mishnah Berurah (halacha)

Mesayaya does NOT transgress even miderabanan (except for payos - special limmud). PERMITTED.

p. 110Kavannah U'Maaseh

Practical case: Woman needs to cut her nails before a Shabbos night tevila (forgot before Shabbos). Taz: forbidden even to let non-Jew cut (mesayaya). Shach / Mishnah Berurah: permitted to ask non-Jew; woman may hold out her hand.

p. 111–112Borrer — Selecting

Borrer

1. Foundations - Borrer, Zoreh & Meraked

Defining the Three Melachos

MelachaMethod (Rashi 73a)Material (Rashi 75b)Stage in Bread-Making (Ran)

Borrer

By hand

Removes stones

Middle stage

Zoreh

By wind (thrown in air)

Removes straw

Early stage

Meraked

With a sieve

Sifts fine flour

Final stage

The consensus of Poskim: the essential difference is method (first reason), not material type (second reason).

Is Borrer a Melacha She'ein Sricha L'gufa?

AuthorityPositionPractical Consequence

Baal HaMeor

Yes - it is she'ein sricha l'gufa (a negative act of removal)

Still Assur midoraisa since it was performed in the Mishkan

Ramban

No - it is she'sricha l'gufa (a positive act of cleaning a mixture)

Chayav because the Melacha itself is positive in essence

Biur Halacha

Follows the Ramban (based on his ruling re: gozez)

This is the operative halachic position

p. 113Borrer — Selecting

Is One Chayav for Removing Only Some of the Pesoles?

SourceRuling

Yerushalmi

Patur unless all pesoles is removed from the mixture (or all pesoles from a grogeres-sized portion)

Bavli

Chayav even for removing some of the pesoles

Halacha L'Maaseh

Follows the Bavli - Assur midoraisa to remove any pesoles from a mixture

Meshamer - Does It Constitute Borrer?

OpinionRuling

Rabbah

Meshamer is included in both Meraked and Borrer (the Rambam rules like Rabbah)

Rebbe Zeira

Meshamer is only Meraked, not Borrer (because in Borrer the good does not descend)

Bottom Line:

Halacha: One is Chayav for Meshamer under both Meraked and Borrer (Rambam / SA).

2. The Three Conditions for Permitted Borrer

To avoid Issur Borrer, all three conditions must be met simultaneously:

ConditionThe RequirementIf Violated

1. B'Yad - By Hand

Select using one's hand only (not a utensil)

Assur midoraisa if kli meyuchad; Assur miderabanan if other utensil

2. Miyad - Immediately

Intend to eat the food right after selecting

Assur midoraisa if selecting for later

3. Ochel Mitoch Pesoles - Good from Bad

Remove the food (ochel), not the pesoles

Assur midoraisa to remove pesoles even with hand, even immediately

p. 114Borrer — Selecting

Bottom Line:

All three conditions must be present simultaneously: select with the hand (b'yad), immediately before eating (miyad), and take the food from the pesoles (ochel mitoch pesoles).

If any one condition is missing, the act of Borrer is Assur midoraisa.

Why Is B'Yad Permitted?

AuthorityRationale

Shibbolei HaLeket / Rashi approach

Using one's hand is a shinui gamur - a complete deviation from the normal way of doing this Melacha, and therefore totally permitted

Rabbeinu Chananel (Rach) / Tosefos

Borrer by hand is derech achila - it is part of the normal eating process, not an act of Melacha

Practical Differences: Rashi vs. Rach/Tosefos

ScenarioAccording to RashiAccording to Rach/Tosefos

Borrer by hand, intent to eat later

Patur (hand = shinui gamur, regardless of intent)

Assur midoraisa (not derech achila if not eating now)

Using kli meyuchad, but eating immediately

May be lenient (intent matters)

Assur midoraisa (kli use is never derech achila)

p. 115Borrer — Selecting

3. Definition of a Taaroves (Mixture)

Types of Mixtures to Which Borrer Applies

TypeDescriptionExamples

1. Mingled / Interspersed

Items mixed together in one place

Peanuts & raisins in a bowl; mixed cutlery; assorted laundry; mixed fruit

2. Embedded / Attached

Pesoles physically attached to the food

Bones in fish; fat in meat; peel on fruit or vegetables; dirt on produce

3. Absorbed / Interfused

Small pieces suspended in a liquid or substance

Small food pieces in soup; insects on lettuce; meat pieces in gravy

Selecting vs. Separating - Rambam vs. Tosefos

QuestionRambamTosefosHalacha

Is Borrer applicable when neither food is pesoles?

Yes - separating two edible types is Assur even when neither is pesoles

No - Borrer requires that one type be viewed as pesoles by the person

Strict like the Rambam (MB / Biur Halacha)

If the person wants both foods equally, may he separate them?

Assur midoraisa if for later use

Permitted - no pesoles exists in the mixture

Assur - follow the Rambam

Practical Example: Peanuts and raisins in a bowl - may one sort them into separate bowls for later?

p. 116Borrer — Selecting

Bottom Line:

According to Rambam (= halacha): FORBIDDEN if intent is to use them later.

According to Tosefos: Permitted (neither is pesoles).

Halacha: Forbidden. This applies equally to toys, books, cutlery (majority of contemporary Poskim follow Taz/MB that Borrer applies to non-food items).

Borrer on One Type of Food

AuthorityRuling on One Type of Food

Terumas HaDeshen (Simun 57)

No Issur Borrer - one type does not constitute a taaroves. Permitted to take larger or smaller pieces.

Taz

Issur Borrer does apply even to one type. Forbidden to select a specific size.

Rama / Mishnah Berurah

Rule like the Terumas HaDeshen - no Issur on one type

Exception: When Size Difference Makes Them 'Two Types'

Even within one 'type,' if the size or feature makes a significant difference in function, the Issur Borrer applies as if they were two separate types.

CaseRuling

Large challos mixed with small rolls

Issur Borrer applies - size affects function significantly

Large spoons mixed with small spoons

Issur Borrer applies - different functions

Chicken legs mixed with thighs

Machlokes: Rav Auerbach strict; Rav Elyashiv and Rav Karelitz lenient

p. 117Borrer — Selecting

Borrer on One Piece of Food (Embedded Pesoles)

Part of the FoodStatusRuling

Totally inedible parts (e.g. actual stones)

Genuine pesoles

Assur midoraisa to remove

Parts edible only with great difficulty (e.g. very tough outer leaves)

Quasi-pesoles

Assur miderabanan (Maggid Mishneh / Rama / MB)

Edible parts the person does not want (e.g. apple peel)

Unwanted but edible

Magen Avraham: Assur (follows Rambam that Borrer applies). Halacha follows the Magen Avraham.

Removing the Skin of Chicken

AuthorityRuling

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Permitted in all cases - chicken skin is not comparable to fruit peel; it is one part of the chicken

Rav Elyashiv

Can be an act of Borrer (comparable to fruit peel) - only permitted if eating the chicken immediately

Filtering Wine / Water - Solid in Liquid

CaseRuling

Clear wine / water with minimal debris

Permitted to filter (Mechaber SA 319:10) - not viewed as a taaroves

Wine/water where person is an istenis (extremely careful)

Biur Halacha: Forbidden even then (Pri Megadim)

Small pieces of food in soup

Considered mixed with soup - Issur Borrer applies

Large chunks in soup (e.g. matzo balls)

Not considered mixed - Issur Borrer does not apply

Small pieces in large amount of gravy

Considered mixed - Issur applies

Large piece of chicken in small amount of gravy

Not considered mixed - Issur does not apply

p. 118Borrer — Selecting

4. Definition of Mixture - When Pieces Are Recognizable

Tray of Two Types of Fish - Recognizable Pieces

QuestionRuling

Is a tray of two types of fish considered a taaroves?

Terumas HaDeshen: Yes - all laws of Borrer apply, even when each piece is recognizable on its own

What if pieces are not touching each other?

Machlokes: Some say no taaroves unless touching; Rav Karelitz and Rav Berkovits: depends on whether people would consider it a mixture - no fixed definition

Moving Items Out of the Way (to Reach Something Beneath)

AuthorityRuling

Mishnah Berurah (Biur Halacha)

At worst Assur miderabanan only (she'ein sricha l'gufa) - one's goal is not to clean the taaroves. In some cases (Terumas HaDeshen type) may be fully lenient.

Orchos Shabbos

Lenient only when items are layered (oranges on top of apples) - but if truly mixed together, cannot move items out of the way

Rav Auerbach / Rav Ribiat

Lenient even when mixed together - permitted to move clothes out of the way in a laundry basket

All agree

Permitted to simply move items within the taaroves without removing them from it - this is not a Maaseh Borrer

p. 119Borrer — Selecting

Removing Good with the Bad ("Taking a Fly from the Wine")

AuthorityPositionScope

Taz / Mishnah Berurah

Permitted to remove pesoles if one takes some of the good along with it

General rule - e.g., take some wine with the fly; take some fish flesh with the bone

Chazon Ish

Generally forbidden to remove good with bad - the fly case is a unique exception because wine is literally between the fly's limbs. In most cases, no such heter.

Strict in most solid-in-liquid cases

Bottom Line:

Halacha follows the Taz and Mishnah Berurah.

Permitted: Remove a fly from wine if you take some wine with it. Remove bones if you take some flesh. Cut off a bad part of a fruit taking some good part with it.

p. 120Borrer — Selecting

5. Taking the Good from the Bad - and Bad from the Good

Ochel Mitoch Pesoles vs. Pesoles Mitoch Ochel

AuthorityPosition on Pesoles from OchelPosition on Ochel from Pesoles

Rambam / Rach / Mechaber (SA 319:4)

Always Assur - even by hand, even for immediate use

Permitted if other conditions met

Tosefos

One must take whatever is greater in quantity (may be pesoles if it is the majority)

Permitted if other conditions met

Tur

Must remove whichever requires least effort (tircha)

Permitted if other conditions met

Rama (SA 319:4)

Follows Rambam - explicitly rejects Tur

Permitted if other conditions met

Mishnah Berurah

Follows Rambam - rejects Tosefos as well

Permitted if other conditions met

Bottom Line:

Halacha: It is ALWAYS forbidden to remove pesoles from food - even by hand, even to eat the food immediately. There is no heter based on quantity or on effort (tircha). Only ochel from pesoles is permitted.

Exceptions - When Removing Pesoles Is Permitted

(a) When There Is No Other Way to Reach the Food

CaseRuling

Peeling fruit (orange, banana, apple, carrot, onion)

Permitted if eating immediately - removing peel is the only way to reach the food; treated as removing ochel from pesoles (Biur Halacha)

Peeling for later

Forbidden - Magen Avraham: applies even to edible peels (apple); halacha follows Magen Avraham

Removing seeds from melon (blocking flesh)

Permitted if eating immediately; ideally put seeds in mouth with melon and spit out. If impossible, shaking is preferable to hand removal.

Food wrappers (hotdog, candy, chocolate)

Rav Feinstein: treats as peel - permitted only if eating immediately. Other Poskim: wrappers are not a taaroves with the food and no Issur Borrer applies.

p. 121Borrer — Selecting

(b) Removing Bones from Fish or Chicken

ScenarioRuling

Adult eating fish - can remove fish from bones

Must remove fish from the bone (ochel from pesoles), or remove bone in mouth. Forbidden to remove bone from fish.

Adult: bone impossible to feel in mouth

Rav Feinstein: permitted to remove bone since there is no other way

Preparing for children or elderly

Permitted to remove bones - no other way for them to eat the food safely

General rule

Bone fish before Shabbos wherever possible

p. 122Borrer — Selecting

6. The Heter of Miyad - Selecting 'Immediately'

Definition of Miyad - Rishonim and Poskim

AuthorityDefinition of 'Immediately'

Ra'avan

Literally immediately before eating - the strictest opinion

Rabbeinu Chananel (Rach)

During the course of the meal; extended by Acharonim to immediately before the meal

Rabbeinu Yerucham

Any time before the upcoming meal

Rambam (for two types of food, neither pesoles)

A few hours before the meal is permitted; only forbidden if clearly for a later meal

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Includes the preparation time for the meal (if preparation takes one hour, may select anytime in that hour)

Rama / Mishnah Berurah (operative halacha)

Immediately before the meal; includes the full preparation time needed for that meal

Practical Rules for the Preparation Period

ScenarioRuling

Preparation takes 2 hours - performing borrer within that window

Permitted, even if some preparation finishes early and a gap exists before the meal

Small, inevitable interruptions during preparation (tending to children, etc.)

Permitted - does not invalidate the miyad status

Deliberately leaving time before the meal to do borrer as a separate act

Forbidden - must be an integrated part of meal preparation

Selecting more food than will definitely be eaten

Permitted - may prepare as much as one deems presentable; even if some is not eaten, the borrer is not retroactively forbidden

Deliberately preparing extra food for a future meal

Forbidden

p. 123Borrer — Selecting

Rambam's Distinction - Genuine Pesoles vs. Two Types of Food

Type of BorrerMiyad Requirement

Ochel from genuine pesoles

Must be immediately before eating (strict definition)

Separating two types of food (neither is genuine pesoles)

Rambam: permitted even a few hours before next meal. Biur Halacha: must be strict - only immediately before. Rav Elyashiv: lenient based on combination of factors.

Miyad Mamesh - Removing Pesoles at the Very Moment of Eating

AuthorityRuling

Rosh

Forbidden to remove pesoles by hand at moment of eating; only the 'tissue at the mouth' heter exists (keeping something out, not removing it)

Ramban

Lenient - miyad mamesh is permitted (Biur Halacha's reading; disputed by Chazon Ish)

Birchei Yosef / Mishnah Berurah

Strict - forbidden to remove pesoles even at the moment of eating

p. 124Borrer — Selecting

Bottom Line:

Halacha: One may not remove pesoles by hand immediately before placing food in the mouth. One may, however, use a tissue or cloth held at the lips to prevent unwanted material from entering (not a Maaseh Borrer - it is exclusion, not selection).

Cutlery Separation - Laying the Shabbos Table

AuthorityRuling

Mishnah Berurah

Must plan to begin the meal immediately after separating cutlery

Rav Elyashiv

Permits separating cutlery a few hours before the next meal (combination of Tosefos + Rambam's leniency for two types)

Rav Auerbach

Permitted if the table setting genuinely enhances Kavod Shabbos (not merely for convenience)

All agree

Taking one piece of cutlery to wash it = immediate use. Once washed, may place it anywhere.

Defrosting / Heating Food

Some Poskim permit removing food from a taaroves to defrost or heat it, treating defrosting as part of the preparation process for the meal.

CaseRuling

Taking dry cooked food out of gravy to place on hotplate (for immediate serving)

Permitted - defrosting/heating is part of meal preparation

Removing challos from freezer (mixed with other food) to defrost for the meal

Permitted for the time needed to defrost - forbidden to remove them earlier (e.g., Friday night for the next day)

p. 125Borrer — Selecting

7. Borrer B'Kli - Utensils and Washing Fruit

Status of Cutlery (Fork / Spoon)

AuthorityPosition

Rav Moshe Feinstein

If the fork/spoon is MORE EFFECTIVE at separating the food (not just more convenient), it is Assur miderabanan - even for good from bad, even for immediate use. If used for cleanliness or manners - permitted.

Rav Elyashiv / Rav Ovadia Yosef

Always permitted to use fork or spoon - using cutlery is inherently derech achila and is not a Maaseh Borrer

Keilim Hameyuchadim L'Borrer - Specialized Selecting Utensils

UtensilStatusRuling

Sieve / strainer

Kli meyuchad l'borrer

Assur midoraisa - forbidden on Shabbos

Slotted spoon (used to drain gravy from food)

Kli meyuchad l'borrer

Assur midoraisa, even if not intending to separate - it is a Psik Reisha

Vegetable peeler

Machlokes: Rav Ovadia lenient; majority of Poskim strict

Forbidden l'chatchila. Regular knife permitted (derech achila) for immediate use.

Regular knife (peeling fruit)

Not kli meyuchad

Permitted for immediate use - this is derech achila

Salt shaker with rice (to prevent clumping)

Machlokes

Rav Elyashiv / Rav Karelitz / Rav Yitzchak Yosef: Permitted. Rav Feinstein / Rav Auerbach / Rav Kotler: Forbidden (kli somewhat effective at borrer).

p. 126Borrer — Selecting

Note: Keilim hameyuchadim l'borrer are Muktzah - may not be moved except for a permitted purpose or if in the way.

Washing Dirty Fruit / Produce

CaseRuling

Rinsing fruit under a stream of water (intent: eat immediately)

Rav Feinstein / Rav Auerbach / Rav Elyashiv: Permitted. Chazon Ish / Rav Wosner: Forbidden even then.

Rinsing fruit for later

Forbidden according to all - must eat immediately

Soaking dirty food in a vessel

Rav Feinstein: Forbidden even for immediate use (soaking = Maaseh Borrer)

Washing a dirty bunch of grapes

Forbidden (rinsing or soaking) - dirt is genuinely in a taaroves with the grapes

Washing fruit to remove chemicals (fruit is essentially clean)

Permitted - the fruit is perfectly edible without washing; no taaroves

Rav Elyashiv's practical recommendation

Wash all fruit before Shabbos to avoid the question entirely

Bottom Line:

Practical halacha on washing fruit: follow Rav Feinstein / Rav Auerbach - rinse under a stream is permitted if eating immediately.

Avoid soaking in a vessel. Wash produce before Shabbos wherever possible.

p. 127Borrer — Selecting

Washing Potatoes / Karshinin

CaseRuling

Soaking karshinin (animal food) in water to remove pesoles

Assur midoraisa (Mechaber 319:8 / Biur Halacha)

Putting water on potatoes to remove dirt (MB)

Forbidden

Scrubbing karshinin by hand to remove dirt

Forbidden - equivalent to Borrer

Placing karshinin in a sieve (pesoles falls through)

Permitted - this is Zoreh, not Borrer by hand

8. Master Practical Summary - Shabbos Table Scenarios

Taking good pieces of fish from a tray of mixed pieces (two types)

PERMITTED if b'yad, miyad, ochel mitoch pesoles

If not eating immediately: Assur

Removing bones from fish (by adult)

FORBIDDEN as a rule

Exception: bone is impossible to feel in mouth. Otherwise: remove fish from bone, or remove bone in mouth.

PERMITTED

p. 128–130Tochein — Grinding

Hilchos Tochein

1. The Definition and Scope of Tochein

Tochein (grinding/cutting) is the Melacha of reducing an object to small particles. In the Mishkan, herbs were ground into powder for dyes. The principle: reducing an object to small, usable particles.

SA 321:12: One who cuts vegetables very small is chayav for Tochein. Rama: forbidden to cut dried figs or carob for elderly people; all this applies to one who cuts and leaves it - but cutting immediately before eating is permitted, like the heter of miyad in Borrer.

p. 131Tochein — Grinding

What Types of Food are Subject to Tochein?

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rambam (Chapter 7, Halacha 5)

Chayav for Tochein only when cutting vegetables in order to cook them afterwards

Implies: cutting without intent to cook = no chiyuv

Ramach

Chayav only when (a) cutting in order to cook AND (b) the vegetable is inedible raw

Parallel to his view on bishul

Tosefos (Shabbos 74b)

Chiyuv only for foods that are normally cut very small (beets as prototype)

Later contradiction in Tosefos resolved: "beets" = category of normally-cut foods

Rosh

No chiyuv Tochein applies to cutting food at all

Had a different girsa in the Gemara

Sefer Yeraim

Assur midoraisa to cut any fruit or vegetable very small - no restriction on intent or food type

Does not specify a minimum size

Mechaber (SA 321:12)

Rules like Sefer Yeraim - assur midoraisa to cut any fruit or vegetable very small

Accepted halacha

Magen Avraham

Simple reading: only assur to cut food for someone who cannot eat it unless it is cut small

Biur Halacha disputes this; Chazon Ish reinterprets MA differently

Biur Halacha

Disputes MA - Tochein is forbidden for everyone, even those who could eat the food uncut

Halacha follows Biur Halacha

How Small Must Food be Cut?

No precise measurement is given by the Rishonim. As a practical guide, Rav Berkovits suggests: cutting a tomato into 8 pieces is clearly permitted; more than 8 may enter the prohibition of Tochein. Err on the side of larger cuts when not eating immediately.

Slicing into Thin Strips - Is it Tochein?

AuthorityPosition

Rav Yosef Shalom Elyashiv

STRICT - forbids slicing carrots/cucumbers into thin slices (comparable to Tochein)

Rav Moshe Feinstein

LENIENT - cutting food into slices is not a significant enough improvement to be Tochein

Rav Berkovits

Follows Rav Feinstein - permitted

p. 132Tochein — Grinding

Practical Rule: Halacha follows Sefer Yeraim and Biur Halacha. Do not cut any fruit or vegetable very small unless eating immediately (see Section 2). No precise shiur, but cut into larger pieces when in doubt. Thin slicing: permitted per Rav Berkovits/Rav Moshe.

p. 133Tochein — Grinding

2. The Heter of Miyad - Cutting Immediately Before Eating

Just as Borrer is permitted for immediate use (miyad), so too Tochein may be permitted when done immediately before eating. The rationale: cutting immediately before eating is considered derech achila - part of the act of eating, not a Melacha.

The Core Machlokes

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rashba

Totally permitted to cut food very small for immediate eating - derech achila, not Melacha

Fundamental heter

Shiltei Gibburim

No heter of miyad for Tochein - always forbidden to cut very small

Minority view

Beis Yosef

Essentially agrees with Rashba, but rules one should cut slightly larger than normal even for immediate use

Chumra l'chatchila

Rama (SA 321:12)

Rules like Rashba - miyad is permitted without the Beis Yosef's chumra

Ashkenaz standard

Mishnah Berurah

Many Acharonim follow Beis Yosef; ideally cut slightly larger than normal

L'chatchila follow MB

Rav Berkovits

B'shaas hadechak (time of need): rely on Rashba/Rama and cut as small as on a weekday

p. 134Tochein — Grinding

Definition of "immediately": the preparation period immediately before a meal is included, as long as eating will follow without interruption for other activities.

Grinding vs. Cutting - Does Miyad Apply to Grinding?

AuthorityPosition

Most Poskim

Miyad applies to grinding as well as cutting - derech achila covers both

Chazon Ish

Miyad does NOT apply to grinding/crushing - crushing is a significant change to the food's nature, like Mishkan Tochein. Forbidden even for immediate use.

Halacha

Does not follow Chazon Ish. But ideally: grind in an unusual manner (shinui) when possible.

p. 135Tochein — Grinding

Cutting for Someone Who Cannot Eat the Food Uncut

AuthorityPosition

Most Poskim / Rav Feinstein

Permitted to cut food for someone who cannot eat it uncut (e.g., a child or elderly person), as long as intent is for immediate eating

Chazon Ish

FORBIDDEN - such a person is categorically like the "zekeinim" case; miyad heter does not apply when the person could not eat the food at all without cutting. Must use a shinui.

Rav Feinstein & Rav Auerbach

Halacha does not follow Chazon Ish. However, ideally be strict for CI if not difficult. Use a shinui when convenient.

p. 136Tochein — Grinding

Mashing Bananas or Avocados - Is This Tochein?

AuthorityPositionPractical Application

Rav Moshe Feinstein

No Tochein - banana/avocado do not break into tiny particles; mashing is not comparable to Mishkan grinding

Halacha follows this

Chazon Ish

Tochein applies - mashing creates a fundamentally changed food form, like grinding dates/figs in the Tosefta

Stricter position

Rav Ben-Tsion Abba Shaul / Rav Ovadia Yosef

Permitted to mash with a fork in the regular fashion

Sefardic practice

Rav Feinstein (practical)

Although permitted m'ikar hadin, ideally be strict for Chazon Ish: mash with a spoon or knife handle as shinui

L'chatchila standard for Ashkenaz

Practical Summary: Cutting immediately before eating = permitted (follow Rashba/Rama). Ideally cut slightly larger than normal (MB). Grinding: permitted but use shinui if possible. Mashing banana/avocado: permitted; ideally use spoon or knife handle as shinui.

p. 137Tochein — Grinding

3. Tochein b'Gidulei Karka - Does Tochein Apply to Meat, Cheese, and Non-Plant Foods?

SA 321:9: Permitted to cut cooked or roasted meat very small with a knife. SA 321:10: Forbidden to grate cheese with a grater.

Is There Tochein for Non-Gidulei Karka Foods?

p. 138Tochein — Grinding
AuthorityPosition on Meat/CheeseNotes

Terumas HaDeshen

NO Tochein for non-gidulei karka foods. Meat and cheese are not gidulei karka. Permitted to cut cooked meat.

Mechaber (Sif 9) follows this for cooked meat

Shiltei Gibburim

Meat and cheese ARE gidulei karka - animals are nourished by plants, so they are indirectly gidulei karka. Tochein applies.

Tosefos (Shabbos 73b)

Definition of gidulei karka varies by context. Does not resolve status of meat for Tochein specifically.

Gra (as explained by Damesek Eliezer)

Tochein with a kli meyuchad lecach applies to any food - gidulei karka or not - when it is the normal way (derech) to cut that food small. Cheese is normally grated, so the grater = Tochein.

Key principle

The Mechaber's Two Rulings - Apparent Contradiction

Sif 9: Permits cutting cooked meat (follows Terumas HaDeshen - meat is not gidulei karka). Sif 10: Forbids grating cheese with a grater. If cheese is also not gidulei karka, why is grating forbidden?

ExplanationAuthority

Mechaber's reason for forbidding cheese grater is Uvdin d'chol, not Tochein (since cheese is also not gidulei karka per SA Sif 9)

Magen Avraham / Tosefes Shabbos

Mechaber combines: (a) Uvdin d'chol + (b) Shiltei Gibburim's view that meat/cheese are gidulei karka = Tochein with kli meyuchad. On Yom Tov: no Tochein issur, so only Uvdin d'chol remains - insufficient alone to forbid.

Tosefes Shabbos / Machsis HaShekel

Gra's view: the grater = Tochein because grating is the normal derech for cheese - regardless of gidulei karka. Permitted to cut cheese with a knife.

Gra / Damesek Eliezer

p. 139Tochein — Grinding

Kli Hameyuchad Lecach - Specialized Cutting Utensils

A kli hameyuchad lecach is a utensil whose specific purpose is to cut or grind food (e.g., grater, food processor, mortar and pestle).

RuleDetails

Forbidden to use kli meyuchad lecach even for immediate use

Rivash: miyad heter does not apply when using such a utensil. Parallel to Borrer: kli meyuchad = doraisa even for miyad.

Regular knife = permitted even for cutting very small (for miyad)

Biur Halacha: knife is derech achila - part of eating. Not comparable to a kli meyuchad.

Grater = kli meyuchad lecach

Forbidden to use on Shabbos

Egg slicer / egg cutter

Rav Shlomo-Zalman Auerbach: NOT a kli meyuchad lecach - merely a series of blades for slicing. Permitted to use even on tomatoes.

Cutting Raw Meat for Animals

Rama (321:9): Forbidden to cut raw meat very small for birds - since they cannot eat it uncut, cutting it constitutes Tochein (making it into food for the first time). Note: even though meat is not gidulei karka, the exemption only applies to edible food; raw meat cut for animals is not yet edible.

Practical Summary: Cooked meat - may cut with a knife (no Tochein). Cheese - do not grate with grater (Tochein / Uvdin d'chol). Any kli meyuchad lecach is forbidden even for miyad. Egg slicer: permitted. Raw meat for animals: forbidden.

p. 140Tochein — Grinding

4. Tochein Achar Tochein - Re-Grinding Previously Ground Food

Parallel to Ein bishul achar bishul (no recooking of cooked food), the Rishonim debate whether once something has been ground, it may be ground again on Shabbos.

The Core Machlokes

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rabbeinu Shmuel (cited in Smag)

Ein tochein achar tochein - once something is already ground, no issur to grind it again. Crumbling bread = permitted.

Rama follows this

Rashba

There IS tochein achar tochein - crumbling bread only permitted for miyad (immediate use). Forbidden to crumble for later.

Rambam (per Mishneh LeMelech)

Holds tochein achar tochein = forbidden. Crumbling bread into flour is forbidden by all - too similar to original Melacha.

Rama (321:12)

Rules like Rabbeinu Shmuel. Crumbling bread = permitted even not for miyad.

Halacha follows this

Chayei Adam

Do not rely on heter of Ein tochein achar tochein. Only crumble bread for miyad.

More stringent position

Mishnah Berurah

Rules like Rama (Ein tochein achar tochein)

Halacha l'maaseh

p. 141Tochein — Grinding

Practical application: crushing medication tablets on Shabbos (where halachically permitted to consume) - the substances were already ground before, so Ein tochein achar tochein applies.

Exceptions - When Tochein Achar Tochein Applies Despite the Heter

Contradiction: SA 302:7 forbids scraping dry cement from clothing because crumbling = Tochein. But cement was already ground when made - should be Ein tochein achar tochein?

AuthorityExplanation of ExceptionApplication

Chazon Ish

Ein tochein achar tochein only applies when the substance was rejoined by human action (e.g., baking bread from flour). If rejoined by nature (e.g., cement hardening), the original grinding is nullified - Tochein achar tochein applies.

Bread: permitted. Cement: forbidden.

Shevisas HaShabbos

Ein tochein achar tochein only when the original grinding was NOT nullified. Making bread does not nullify the flour's ground state. But cement's hardening completely nullifies the original grinding.

Same practical result

Biur Halacha

Using a kli meyuchad lecach = forbidden even for Ein tochein achar tochein material

E.g., no running already-ground food through a food processor

p. 142Tochein — Grinding

Practical Rule: Crumbling bread = permitted (Rama/MB). Grinding bread into flour = forbidden by all. Crumbling dry cement = forbidden. Mashing already-cooked and softened food = forbidden unless thoroughly mashed before Shabbos (Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits).

p. 143Tochein — Grinding

5. Tochein b'Shinui - Grinding in an Unusual Fashion

SA 321:7: Permitted to crush pepper with the handle of a knife and a bowl. Normally, crushing with a shinui is assur miderabanan - why is this shinui totally permitted?

The Concept of Shinui Gamur

AuthorityPosition

Sheiltos / Rabbeinu Tam

Gemara (Shabbos 141a) refers to Yom Tov only - on Shabbos, even crushing with a shinui is forbidden

Ri / Rosh

Gemara refers to Shabbos. Crushing pepper with a knife handle = totally permitted on Shabbos because it is a "Shinui gamur" - a complete/total unusual method

Shibollei HaLeket

A Shinui gamur is a method so unusual and inefficient that it is categorically different from a normal shinui. It is totally permitted (not even miderabanan). Same principle underlies why Borer by hand is permitted.

Halacha (Gra, Mishnah Berurah)

Ruling like Ri/Rosh: permitted to crush with knife handle - this is a Shinui gamur. Use of mortar = Uvdin d'chol (Taz).

p. 144Tochein — Grinding

What Qualifies as a Shinui Gamur?

ExampleStatus

Crushing with the handle of a knife

PERMITTED - established as Shinui gamur in Gemara/SA

Mashing a banana with a spoon

PERMITTED as shinui (Rav Moshe)

Mashing with a fork (normal use)

Rav Ben-Tsion / Rav Ovadia: permitted. Stricter position: use spoon/handle instead.

Using a potato masher

FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol (and possibly Tochein)

Any other unusual method

Cannot assume it qualifies as Shinui gamur without a specific ruling from a qualified Rav

p. 145Tochein — Grinding

Tochein of a Previously Cooked Vegetable

ScenarioHalacha

Mashing a potato that was cooked before Shabbos (now soft)

FORBIDDEN - Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits: cooking softens but does not constitute Tochein; mashing is still a new act of Tochein. Must be thoroughly mashed before Shabbos.

Mashing an over-ripe, very soft banana

FORBIDDEN - Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits: natural softening does not exempt from Tochein

Food that was thoroughly mashed before Shabbos

PERMITTED - Ein tochein achar tochein applies (human processing + not nullified)

Practical Rule: Crush with knife handle = permitted (Shinui gamur). Spoon for mashing = permitted shinui. Potato masher = forbidden (Uvdin d'chol). Do not mash cooked potatoes unless already mashed before Shabbos. Cannot rely on a new shinui method without rabbinic ruling.

p. 146Tochein — Grinding

6. Uvdin d'Chol - Weekday-like Activities

Uvdin d'chol is a Rabbinic prohibition against activities that, while not technically a Melacha, resemble weekday labor or are incompatible with the spirit of Shabbos rest.

Source and Status of the Issur

AuthorityPositionNotes

Ramban (Vayikra 23:24)

There is a positive Torah mitzvah (based on "Shabbaton") to rest from non-Melacha activities as well. Chazal defined which activities are included. Possibly only an asmachta (Rabbinical with Torah support).

Foundational source

Ritva

Confirms: basis of resting from non-Melacha activities is from the Torah per Ramban

Rambam / Maggid Mishneh

Either Torah commanded us to refrain and Chazal determined specifics, or it is entirely Rabbinical with "tishbos" as an asmachta

Dispute within the Rambam's position

Chasam Sofer

One who opens his store on Shabbos (even without doing Melacha) is called a Shabbos desecrator - confirms the issur has real force

p. 147Tochein — Grinding

Definition of Uvdin d'Chol

DefinitionAuthority

1. The action resembles one of the 39 forbidden Melachos 2. The action could lead to performing a Melacha 3. The action involves excessive exertion

Tiferes Yisrael (Kalkeles HaShabbos)

An action performed in a way similar to how one goes about weekday work - e.g., gathering fruit from a courtyard into a basket (field-like activity). Simple home food preparation is NOT Uvdin d'chol.

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Using utensils that store owners use to cut/process food = Uvdin d'chol. Regular household utensils (egg cutter, home knife) = NOT Uvdin d'chol.

Rav Shlomo-Zalman Auerbach

Two types: (a) could lead to Melacha - forbidden even for mitzva/great need; (b) involves excessive exertion only - permitted for great need or mitzva

Rav Pesach Eliyahu Falk

p. 148Tochein — Grinding

Practical Examples

ActivityStatus

Gathering fruit from courtyard into a large basket

FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol (resembles field work)

Putting fruit into a small vessel

PERMITTED - not how field work is done

Using a cheese grater

FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol (and possibly Tochein per some opinions)

Using an egg slicer/cutter

PERMITTED (Rav Auerbach) - household utensil, not commercial equipment

Using a potato masher

FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol

Chess set on Shabbos

Minhag to use a designated Shabbos set (Rav Dovid Ribiat)

Hairbrush on Shabbos

May gently brush with soft-bristle brush. Minhag: use a designated Shabbos brush (regular brush may be Uvdin d'chol / concerns of Gozez).

Grater / food processor

FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol and/or kli meyuchad lecach

Uvdin d'chol = Rabbinical prohibition based on "Shabbaton." Activities that resemble weekday labor, could lead to Melacha, or involve excessive exertion are forbidden. Commercial-grade or specialized processing utensils = Uvdin d'chol. Simple home utensils used for direct food preparation = generally permitted.

p. 149Tochein — Grinding
