Substances already ground

p. 150–151Dosh — Threshing

Hilchos Dosh

1. The Definition of Dosh

The Melacha of Dosh (threshing) means to extract a substance from that which encases it. In the Mishkan, herbs were extracted from their casing for dyeing, and grain was extracted from its casing for bread-making.

Core Definition

AuthorityPositionKey Point

Rashi (Shabbos 73b)

Dosh = "mefarek" - unloading the inner substance from its casing, like unloading a donkey

The casing must be unusable/inedible; if usable, it is not Dosh

Tosefos (Shabbos 73b)

Dosh = removing the date from its outer peel

Same principle - inner extracted from outer

Mishnah Berurah (Sh"Ts 319:15)

Distinction: Dosh = dislodging inner matter from outer casing (even if some outer remains mixed in). Borrer = separating components in an already-mixed mixture

Both Dosh and Borrer can occur simultaneously when inner is fully separated from outer

p. 152Dosh — Threshing

Mollel Melilos - Rubbing Ears of Grain

Machlokes Rishonim whether it is permitted to rub ears of grain (mollel melilos) with a shinui on Shabbos:

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rif, Rambam, Ramban

Permitted with shinui (e.g., fingertips) on Shabbos

Mechaber follows this

Baal HaMeor, Ran, Mordechai

Forbidden - either assur miderabanan or issur applies even with shinui

Rama is strict

Halacha l'maaseh (Rama)

One should not remove walnuts from green peels - equivalent to removing kernel from stalk, since one can eat walnut with peel

Stringent position accepted by Ashkenazim

Rubbing with One's Hand vs. Utensil

AuthorityStatus of Rubbing Grain by Hand

Rashi

Assur miderabanan only (not doraisa)

Rabbeinu Chananel (Rach)

Assur midoraisa - rubbing by hand is the Melacha itself

Mishnah Berurah (Sh"Ts 319:11)

Confirms: according to Rach, by hand = doraisa

p. 153Dosh — Threshing

Practical Rule: Do not rub ears of grain or similar actions on Shabbos. Regarding removing outer peels - see Section 2.

2. Dosh and Peeling Food

Not all peeling constitutes Dosh. The key question is whether the outer layer is considered a distinct, inedible casing. Several heterim apply.

The Core Distinction: Production Process vs. Home Peeling

ScenarioHalacha

Peeling fruit normally peeled at home before eating (oranges, bananas)

No issur Dosh - this is part of the eating process, not production (Rav Moshe Feinstein, Igros Moshe OC 125)

Peeling done as part of factory/production process (before reaching stores)

Assur - considered Dosh even if done immediately before eating

Peeling done at home when buying the item with peel attached

Permitted (e.g., cracking hard shell of walnut)

Removing outer peel of walnut (green outer layer, removed in production)

FORBIDDEN - this is factory-stage processing (Rav Moshe; Rama)

p. 154Dosh — Threshing

Heterim for Peeling (Why Some Peeling is Not Dosh)

RationaleDetails

Bitul - outer layer is batul to the food

Magen Avraham / R. Akiva Eiger: peels very closely attached to food are batul and viewed as part of the food. Applies to inner garlic/onion peel.

Outer layer is edible

Dosh only applies when outer layer is inedible/unusable. If edible, removing it = removing one food layer from another (Magen Avraham)

Home-use item

Rav Moshe: if peel is left on until home use (not removed in factory), peeling = part of eating, not Dosh

Specific Cases

ItemHalachaReason

Orange, banana, apple

PERMITTED - no issur Dosh

Peeling is home-stage; not factory-stage production

Garlic / onion (inner peel)

PERMITTED (Rama 321:19)

Batul to the food (R. Akiva Eiger / Magen Avraham)

Outer peel of garlic

Pri Megadim: uncertain - less closely attached, so may not be batul

Be strict l'chatchila

Walnut - hard inner shell

PERMITTED (Rav Moshe)

Sold in stores with shell attached = home-stage

Walnut - green outer peel

FORBIDDEN (Rav Moshe; Rama)

Removed in production, before reaching stores

Peanuts - outer shell

Most Poskim: PERMITTED. Rav Wosner: FORBIDDEN (outer shell)

Follow majority lenient opinion l'maaseh

Peas (inedible pod)

Dosh midoraisa. If intent is for later: also Borrer midoraisa

Classic example of Dosh - inedible outer, edible inner

p. 155Dosh — Threshing

Important: Borrer Issue Always Applies

Even when there is no issur Dosh in peeling, the issur of Borrer (separating) applies if one intends to eat the food later rather than immediately. Always peel immediately before eating.

p. 156Dosh — Threshing

3. Dosh b'Gidulei Karka - Does Dosh Apply to Non-Plant Materials?

The Gemara (Shabbos 75a) records a machlokes Tanaim whether Dosh applies only to plants or also to animals and other substances.

The Basic Machlokes

OpinionPosition

Chachamim

Ein dosh ela b'gidulei karka - Dosh doraisa applies only to plants. Dosh on non-plants is assur miderabanan.

Rabbi Yehuda

Dosh applies even to substances that are not gidulei karka

Halacha

Follows Chachamim

Milking a Cow - The Classic Case

The Braissa (Shabbos 95a) states milking a cow is forbidden on Shabbos as "mefarek," a tolda of Dosh. But a cow is not a plant - how?

AuthorityPositionExplanation

Tosefos

Milking a cow = doraisa only per Rabbi Yehuda; per Chachamim only miderabanan

Proof from Gemara that milking with shinui is needed for pain-relief - implies without shinui = doraisa

Rambam

Milking a cow = assur doraisa

Seemingly contradicts Ein dosh ela b'gidulei karka

Maggid Mishneh

Rambam: cow is considered gidulei karka because it is nourished by plants. Fish are not (not nourished by plants).

Fish: only miderabanan per Rambam

Rav Avraham b. Rambam

Ein dosh ela b'gidulei karka applies only to the Av Melacha. Mefarek (the tolda) applies even to non-gidulei karka - so milking = doraisa regardless

Rashba / Rach

Milking = doraisa (cow is gidulei karka). Rav Hai Gaon: only miderabanan.

p. 157–158Dosh — Threshing

The Eglei Tal's Rules

RuleApplication

If outer casing is gidulei karka, Dosh applies - even if inner substance is not

E.g., squeezing water out of cotton (for the water) = Dosh doraisa - cotton is gidulei karka

If outer casing is NOT gidulei karka, no Dosh doraisa - even if inner substance is gidulei karka

E.g., squeezing oil out of fish for the oil = not doraisa - fish is not gidulei karka

Dosh applies to materials found within the karka itself, not only things that grow from it

Dosh does NOT apply to something attached to the ground

If it did, every act of kotser would also be Dosh

Practical Rule: It is assur miderabanan to milk a cow on Shabbos (at minimum), and most Poskim hold it is assur midoraisa. L'maaseh it is fully forbidden.

p. 159Dosh — Threshing

4. Sechita b'Peiros - Squeezing Fruit (Part 1)

Squeezing liquid from fruit is a form of Dosh (or a tolda thereof). There are three categories of fruit with different levels of issur.

Three Categories of Fruit

CategoryExamplesHalacha

Commonly squeezed for juice

Olives, grapes

ASSUR MIDORAISA to squeeze

Sometimes squeezed for juice

Strawberries, pomegranates (and nowadays, most fruit)

ASSUR MIDERABANAN to squeeze

Never squeezed for juice

Possibly gooseberries, cucumbers

PERMITTED to squeeze

Note: Nowadays, almost all fruit are sometimes squeezed. Therefore, the miderabanan category applies broadly.

Squeezing for Liquid vs. for the Food

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rashi & Tosefos

Forbidden to squeeze any fruit for the sake of its liquid. Only permitted to squeeze "other fruit" when intent is to improve the taste of the fruit itself.

Taz agrees; stricter position

Rif, Rambam, Rosh

Permitted to squeeze "other fruit" even when one wants the liquid - liquid of such fruit never attains independent importance

Halacha follows this

Mechaber & Rama (320:1)

Rule like Rif. Taz: be strict for Rashi/Tosefos. Biur Halacha: lenient.

Halacha l'maaseh: follow Rif/Mechaber

p. 160Dosh — Threshing

Drinking Liquid that Flowed Out by Itself (Gezeira)

ScenarioHalacha

Juice of olives or grapes that flowed out on Shabbos by itself

FORBIDDEN to drink - even if intent was to eat (not squeeze) the fruit

Juice of "sometimes squeezed" fruit that flowed out

PERMITTED to drink - if person's intent was to eat the fruit, not squeeze it for liquid

Juice of "never squeezed" fruit that flowed out

Always PERMITTED to drink

Practical Summary: Squeezing grapes or olives = assur doraisa. Squeezing most modern fruit = assur miderabanan. Squeezing fruit that is never squeezed for juice (if such exists) = permitted. Always squeeze directly onto food where possible - see Section 5.

p. 161Dosh — Threshing

5. Sechita b'Peiros - Squeezing onto Food, Kevashim, Lemons (Part 2)

Squeezing Directly onto Food

When liquid goes directly onto food (tavshil), it may never become an independent entity. Does this permit squeezing normally-forbidden fruit?

AuthorityPositionApplication

Shmuel (Shabbos 144b)

PERMITTED to squeeze olives/grapes directly onto food - juice goes from one food to another and never becomes an independent liquid

Basic heter

Rif, Rambam, Rosh

Rule like Shmuel - squeezing onto food is permitted

Mechaber follows this

Rach (Rabbeinu Chananel)

FORBIDDEN midoraisa to squeeze olives/grapes onto food - disputes Shmuel's leniency

Rama adds this opinion

Mechaber/Rama (320:4)

Mechaber: follow Rif (permitted). Rama: praiseworthy to be strict per Rach.

L'chatchila: be strict. B'dieved: permitted.

p. 162Dosh — Threshing

Kevashim and Shelakos

Kevashim = pickled foods. Shelakos = foods cooked thoroughly in water and filled with it.

ScenarioRif / RambamRach

Squeezing for the sake of the food

PERMITTED

PERMITTED

Squeezing for the liquid - into empty vessel

ASSUR miderabanan

ASSUR midoraisa

Squeezing for the liquid - onto food

PERMITTED (like olives/grapes onto food)

ASSUR midoraisa - disputes Shmuel's heter entirely

Mechaber (320:7): Brings Rif as ikar, but mentions Rach. Rosh: one who is strict is praiseworthy. Biur Halacha: be strict (midoraisa) for squeezing into empty vessel.

Squeezing Lemons

ScenarioHalacha

Squeezing lemon onto food

PERMITTED (Rosh, Mechaber; Biur Halacha)

Squeezing lemon onto sugar

PERMITTED (Mishnah Berurah); Chazon Ish: FORBIDDEN

Squeezing lemon into empty vessel or liquid

Mishnah Berurah: FORBIDDEN. Mechaber (20th-century context): assur into empty vessel.

Sefardim

Rav Ovadia & Rav Ben-Tsion Abba Shaul: m'ikar hadin permitted in all circumstances; praiseworthy to be strict

Leaving lemon slice in drink

PERMITTED - as long as one does not squeeze it

p. 163Dosh — Threshing

Practical Summary: Squeeze lemon onto food = permitted. Into empty cup or liquid = be strict (forbidden). Leaving a slice in tea = fine as long as not squeezed. Ashkenazim: do not squeeze olives/grapes onto food l'chatchila.

p. 164Dosh — Threshing

6. Squeezing Wet Clothes and Materials

Two separate melachos may apply when squeezing wet clothing: (1) Dosh/Sechita - extracting liquid; (2) Melabein - cleaning/whitening.

The Two Issurim

IssurTrigger

Dosh / Sechita

When one intends to gather and use the liquid that is squeezed out

Melabein (whitening/cleaning)

When the squeezing cleans the material - applies to water always; machlokes for colored liquids

Squeezing Colored Liquid (Wine) out of Clothing

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rambam / Ramban / Kesef Mishneh

Melabein applies even for squeezing out colored liquid from clothing

Strict position

Rashba

Melabein limited to squeezing out water; not colored liquid

Lenient position

Rabbeinu Tam

No Melabein for colored liquid AND no Dosh (since wine goes to waste)

But Ri: still assur miderabanan

Ri (in Tosefos)

Even though wine goes to waste, it is Dosh miderabanan; also Melabein applies = also miderabanan

Mishnah Berurah: be strict

Halacha

Implication of Mishnah Berurah: be strict - Melabein applies to colored liquid going to waste

p. 165Dosh — Threshing

Psik Reisha and Squeezing - The Barrel Sealing Case

SA 320:18: A barrel sealed with a flax stopper - it is inevitable wine will be squeezed as it is inserted/removed (psik reisha).

FactorOpinionApplication

Aruch

Psik reisha d'lo nichah leih = permitted

Basis for leniency (but most Rishonim disagree)

Most Rishonim

Psik reisha d'lo nichah leih = assur miderabanan

Main ruling

Wine goes to waste

Many Rishonim: when wine is discarded, no Dosh even miderabanan

Combined with other leniencies allows some to be lenient

Handle present

Material attached to metal rod = like sponge with handle (see below)

Mechaber: not fully convincing, but used as support

Biur Halacha

Reminds: whole seif concerns Dosh only; those who hold Melabein applies to colored liquid have no basis for leniency

p. 166Dosh — Threshing

Squeezing a Sponge

ScenarioHalacha

Wiping with a wet sponge (no handle)

FORBIDDEN - psik reisha that water will be squeezed out

Sponge with a handle - water NOT inevitable

PERMITTED - holding the handle means squeezing is not certain (Rashi, Rambam)

Sponge with a handle - water IS inevitable

Rashi & Rambam: FORBIDDEN. Raavad: PERMITTED (like pouring from a vessel).

Practical rule (Mechaber/Rama)

Only use sponge with handle where it is not inevitable that water will be squeezed out

Summary - Squeezing Wet Material

Squeezing material soaked in water = assur (Melabein). If also intending to collect the water = also assur doraisa (Dosh). Squeezing material with colored liquid = assur (Melabein per MB); if intending to collect = doraisa. Do not wipe with very wet sponge without a handle.

p. 167Dosh — Threshing

7. Squeezing Hair, Brushes, and Baby Wipes

Squeezing Hair

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rabbah & Rav Yosef

No issur Dosh for squeezing oil from hair - hair does not absorb like cloth; squeezing = like pouring from a vessel

Rambam follows this (Chapter 9, Halacha 11)

Rav Ashi

Dosh may apply to squeezing hair

Kesef Mishneh: Rav Ashi is not disputing; all agree no doraisa; miderabanan applies when intending to use the liquid

Rach

Dosh applies to hair - forbidden

Strict position

Mechaber (330:1)

Assur miderabanan to squeeze hair

Kesef Mishneh: all agree no doraisa

Rav Moshe Feinstein (Igros Moshe OC 1:139)

Permitted to wash hair/beard - no Melabein for body, and no Sechita if intent is not to squeeze out water (only miderabanan, and Chazal only forbade with intent)

p. 168Dosh — Threshing

Toothbrush

PositionRuling

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Should not wet a toothbrush - equates bristles to hair (miderabanan). Also forbidden due to Memachek (smoothing) from toothpaste.

Rav Berkovits

Follows strict position - do not use wet toothbrush

Rav Ben-Tsion Abba Shaul / Rav Ovadia Yosef

Permit wetting toothbrush. All agree toothpaste with regular paste = issur Memachek.

Baby Wipes

PositionRuling

Most Poskim (including Rav Berkovits)

FORBIDDEN - liquid is squeezed out in use and person wants the liquid to do the cleaning (= doraisa, since not "going to waste")

Some Poskim (lenient)

Permit certain wipes where liquid rests on surface and is not absorbed into the wipe itself - no Sechita occurs. Strict position: impossible to verify.

Rav Asher Weiss

Permits using baby wipes on Shabbos

Rav Ovadia Yosef

Permits in a time of need (sha'as hadechak) - if wiping very gently

Practical recommendation

L'chatchila: squeeze out wipes before Shabbos. B'dieved or in need: some lenient opinions exist. Do NOT use to wipe clothing stains (issur Melabein applies - all agree).

p. 169Dosh — Threshing

Practical Rule: Do not squeeze hair intentionally. May wash hair and body normally (no intent to squeeze). Toothbrush: be strict. Baby wipes: squeeze out beforehand or rely on lenient opinions in case of need.

p. 170Dosh — Threshing

8. Melting Ice and Snow

Crushing ice or causing snow/ice to melt is related to the category of Dosh. The Rishonim dispute the reason for the issur and its scope.

Why is Crushing Ice Forbidden?

AuthorityReason for IssurPractical Implication

Rashi

Creating water from ice resembles Melacha (nisht mefurash which one)

Forbidden to crush; permitted to let melt on its own

Rambam & Rashba

Gezeira - lest one come to squeeze fruit

Same issur, different reason

Sefer HaTerumah

Nolad - forbidden to create a "new" state (liquid from solid). Even water that melted on its own may be forbidden b'dieved.

Strictest position

Crushing Ice into a Cup

AuthorityPosition

Rashi

FORBIDDEN to actively crush ice even into a cup of water - only permitted to place whole ice and let it melt

Rambam, Rashba, Ran (per Yerushalmi)

PERMITTED to crush ice into a cup of water

Mechaber (320:9)

Implies like Rashi - does not mention Rambam's heter of crushing into cup

Mishnah Berurah

Brings both opinions. In Shaar Hatsion (318:146): good to be strict.

p. 171Dosh — Threshing

Causing Ice to Melt (Leaving in Warm Place)

ScenarioHalacha

Placing ice in a warm place to melt

Rashi & Rambam: PERMITTED. Sefer HaTerumah: FORBIDDEN. Mechaber: lenient. Rama: strict (for Ashkenazim) unless time of need.

Placing ice in a cup of water (melts into liquid)

PERMITTED - all agree (Mechaber 320:9)

Melting fat onto a food dish

PERMITTED if melts directly into food. FORBIDDEN if forms a visible puddle (Rama 318:16 per Sefer HaTerumah).

Taking ice from freezer to room temperature to melt

Rav Wosner: totally permitted. Orchos Shabbos: permitted if needed for Shabbos.

p. 172Dosh — Threshing

Other Ice/Snow Halachos

ScenarioHalacha

Breaking ice to reach water underneath

PERMITTED - not Soser (destroying)

Washing hands with water mixed with snow/ice

FORBIDDEN - snow will inevitably be crushed. Biur Halacha: be strict.

Walking on snow (snow may melt)

PERMITTED - one does not intend to melt it, and Chazal did not forbid impossible-to-avoid situations

Urinating on snow

Maharam MiRotenburg & Taz: permitted (like walking). Rosh: forbidden. Mishnah Berurah: be strict if easy to do so.

Practical Summary: Do not crush ice. May place ice in drinks or cups of water. May leave ice near warmth to melt (some dispute for Ashkenazim l'chatchila). May walk on snow. Melting fat: only if goes directly onto food without forming a puddle.

p. 173Dosh — Threshing

p. 174–176Melabein — Laundering

Melabein

1. Foundations - The Melacha of Melabein

Melabein (whitening/laundering) in the Mishkan involved cleansing the wool shorn from animals. The core question debated by the Rishonim is whether Melabein is limited to washing with water or extends to other forms of cleaning.

The Core Question: Can There Be Melabein Without Water?

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rashi (Shabbos 141a)

Melabein mid'oraisa requires water - scraping dirt from the outside of clothing is only derabanan

BUT: Rashi also implies (Shabbos 146b) that shaking dust from a Tallis is chayav chataas - an apparent contradiction

Shaar HaTzion (302:41)

Resolves the contradiction: Melabein without water is mid'oraisa only when the dirt is completely removed

If a stain remains after cleaning without water, no issur doraisa. Rubbing a kerchief (already clean) = only derabanan even per Rashi

Rach & Tosefos (Shabbos 177a)

No Melabein without water - period

The shaking case in the Gemara involved dew; the water in the dew causes the cleaning

Mechaber (SA 302:1)

Rules like Rach/Tosefos - no Melabein without water

Lenient position

Rama (SA 302:1)

Cites Rashi - one should be strict

Ashkenazic practice follows Rama

Rav Ovadia Yosef

Sefardim may be lenient and shake dust off clothing even if makpid

Follows Mechaber's ruling

p. 177Melabein — Laundering

Bottom Line: Mechaber rules leniently (no Melabein without water). Rama rules strictly. Ashkenazim follow Rama. Sefardim may follow Mechaber.

2. Cleaning Without Water - Rubbing Clothing

Rubbing Clothing to Soften vs. to Whiten

The Gemara (Shabbos 140a) distinguishes between rubbing clothing to soften it (permitted) and rubbing to whiten it (forbidden). Intent is the determining factor for regular clothing - but for certain items (kerchiefs, linen), intent is presumed to be whitening.

ItemRambam / MechaberRaavad / RambanRama / MB

Regular (non-linen) clothing

Permitted - presumed intent is to soften

Permitted

Permitted unless clearly intending to whiten (MB 302:24)

Kerchief (mitpachas)

Forbidden - presumed intent is to whiten/shine

Permitted if not intending to whiten

Forbidden (Mechaber rules like Rambam)

Linen clothing (not undergarment)

-

-

Forbidden - same status as kerchief (Shibbolei HaLeket, cited by Rama; MB 302:25)

Linen undergarment

-

-

Permitted - nobody sees it, so intent is presumed to be softening, not whitening (MB)

p. 178Melabein — Laundering

Practical Rule: Do not rub a kerchief or any visible linen garment. Rubbing non-linen clothing to soften it is permitted, but forbidden if you clearly intend to whiten it. Linen undergarments may be rubbed.

3. Shaking Dust or Dew from Clothing

The Gemara's Conditions: New, Black, and Makpid

The Gemara forbids shaking a new, black Tallis of dew/dust only when the person is makpid (particular) about not wearing it with that dirt. The Biur Halacha (302, Dh: Aleha) clarifies that 'makpid' is the essential factor; 'new' and 'black' are merely indicators that a person tends to be makpid on such a Tallis.

AuthorityExplanation of Why These Conditions Matter

Rambam (Shabbos 10:16,18)

The issur is not Melabein at all - it is Makeh B'patish (completing an object). Removing leftover production material to make the Tallis wearable constitutes the final act of completing it - forbidden only if makpid

Rashba (cited by Maggid Mishneh)

Follows Rach: the person shakes dew, and cleaning is a side effect. If makpid, we assume he wants the cleaning - forbidden. If not makpid (would wear it as-is), cleaning is eino miskavein - permitted

Biur Halacha (302:2)

New and black are not absolute conditions - they are predictors of makpid. A person who is known to be makpid on an old or white Tallis is also forbidden to shake it

p. 179Melabein — Laundering

Practical Halacha - Shaking Clothing

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Shaking dust from new black Tallis (makpid)

FORBIDDEN mid'oraisa per Rashi; Rama rules strictly

Shaking dust when NOT makpid (would wear it dirty)

PERMITTED - Rashba: cleaning is eino miskavein

Shaking dust on Shabbos (Ashkenazim generally)

FORBIDDEN - since Shabbos requires best dress, person is presumed makpid (Poskim)

Shaking dust from old garment

Biur Halacha: strict; permits only with shinui (back of hand)

Shaking dust from light-colored garment

Treated same as above - strict

Shaking with a brush

FORBIDDEN in all cases (Biur Halacha 302:2)

Removing surface dirt not embedded in fabric

PERMITTED - removing feathers heter (Rama 302:1; MB 302:7)

Asking a non-Jew to shake the dust (kavod habriyos)

PERMITTED - since many Rishonim permit, can rely on them for amira l'akum (MB)

Sefardim - shaking dust (even if makpid)

Rav Ovadia Yosef: PERMITTED per Mechaber

p. 180Melabein — Laundering

4. Cleaning with Water

The Gemara (Zevachim 94a) rules: 'Shriyuso zehu kibuso' - for fabric material, soaking IS laundering. Even placing a small amount of water on fabric without scrubbing constitutes Melabein mid'oraisa. However, several Gemaras appear to contradict this, and the Rishonim offer two main resolutions.

The Two Approaches to Contradictions

ApproachAuthorityThe PrinciplePractical Implication

Approach 1: Only dirty material

Tosefos (1st opinion); Rosh; Ri

Shriyuso zehu kibuso applies only to dirty or stained material. Wetting clean clothing = no Melabein

Drying hands on a towel is permitted (towel is clean). Wiping a spill on already-dirty clothing = forbidden

Approach 2: Derech Lichluch

Rabbeinu Tam (Tosefos 2nd opinion)

Shriyuso zehu kibuso only applies when wetting in the normal way of cleaning. Wetting in a way that dirties (derech lichluch) = permitted even on dirty material

Walking through water, immersing in mikveh = permitted (not derech kibbus). Women wiping hands on children's soiled clothing = permitted per R. Tam; forbidden per Ri

Approach 3: Small amount

Tur; Mordechai

Rejects both above leniencies. Permits only when there is a very small amount of water (e.g., drying hands after washing)

Dry hands before wiping on towel (Mordechai). Basic leniency is narrower than approaches 1 and 2

p. 181Melabein — Laundering

The Halacha - Mechaber and Rama

AuthorityPosition

Mechaber (SA 302:9-10)

Brings both approaches from Tosefos. Cites Mordechai that it is good to shake water off hands first - but does not rule definitively which approach he follows

Rama

Notes that the minhag is to be lenient (not to shake hands first)

Mishnah Berurah (302:48,50)

Basic halacha follows Approach 1 (no Melabein on clean material). BUT must also be strict for Rabbeinu Tam (Approach 2) - therefore even a small amount of water on clean clothing is forbidden

Biur Halacha (302)

In time of need, may combine the leniency of clean material with other factors

Practical Halacha - Wetting Fabric

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Placing water on a stain or dirty mark

FORBIDDEN mid'oraisa - all agree (even if stain not fully removed)

Drying hands on a towel (hands not very wet)

PERMITTED - Mordechai / minhag (Rama); MB follows leniently

Drying hands on a towel (hands very wet)

Tur: forbidden. MB: follows leniently per minhag; Mordechai recommends shaking first

Drying wet glasses/cutlery with a towel

PERMITTED - as long as towel doesn't become very wet (MB 302:58-60)

Drying many items with same towel (towel gets soaked)

FORBIDDEN - inevitable squeezing (MB)

Drying colored liquid (e.g., juice) with a towel

FORBIDDEN - assur miderabanan (Dosh), even though no Melabein for colored liquids (MB)

Using a towel the person doesn't care about wetting

PERMITTED - no concern of squeezing (MB)

Wetting leather

PERMITTED - Shriyuso zehu kibuso does not apply to leather

Scrubbing leather with water

FORBIDDEN (soft leather); permitted per Chachamim for hard leather

p. 182Melabein — Laundering

Key Rule: Placing water on any stain or dirt = forbidden mid'oraisa. Wetting clean fabric = dispute; MB rules strictly. Leather = more lenient (wetting permitted; scrubbing forbidden).

5. Drying Wet Clothes and the Gezeiros Against Squeezing

Drying Wet Clothes with Heat

The Mordechai rules that drying wet clothing by a fire constitutes Melabein (and also Bishul) because it assists the cleaning process. The Biur Halacha (302) extends this to drying in the sun as well.

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Drying wet clothes by fire or any heat source

FORBIDDEN - Melabein (and Bishul) (Mordechai; Biur Halacha 302)

Drying wet clothes in the sun

FORBIDDEN - Biur Halacha rules this is Melabein

Drying slightly moist clothing by fire

FORBIDDEN - even if only slightly moist (SA 301:46; MB 301:168)

Hanging wet clothes to dry on Shabbos (even in private)

FORBIDDEN - looks like clothes were washed on Shabbos (Mishna, Shabbos 146b)

Leaving wet clothes hung that were spread on Erev Shabbos

PERMITTED - may leave them there on Shabbos (SA 301:45)

Wearing wet clothes on Shabbos (already on)

PERMITTED - may continue wearing them (Mishna, Shabbos 146b)

Putting on wet clothes on Shabbos

FORBIDDEN unless no other clothing is available (MB 301:161-2)

Spreading out clothes moist with sweat

FORBIDDEN (Tosefta; SA 301:47)

Spreading out clothes moist with dirt (will remain dirty when dry)

PERMITTED (MB 301:164)

p. 185–187Losh — Kneading

Losh

Definition of Losh

Losh (kneading): Combining tiny particles into a solid or semi-solid mass by means of a liquid. Many Poskim include adding and mixing liquid into a thick sauce or pasty substance. In the Mishkan: ground herbs mixed with water into thick paste.

Key Terms

TermDefinition

Bar Gibul

Two substances that fuse well through kneading. Classic example: flour and water.

Lav Bar Gibul

Two substances that do NOT fuse well. Classic example: ash and water.

Blilah Avah

Thick mixture (e.g., stiff dough, thick paste)

Blilah Racah

Loose mixture (e.g., thin batter, runny consistency)

Shinui Seder

Reversing the normal order in which ingredients are combined

Shinui Gibul

Mixing in an unusual way (e.g., with a finger, criss-cross, small amounts at a time)

p. 188Losh — Kneading

1. Bar Gibul - When Does Losh Begin?

Machlokes Tanaim: At what point does the issur doraisa of losh apply?

TannaPositionNotes

Rebbe

Chayav as soon as liquid is placed into the dry substance - before any stirring

Smag, Sefer HaTerumah rule like Rebbe

Rebbe Yosi Bar Yehuda (halacha)

Not chayav until one actively kneads the combination. Placing liquid = assur miderabanan only.

Rif, Rambam, Rosh, Mechaber rule like RYbY

Mechaber (321:14): Rules like Rebbe Yosi Bar Yehuda but cites Rebbe as 'yesh omrim.' Pri Megadim: Even Rebbe Yosi Bar Yehuda holds that placing water into a bar gibul is assur miderabanan.

p. 189Losh — Kneading

2. Lav Bar Gibul - Is There an Issur Losh?

AuthorityPositionPractical Result

Rambam + Rashi

NO issur losh at all for a lav bar gibul - neither for placing the liquid nor for kneading

Assur only miderabanan (Gezeiros; see below)

Tosefos + Raavad

Everyone (even Rebbe Yosi Bar Yehuda) agrees: ASSUR MIDORAISA to even place liquid into a lav bar gibul

More stringent than a bar gibul in this respect

Mechaber

Rules like Rambam - lav bar gibul is not subject to losh doraisa

Magen Avraham / Mishnah Berurah (halacha l'maaseh)

Rules like Tosefos/Raavad - ASSUR MIDORAISA to form any lav bar gibul

Standard Ashkenazic practice

Yesh Losh Achar Losh: It is assur midoraisa to knead a mixture that has already been kneaded. One cannot 're-knead' a pre-made dough and assume it is permitted (Biur Halacha, based on Yerushalmi).

p. 190Losh — Kneading

3. Rabbinic Gezeiros Even for Lav Bar Gibul (Rambam's System)

Even the Rambam/Mechaber, who hold there is no doraisa for lav bar gibul, forbid the following three cases miderabanan:

SubstanceGezeira ReasonStatus

Roasted flour (kemach kali)

Gezeira: resembles regular flour (bar gibul) - lest one come to knead regular flour

Assur miderabanan (Rambam); Assur midoraisa (Mishnah Berurah - since it IS a bar gibul)

Shasisa (thick animal food)

Resembles losh visually when made into a blilah avah

Assur to make into blilah avah

Mursan (animal food)

Resembles dust; dust is a bar gibul - gezeira lest one come to knead dust

Rambam: assur miderabanan. Mishnah Berurah: assur midoraisa (it IS a bar gibul per Tosefos)

p. 191–192Losh — Kneading

Blilah Avah on Shabbos: L'chatchila, never make a blilah avah on Shabbos. Exception: if making before Shabbos would ruin the food (e.g., radish with vinegar deteriorates), it is permitted with full shinuyim. Similarly permitted for Mitzva purposes (charoses).

Shinui Seder when there is no normal order: Terumas HaDeshen - put food first, liquid second. Taz - no shinui seder heter applies at all. Mishnah Berurah rules leniently like Terumas HaDeshen.

5. What Is and Is Not Losh

ActionStatus

Placing liquid into flour (bar gibul)

Assur midoraisa (Rebbe) or assur miderabanan (Rebbe Yosi Bar Yehuda / halacha). Kneading: assur midoraisa for all.

Placing water into flax seeds (zeronei pishtan) - bind extremely well

ASSUR MIDORAISA - everyone agrees (even before kneading)

Placing water into ash (lav bar gibul)

Assur midoraisa (Mishnah Berurah / Magen Avraham). Permitted midoraisa (Rambam/Mechaber).

Mixing large pieces of vegetables with liquid - do not stick together

MUTAR - not losh (no binding occurs)

Adding liquid to a pre-made mixture to LOOSEN it (not thicken)

MUTAR - opposite effect of losh

Adding liquid to a pre-made mixture to THICKEN it

ASSUR - losh achar losh

Adding flour/powder to a thin batter to thicken it

ASSUR

Mixing liquids into cooked foods (even if paste-like result)

MUTAR - cooked foods are exempt from losh

Dissolving a powder in liquid (result is liquid consistency)

MUTAR - not losh (Chazon Ish: no losh when end result is liquid)

Baby formula: dissolving powder in water

MUTAR - dissolves, does not bind

Compressing dry flour/oatmeal/dirt with no liquid

MUTAR - no liquid medium, no losh

Compressing bread/cake crumbs (absorbed moisture present)

Problematic - absorbed oil/moisture may act as binding agent

Soaking matzah in soup / cookies in milk (items break apart)

MUTAR - substances fall apart, do not bind together

Pouring water onto sand (produces mud)

ASSUR - losh applies to non-foods too

Urinating on mud (psik reisha d'lo nichah leih)

Assur miderabanan. Mishnah Berurah: lenient in time of need on someone else's mud.

Mashing banana in its own juices

Mutar (also a Tochein concern - do l'chatchila with a shinui)

Mixing oil/mayo into mashed avocado

ASSUR - losh

Mixing oil/butter into cooked, mashed potatoes

Mutar m'ikar hadin - cooked food. Some are strict.

Adding mayo/ketchup to ground horseradish (if previously mixed before Shabbos)

MUTAR - adding liquid to pre-made mixture that loosens it; stir with shinui

Adding oil/mayo to finely ground chopped liver + eggs

Problematic - use larger pieces or prepare before Shabbos; if necessary: shinui seder + shinui gibul

Melting medicine tablet in spoon of water for child

MUTAR

Making ketchup with mustard / mayo together (very loose)

MUTAR - blilah racah, may stir normally

Stirring honey with sour cream / sugar into yoghurt

MUTAR - very loose combinations

Jelled desserts (begin loose, invariably thicken)

Some Poskim forbid - mixture thickens after a few minutes

Thick oatmeal / instant potato

ASSUR - like flax seeds; produces thick sticky mass on contact

Children pouring water on sandbox sand

Should be prevented - losh

p. 196–197Me'abed — Tanning

Me'abed

1. Foundations

What Is Me'abed?

Me'abed (tanning) involves preserving and hardening animal hides. It was required in the Mishkan to prepare the hides used as coverings. The melacha consists of applying salt or brine to raw hides, drawing out moisture and causing them to dry and harden.

Does Me'abed Apply to Food? - The Core Machlokes Rishonim

AuthorityPositionNotes

Rach (Rabbeinu Chananel)

No issur of Me'abed with food - totally permitted to salt even heavily

Rules like Rava - Ein ibud b'ochlin

Rambam (Shabbos 22:10)

No issur of Me'abed with food - all food-salt prohibitions stem from bishul

Agrees with Rach on this fundamental point

Rashi & Tosefos (Shabbos 75b)

Issur derabanan of Me'abed applies to food

Rules that heavily salting food resembles tanning

Rava (Shabbos 75b)

Ein ibud b'ochlin - no Me'abed with food at all

Even Rabbah bar Huna agrees: light salting for eating = permitted

Rabbah bar Huna (Shabbos 75b)

Heavily salting meat = Me'abed mid'oraisa

Rav Ashi: he agrees light salting to eat is not Me'abed

p. 198Me'abed — Tanning

Bottom Line: The Rach and Rambam permit salting food freely. Rashi and Tosefos hold there is an issur derabanan. The Mechaber rules like Rashi/Tosefos for most cases (see below).

2. Salt Water - Hilmi

The Issur to Make Salt Water

Chazal forbade making hilmi (a large concentration of salt water) on Shabbos. The Mechaber (SA 321:2) follows Rashi that this resembles the tanning process, where a brine solution was prepared to soak hides.

ScenarioHalacha L'Maaseh

Large amount of salt water

FORBIDDEN - resembles Me'abed (Rashi) / tikunim of bishul (Rambam)

Small amount of salt water (for immediate use)

PERMITTED - small amounts were never made in tanning process

Very strong salt water - 2/3 salt, 1/3 water (even small amount)

FORBIDDEN - resembles muryas (fish pickling brine) per SA 321:2

Adding oil before adding salt to small amount of water

PERMITTED - oil prevents resemblance to Me'abed (MB 321:10-11)

Adding oil after salt water has already been made

FORBIDDEN - oil only helps if added before the salt (MB)

Making salt water for a later meal (small amount)

PERMITTED per Mishnah Berurah; Magen Avraham is strict

Making large salt water to put into a cooked dish

Tosefes Shabbos: permitted; Mishnah Berurah: strict

The Ran's Limitation on Small Amounts

p. 199Me'abed — Tanning
AuthorityPosition

Ran (plain reading)

Permitted to make as much salt water as needed for one meal; forbidden to make more for a later meal

Magen Avraham

Interprets Ran more strictly: forbidden to make any amount of salt water if intent is for a later meal - even if small

Mishnah Berurah (321:10)

Rejects Magen Avraham - permits a small amount of salt water even for a later meal

3. Salting Vegetables - Yerakos

Why Salting Vegetables Is Forbidden

AuthorityReason for Issur

Rashi (Shabbos 108b)

Salt hardens the vegetable - effect similar to Me'abed

Rambam

Resembles pickling vegetables, which is assur miderabanan because it resembles bishul (cooking)

Mechaber (SA 321:3)

Rules like Rambam for vegetables - resembles pickling; rules like Rashi for salt water

Pri Megadim (321:3,5)

Mechaber chose Rambam for vegetables because it is hard to see how a little salt creates the Me'abed effect

How Many Vegetables May Be Salted at Once?

AuthorityPositionNotes

Terumas HaDeshen

Permitted to dip each one individually, leave them briefly, then eat all together

Forbidden only if left in salt after the meal ends

Bach

Permitted to salt two together; forbidden to salt three or more simultaneously

By the time salt reaches piece #3, piece #1 is already sweating

Taz (321:1)

Forbidden to salt even two together; permitted to salt one at a time and leave for short time in meal

Agrees with Terumas HaDeshen's heter for sequential salting

Magen Avraham (321:6)

Forbidden to salt three together; two is permitted; but minhag is one at a time eaten immediately

Practical minhag is stricter than his own ruling

Mishnah Berurah (321:14,20)

Rules according to Magen Avraham's reported minhag: one at a time only

This is the standard practice

p. 200Me'abed — Tanning

Leniencies - When Pickling Is Uncommon

Since the issur is because salting resembles pickling, if the item is not normally pickled in that form, it is permitted.

CaseHalacha L'Maaseh

Peeled cucumbers

PERMITTED - not normally pickled when peeled

Cut-up salad (cucumbers, tomatoes)

Rav S.Z. Auerbach and Rav Elyashiv: PERMITTED (not pickled when cut). Orchos Shabbos: FORBIDDEN (not in SA/MB)

Salad mostly of vegetables not normally pickled (carrots, potatoes)

PERMITTED even per Orchos Shabbos

Putting salt on salad immediately followed by oil or vinegar

PERMITTED - oil/vinegar prevents the pickling effect (MB 321:14)

Salting for same Shabbos meal

PERMITTED per Magen Avraham and Taz

Salting for a later Shabbos meal

PERMITTED per Mishnah Berurah; forbidden per MA and Taz

Salting for after Shabbos

FORBIDDEN according to all

p. 201Me'abed — Tanning

4. Salting Eggs and Cooked Meat

Is There an Issur at All?

The Rambam holds there is no issur to salt eggs or cooked meat for any duration, since pickling does not apply to them. Rashi holds there can be a Me'abed-type issur if they are left in salt long enough to harden. The Mechaber (SA 321:5) is strict like Rashi.

How Long Is 'Too Long'?

AuthorityPosition

Taz and Magen Avraham

Forbidden if intent is to eat at a later meal - even later in the same day

Mishnah Berurah (321:21)

Lenient - only forbidden if intent is to keep until after Shabbos; permits salting for a later meal on the same day

Halacha L'Maaseh

Follow Mishnah Berurah - salting eggs/cooked meat for any Shabbos meal is permitted

Practical Rule: One may salt eggs or cooked meat for any Shabbos meal. Salting them to keep until after Shabbos is forbidden.

p. 202Me'abed — Tanning

5. Other Cases of Me'abed

Item / CaseHalacha L'Maaseh

Beans or lentils cooked in their skins

FORBIDDEN to salt - same status as radish (SA 321:6; Taz)

Fish - salting to preserve

FORBIDDEN - Me'abed applies (MB 321:21)

Meat - salting to preserve (not for immediate eating)

FORBIDDEN

Washing blood from meat - not yet third day

PERMITTED

Washing blood from meat - third day (meat was not salted for 3 days)

FORBIDDEN for a Jew; in case of significant loss, ask a non-Jew; if no non-Jew available, a Jew may do it

TopicMechaber's ApproachAuthority He Follows

Salt water (hilmi)

Forbidden because it resembles Me'abed

Rashi and Tosefos

Salting vegetables

Forbidden because it resembles pickling - which resembles bishul

Rambam

Salting cooked meat/eggs to leave

Forbidden - concerned for Rashi's view that hardening effect constitutes Me'abed

Rashi (via Taz's explanation)

p. 203Me'abed — Tanning

The Pri Megadim (321:3,5) explains the Mechaber's mixed rulings: for salt water, most Rishonim agree with Rashi so he followed Rashi. For vegetables, the Rambam's reason (resemblance to pickling) is more readily understandable than Rashi's (a small amount of salt causing Me'abed hardening), so he followed the Rambam there.

p. 204–205Muktza

Hilchos Muktza

1. Foundations

Status of the Prohibition

Muktza is an issur miderabanan. Rashi (Pesachim 47b) appeared to hold it has a Torah source, but Tosefos (Pesachim 30a) definitively ruled otherwise. The halacha follows Tosefos.

The Core Machlokes: Rebbe Yehuda vs. Rebbe Shimon

PositionView on Muktza

Rebbe Yehuda

Strict - any item set aside for a specific, forbidden purpose may not be moved or used for another purpose.

Rebbe Shimon

Lenient - if an item has possible alternative uses, the person never fully 'sets it aside' mentally and it is not Muktza. The issur exists but is far more limited.

Which Posek Follows Which Opinion?

AuthorityAuthorityShabbosYom Tov

Rif / Rambam / Mechaber (SA)

Rif / Rambam / Mechaber (SA)

Rebbe Shimon (lenient)

Rebbe Yehuda (strict)

Rabbeinu Tam / Rama

Rabbeinu Tam / Rama

Rebbe Shimon for regular Muktza; Rebbe Yehuda for Nolad

Same as Shabbos

Rach / Mishnah Berurah

Rach / Mishnah Berurah

Rebbe Shimon (lenient)

Rebbe Shimon except for Nolad

Halacha

The halacha follows the Mishnah Berurah (=Rach): Rebbe Shimon always, except Nolad on Yom Tov.

The halacha follows the Mishnah Berurah (=Rach): Rebbe Shimon always, except Nolad on Yom Tov.

The halacha follows the Mishnah Berurah (=Rach): Rebbe Shimon always, except Nolad on Yom Tov.

p. 206Muktza

Nolad - Something That Came into Existence on Shabbos

Nolad is a sub-category of Muktza for items that did not exist (or were in a totally different state) before Shabbos. Examples:

  • An egg laid on Shabbos - Muktza according to all opinions.
  • Seeds that were in fruit at the onset of Shabbos and fell out on Shabbos - Muktza according to Rebbe Yehuda; Rebbe Shimon is lenient on Shabbos.
  • Condensation from an air conditioner - Nolad according to all opinions; assur to move.

2. The Five Categories of Muktza

Category 1: Muktza Machmas Gufa

Items with no conceivable Shabbos use - they are inherently set aside.

  • Examples: Stones, raw money, dirt.
  • For food: requires (a) dechiya beyadayim - an active act that made it inedible, AND (b) lo chazi - it is totally inedible. E.g., figs placed on a roof to dry (grogeres, tzimukim).
  • For non-food items (e.g., stones): the two conditions above are not required.
  • Rambam: only condition for food is that it is totally inedible - no requirement of dechiya beyadayim. Mechaber rules like Rashi/Tosefos: both conditions required for food.
p. 207Muktza

Category 2: Muktza Machmas Chisaron Kis

Items the person is careful to use only for their designated purpose, never to use them casually, and keeps in a set place - out of fear of financial loss.

  • Examples: Expensive tools, a mohel's scalpel, writing instruments (lechatchila - Rav Berkovits).
  • A wallet: The Elyah Rabbah rules it is generally Kli shemelachto l'issur, not Muktza machmas chisaron kis, since most people also keep non-Muktza items in their wallet.
  • A bed designated for money: If money is on it during Bein hashmashos, the bed becomes a bassis (see Section 4).
  • Wall clocks/paintings: Chazon Ish rules they are Muktza machmas chisaron kis. Rav Moshe Feinstein disagrees - they stay in place for function/decoration, not fear of damage.
  • Pesach cutlery: Rav Auerbach rules it is NOT Muktza machmas chisaron kis - the reason the person is careful with it is not one of the reasons recognized by Chazal.

Category 3: Muktza Machmas Issur

Items that were forbidden to use as Shabbos began, where there was also dechiya beyadayim (an active act that caused the forbidden state).

  • Classic example: A candle lit before Shabbos. The act of lighting = dechiya beyadayim; it is forbidden to move while lit. After it goes out, Rebbe Meir holds it remains Muktza. Rebbe Shimon permits - he expected it to go out (yoshev u'metsapeh).
  • Halacha follows Rebbe Meir (strict) re: Muktza machmas issur. The Mechaber rules a lit candle's wax remains Muktza after it goes out.
  • Animal carcass that died on Shabbos: NOT Muktza machmas issur - there was no dechiya beyadayim; the person did nothing to cause the issur. Permitted to feed to one's animals (Mechaber, SA 324:7).
  • Vegetable cut by a non-Jew on Shabbos: IS Muktza machmas issur - the Beis Yosef explains that failing to pick it before Shabbos is itself treated as dechiya beyadayim (a minor act to do; not doing it shows intent).

Key Rule

Muktza machmas issur requires dechiya beyadayim - an active act (or its near-equivalent) that put the object into a forbidden state as Shabbos began.

p. 208Muktza

Category 4: Kli Shemelachto L'issur

A utensil whose primary function is forbidden on Shabbos, but which has possible permitted uses. This is a more lenient category of Muktza - it may be moved in two situations:

Permitted Reason to MoveExamples

L'sorech gufo - to use the kli itself for a permitted purpose

Using a hammer to crack open nuts; using a knife for food.

L'sorech mekomo - the kli is in the way and you need the space

Moving a hammer off the couch to sit down.

  • If neither condition applies - do not move.
  • Kli shemelachto l'issur with NO possible permitted use at all: Baal HaMeor rules it is Muktza machmas gufa. Rashba rules it remains Kli shemelachto l'issur. Rav Moshe and Rav Berkovits rule leniently like the Rashba. Examples: umbrellas, thermometers, telephones.

Category 5: Kli Shemelachto L'heter

A utensil whose primary function is permitted on Shabbos. It may be moved for any purpose, including l'tsorech gufo or even without any need at all. Examples: plates, cups, books.

3. Selected Practical Cases

Balls and Toys

AuthorityRuling

Mechaber (SA 308:45)

Balls are Muktza machmas gufa - no valid kli function.

Rav Elyashiv, Rav Auerbach, Rav Wosner

Balls today are manufactured for play; Mechaber would be lenient.

Rav Ovadia Yosef, Rav Abba Shaul

Mechaber is strict even today. A child may rely on the Rama.

Rama (and Minhag)

Lenient - balls (and toys that do no Melacha) are not Muktza.

Mishnah Berurah

Appears lenient. Minhag is to be lenient.

p. 209Muktza

Pets and Animals

  • All non-domesticated animals: Muktza according to everyone.
  • Pets: Machlokes Rishonim (Rosh is strict; Maharich Ohr Zaruah is lenient). Consensus among Poskim: even pets are Muktza.
  • Fish tank: Rav Auerbach permits moving the tank (not the fish) - the tank serves a decorative function, not the fish alone, so it is not a bassis.

Flames and Electric Elements

  • A lit candle: Muktza - it is a bassis to the flame, which is Muktza.
  • Electric appliance with a heating element (lamp, hot plate, electric blanket): Machlokes. Rav Elyashiv: Muktza machmas gufa. Rav Moshe Feinstein, Rav Berkovits: Not Muktza machmas gufa - but it is Kli shemelachto l'issur.
  • Practical implication: May move such appliances l'sorech gufo or l'sorech mekomo only.

Keilim That Get Used Up

  • Candles, soap, erasers, pencils: Mor U'ketsiah rules they lack shem kli and are Muktza. Mishnah Berurah rules they are not Muktza (but may be Kli shemelachto l'issur).
  • Rav Berkovits: Lechatchila be strict for the Mor U'ketsiah with pencils, soap, and erasers.
p. 210Muktza

4. Bassis L'Dvar Issur

If Muktza rests intentionally on a non-Muktza object as Bein hashmashos begins, the supporting object (bassis) itself becomes Muktza - with the same severity as the Muktza placed upon it. It remains Muktza even if the Muktza item is removed during Shabbos.

When Does the Supporting Object Become a Bassis?

ScenarioBecomes Bassis?Notes

Muktza deliberately placed on object, remains through Bein hashmashos

YES

Classic case. Wallet in jacket pocket; candlesticks on table.

Placed on Friday with no specific intent to leave there

YES

Close proximity to Shabbos = assumed intent.

Placed mid-week (not usual storage spot) with no conscious Shabbos intent

NO

Inadvertent placement does not create bassis.

Muktza placed in usual storage spot

YES

Even if inadvertent - it is the expected place.

Muktza placed by someone else (chaveira)

NO

Owner never intended it.

Child placed the Muktza

NO

Child lacks halachic capacity to create a bassis.

Muktza fell onto item (coins fell onto chair)

NO

Unintentional placement.

Muktza placed on Shabbos itself

Disputed

MB: forbidden to move; may shake off Muktza, or place something more chashuv and move together.

p. 211Muktza

Bassis L'Dvar Heter V'Issur - Mixed Contents

If non-Muktza items of greater importance are also on the object during Bein hashmashos, the object does NOT become Muktza.

p. 212Muktza
  • 'Greater importance' is measured by necessity for Shabbos - not financial value.
  • Example: Challos and candlesticks on the Shabbos table. Since the challos are more needed, the table is not a bassis.
  • Money in a drawer that also has clothing needed for Shabbos: drawer does not become Muktza.

Practical Cases

CaseRuling

Candlesticks on a table (no important Dvar Heter)

Table becomes Muktza.

Wallet left in weekday jacket pocket

Jacket becomes Muktza.

Money left in drawer

Drawer becomes Muktza.

Money in drawer + clothing needed for Shabbos

Drawer does NOT become Muktza.

Candlesticks + challos on table during Bein hashmashos

Table does NOT become Muktza.

Visitor's money on host's plate

Plate does NOT become Muktza (chaveira).

Stone on top of book pages (stone is serving the book)

Book does NOT become Muktza.

Batteries inside a digital clock

Clock does NOT become Muktza - batteries serve the clock.

Raw meat on top of cake in freezer

Cake does NOT become Muktza (random stacking). Ideally place cake on top.

5. Broken Keilim & Gamru Bidei Adam

Kli That Breaks on Shabbos

ScenarioStatus

Breaks on Shabbos; no use whatsoever in new state

Muktza - all agree.

Breaks on Shabbos; can still be used for same purpose as before

NOT Muktza.

Breaks on Shabbos; can be used for a different purpose (but not original)

NOT Muktza (Mechaber). However, if it was originally Muktza machmas chisaron kis: Magen Avraham - still Muktza. Rebbe Akiva Eiger - not Muktza. MB rules like Magen Avraham.

Breaks on Erev Shabbos (still useable)

NOT Muktza.

Breaks on Erev Shabbos and is thrown in garbage on Erev Shabbos

Muktza - even if still has possible use.

Door of house detaches

Muktza - was never a kli independently.

Door of small cabinet detaches

NOT Muktza if has uses in new form - it had shem kli while attached.

p. 213Muktza

Gamru Bidei Adam - Inevitable Completion

If an item was in an unusable state as Shabbos began, but it was certain (not just possible) that it would become usable on Shabbos, it is not Muktza when it becomes usable.

CaseRuling

Raw food on the fire as Shabbos begins

NOT Muktza when cooked - Gamru bidei adam applies.

Wet clothing - will definitely dry (Muktza machmas issur)

Machlokes: Rav Zilber + Rav Elyashiv: still Muktza (Gamru bidei adam doesn't apply to Muktza machmas issur). Rav Minchas Yitzchak + Rav Auerbach + Rav Berkovits: NOT Muktza when dry.

Tanai (Pre-Shabbos Condition)

AuthorityRuling

Ramban / Mechaber

A tanai before Shabbos that one does not intend to set aside the object IS effective - object is not Muktza when it becomes usable.

Tosefos / Rama

A tanai does not help (unless the object was only lit accidentally and remained lit into Shabbos). Minhag follows Rama.

p. 214Muktza

6. Bittul Kli Miheichano

It is forbidden to actively make a kli Muktza on Shabbos by placing Muktza into it or on it - this is called bittul kli miheichano (nullifying a utensil from its [permitted] use).

Rules

  • Forbidden even for a short period - unless there is significant financial loss (Mishnah Berurah).
  • Permitted for a very short time, if the Muktza can be immediately shaken off.
  • Permitted for the whole Shabbos in a case of tzaar baalei chaim (animal suffering).
  • Permitted to place Kli shemelachto l'issur on a permitted item (it is still movable in certain situations). Forbidden to place Muktza machmas gufa on it.

Practical Cases

CaseRuling

Placing bucket under air conditioner drip (water = Nolad)

FORBIDDEN - bittul kli miheichano. Permitted only if a more chashuv non-Muktza item is also in the bucket.

Making clothing very dirty so it cannot be worn

FORBIDDEN - renders the garment Muktza.

Putting garbage into a garbage bin

PERMITTED - this is the bin's primary use.

Putting garbage into plastic bags / plates

PERMITTED - commonly used this way.

Placing pillows under glass keilim (to prevent breakage)

PERMITTED - significant financial loss.

p. 215–216Muktza

Quick Summary: The Five Categories

CategoryDefinitionHalacha L'Maaseh

1. Muktza Machmas Gufa

No conceivable Shabbos use. For food: needs dechiya beyadayim + lo chazi.

Forbidden to move in any circumstance.

2. Muktza Machmas Chisaron Kis

Valuable kli person is careful to keep only for its designated use.

Forbidden to move in any circumstance (Magen Avraham; MB).

3. Muktza Machmas Issur

Forbidden as Shabbos begins + dechiya beyadayim.

Forbidden to move. Rebbe Shimon lenient if yoshev u'metsapeh - but halacha follows Rebbe Meir.

4. Kli Shemelachto L'issur

Utensil primarily for forbidden Shabbos use, but has permitted uses.

May move l'sorech gufo or l'sorech mekomo only.

5. Kli Shemelachto L'heter

Utensil primarily for permitted Shabbos use.

May move freely, even without any need.

Bottom Line

When in doubt about a specific case, the question to ask is: (1) Does this item have a valid Shabbos use? (2) Was it deliberately set aside? (3) Was there dechiya beyadayim? These three questions determine the category.

p. 217Refuah — Medical Treatment

Hilchos Refuah on Shabbos

1. The Five Categories of People

Chazal forbade refuah (medical treatment) on Shabbos out of concern that a person would grind herbs to make medicine - transgressing the Melacha of Tochein. The scope of this gezeira depends on the person's level of illness.

CategoryDefinitionRefuah Status on Shabbos

1. Totally healthy person

No illness whatsoever.

May consume Maachal briyim freely. Issur refuah on non-Maachal-briyim items if intent is health (MA; MB).

2. Baal meichush

Somewhat unwell; walking around.

May consume Maachal briyim. Forbidden to take non-Maachal-briyim items for refuah; Machlokes if for eating only (Elyah Rabbah strict).

3. Choleh she'ein boh sakana

Severely ill throughout body; not life-threatening. Bed-ridden OR whole body feels weak.

May take medicine (minhag); may ask non-Jew to do Melacha doraisa; Jew may do Issur derabanan with shinui (Ramban/MB).

4. Sakanas eiver

Limb at risk of being lost; not life-threatening.

All Issurei derabanan permitted (Ran, Ramban).

5. Choleh she'yesh boh sakana

Life-threatening situation.

All Issurei doraisa permitted and obligatory; Shabbos is docheh.

p. 218Refuah — Medical Treatment

Why Animals?

Chazal did not forbid refuah for animals - the Rif explains that a person does not panic about an animal's illness the same way he panics about his own, so the concern of grinding herbs does not apply.

2. Maachal Briyim - Food of Healthy People

Maachal briyim refers to food and drink consumed by healthy people, even if some eat it primarily for health. It is the key concept that separates permitted from forbidden consumption for Baalei Meichush.

Rules by Person Type

PersonConsuming Maachal BriyimConsuming Non-Maachal-Briyim

Totally healthy

Always permitted - for any reason.

Machlokes: Mechaber (lenient); Magen Avraham (strict if for health); MB strict for MA. Rav Moshe: MA only applies if the person has some weakness. Rav Auerbach: MA applies to all.

Baal meichush

Permitted - for any reason.

Forbidden if intent is refuah. Machlokes if intent is for eating only: MB strict for Elyah Rabbah.

Choleh she'ein boh sakana

Permitted.

Medicine permitted (minhag/Radbaz).

Vitamins - Practical Application

AuthorityRuling on Vitamins

Rav Auerbach / Orchos Shabbos

Forbidden for everyone - falls under MA's prohibition on non-Maachal-briyim items.

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Forbidden only if vitamin-deficient or weak in a specific area. Totally healthy person - permitted.

Tzitz Eliezer

Permitted - vitamins today are used like food (Maachal briyim). Most Poskim dispute this.

Sefardim (Mechaber)

Permitted - healthy person may consume non-Maachal-briyim for any reason.

p. 219Refuah — Medical Treatment

3. Scope of the Gezeira & Non-Medication Treatments

The gezeira only applies to treatments where there is a concern the person will grind herbs (i.e., treatments that could be replaced by medication). Treatments for which no medication could be used are not within the gezeira - but may still be forbidden due to Uvdin d'chol.

TreatmentStatus

Hot cup on stomach for pain

Permitted - no herb-grinding concern; permitted even for Baal meichush.

Back exercises for back pain

Forbidden - pain could theoretically be treated with medication, so any form of refuah is included in the gezeira (Orchos Shabbos).

Vigorous self-massage / rubbing hard

Forbidden if for health (Rambam/Biur Halacha). Permitted for pleasure with a shinui (SA 327:2).

Rubbing with feet on saliva

Permitted - not done for health, not Memarayach (Magen Avraham).

Bathing in healing waters (Diomsis-type)

Forbidden - either Uvdin d'chol or healing waters.

Sunbathing for health

Forbidden (Chelkas Yaakov). Also possible Tzovaya if tanning is intended (Minchas Yitzchak). Rav Fisher and Shemiras Shabbos K'Hilchasa: no Tzovaya issue.

Physiotherapy / exercises

Forbidden today even without sweating - the modern equivalent is done for health (Orchos Shabbos), which brings it into the gezeira.

Mouthwash

Permitted - removes bad breath only, not the source of bad breath (Eglei Tal distinction).

Substances removing cause of bad breath

Machlokes: HaRav Yosef forbids (Gezeiras refuah); Tosefos permits (issue of carrying, not refuah).

p. 220Refuah — Medical Treatment

4. Preventative Treatment, Bandages & Mixing Medicine

Key Rule

Preventative treatment - protecting against future harm - is NOT within the gezeiras refuah. Only actual healing is forbidden for Baalei Meichush.

CaseRuling

Putting bandage on wound to protect from infection

Permitted - protective, not healing.

Putting old clothing on unworn wound

Forbidden - old unused bandages have healing properties (SA 328:23).

Old clothing already previously used on wound

Permitted - it has lost its healing property.

New clothing/sponge on wound

Permitted - for protection only, not healing.

Cream or ointment on bandage

Forbidden unless Choleh she'ein boh sakana (Memarayach issue also applies).

Bandage with ointment fell on ground

Forbidden to return (concern of Memarayach); if fell onto a kli - permitted to return (SA 328:25; Rif; Rambam).

Wound that has already healed

Permitted to put bandage - purely protective (SA 328:27).

p. 221Refuah — Medical Treatment

Mixing Medicine with Food or Drink

AuthorityRuling

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Forbidden to drink liquid in which pills were dissolved on Erev Shabbos, unless it is normal to dissolve them immediately before consuming them (like kilor eye drops).

Rav Auerbach, Rav Wosner, Rav Karelitz, Minchas Yitzchak

Permitted - on condition that the medication is not recognizable in the food or drink.

Preventative Medication

  • Toothpaste: Permitted - purpose is preventative, not healing (Rav Ovadia Yosef; accepted by most).
  • Retainers/braces: Rav Klein forbids (Tikkun eivarim on Shabbos). Rav Auerbach permits.
  • Preventative medication before a condition worsens: Rav Auerbach permits - if one knows a small headache will become a migraine without medication, may take it now. Rav Moshe disagrees.

Antibiotics

AuthorityRuling

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Forbidden in most cases even if mid-course; permitted only if without it the person would never heal and emotional illness is a concern.

Rav Auerbach

Permitted if the course is 7+ days. If less than 7 days - should begin after Shabbos to avoid taking on Shabbos.

Rav Shlomo Kluger / Chazon Ish

Permitted even if course is less than 7 days.

p. 222Refuah — Medical Treatment

5. Choleh She'ein Boh Sakana - Definition & Halachos

Definition

AuthorityDefinition

Ran (Shabbos 39b)

Must be bed-ridden. If able to walk, even in great pain - not a Choleh she'ein boh sakana.

Maggid Mishneh (in name of Rashba)

OR: in pain and sick from it throughout the body.

Rama (SA 328:37)

Even if able to walk, if his entire body feels ill due to the pain - qualifies.

Examples

ConditionStatus

Severe cramps; severe back pain

Choleh she'ein boh sakana.

Migraine headache

Choleh she'ein boh sakana.

Chicken-pox, measles, conjunctivitis

Choleh she'ein boh sakana.

Children

Lower threshold - if unable to function normally, likely qualifies.

p. 223Refuah — Medical Treatment

What a Jew May Do for a Choleh She'ein Boh Sakana

OpinionSakanas EiverCholeh She'ein Boh Sakana

Ran

All Issurei derabanan permitted.

No Issur derabanan permitted for a Jew.

Ramban / Mechaber

All Issurei derabanan.

Issur derabanan with a shinui.

Tur's reading of Rambam

All Issurei derabanan.

All Issurei derabanan.

Maggid Mishneh (Rambam)

All Issurei derabanan.

Only Issurei derabanan not designed to prevent doraisa violations.

What is Always PermittedWhat is ConditionalWhat is Forbidden

Asking a non-Jew to do Melacha doraisa.

Issur derabanan with shinui - permitted (MB reads Ramban this way).

Regular Issur derabanan without shinui (Ramban/MB).

Giving medicine (accepted minhag; Radbaz; Rama).

Issur doraisa with shinui - permitted if no non-Jew available (SA HaRav; Rav Auerbach).

Issur doraisa by a Jew in normal fashion.

Practical Cases (Choleh She'ein Boh Sakana)

CaseRuling

Carrying medicine in Carmelis in unusual way

Permitted (Issur derabanan with shinui).

Smearing medical salve with back of a spoon

Permitted (Memarayach derabanan + shinui).

Turning on hot water tap with Dud shemesh, unusually

Permitted (shinui).

Signing a form to get treatment, with weak hand

Rav Auerbach: Permitted if no other way (writing + shinui).

Bishul akum cooked on Shabbos for Choleh

Permitted for Choleh. After Shabbos for healthy person: Rama permits (like Reah); MB/Taz forbid. Pri Megadim: Even forbidden for Choleh on weekday.

p. 224Refuah — Medical Treatment

Medicine for a Choleh She'ein Boh Sakana

AuthorityAuthorityPosition

Rambam, Ramban, Beis Yosef, Radbaz, Rama, Magen Avraham

Rambam, Ramban, Beis Yosef, Radbaz, Rama, Magen Avraham

Permitted - Chazal never included medicine for a Choleh she'ein boh sakana in the gezeira.

Bach, Taz, Pri Megadim

Bach, Taz, Pri Megadim

Appear to forbid - violation of the Ramban's principle.

Mishnah Berurah

Mishnah Berurah

Ideal to be strict, but need not protest those who are lenient. Most contemporary Poskim are lenient. Minhag is to be lenient.

Bottom Line

The accepted minhag is that a Choleh she'ein boh sakana may take medicine on Shabbos.

The accepted minhag is that a Choleh she'ein boh sakana may take medicine on Shabbos.

p. 225Refuah — Medical Treatment

6. Choleh She'yesh Boh Sakana - Pikuach Nefesh

Fundamental Rule

It is not only permitted but obligatory to break Shabbos to save a life. One who acts with alacrity is praiseworthy (Rambam). One who is unnecessarily hesitant is to be rebuked.

Hutra or Dechuya - Nature of the Heter

AuthorityPosition

Maharam MiRottenburg / Avnei Nezer (reading of Rambam)

Shabbos is Hutra - as if no Issur is being committed at all. Comparable to Yom Tov Melacha for food.

Rashba, Ran, simple reading of Rambam (Halacha 1)

Shabbos is Dechuya - the Issur is present but overridden.

Mishnah Berurah

Appears to hold Dechuya.

Defining 'Danger' - When Do We Act?

ScenarioRuling

Safek (doubt) whether life is at risk

Break Shabbos - safek nefashos lehakel.

Sfek sfeika (double doubt)

Break Shabbos.

Will extend life only briefly

Break Shabbos (Chai bahem principle).

Person sentenced to death by Beis Din

Biur Halacha: forbidden to break Shabbos for him.

Not in danger today but danger in future

Break Shabbos to prevent the future danger (SA 328:11; MB).

Certain that not doing Melacha will NOT endanger

Wait until after Shabbos.

p. 226Refuah — Medical Treatment

What Melachos are Permitted?

AuthorityScope

Rambam / Ramban / Mechaber

Permitted to do any Melacha normally done in the week for the Choleh - even non-life-saving needs.

Rashi and many Rishonim

Only Melacha directly connected to saving the life.

Biur Halacha

Non-life-saving Melachos should be done by a non-Jew; Melachos strengthening the Choleh where weakness could be dangerous - permitted by a Jew.

By Whom Should the Melacha Be Done?

AuthorityRuling

Rambam / Mechaber

A Jew (adult man) should do the Melacha - not non-Jew, woman, or child. (Concern about misimpression that it is forbidden for Jews to do Melacha for pikuach nefesh.)

Tosefos / Rama

If there is no concern that the non-Jew will be lax: better that he do it. This is the minhag.

Taz

A Jew will act with greater urgency - better that he do the Melacha.

Doing Melacha with a Shinui

AuthorityRuling

Ramban

In all cases of pikuach nefesh, if it can be done with a shinui without dangerous delay - must do shinui.

Rambam / Mechaber

The shinui requirement is limited to a Yoledes (childbirth). Other cases: no shinui required.

Rama

Rules like Ramban - shinui where possible in all pikuach nefesh cases.

p. 227Refuah — Medical Treatment

Miscellaneous Pikuach Nefesh Rules

  • Doing Melacha to allay the Choleh's fear: Permitted (Ramban, Tosefos) - fear itself is dangerous.
  • Husband accompanying wife in labor to hospital: Permitted if she is afraid to go alone (Rav Moshe).
  • Intending for additional Melacha while saving a life (e.g., catching fish while saving baby): Machlokes Rishonim. MB appears strict.
  • Marbeh b'shiurim: Forbidden - do not perform Melacha on a larger quantity than necessary. Better to do one act on a larger amount than two acts on a smaller amount.

7. Doctors, Patients & Who Decides

ScenarioRuling

Choleh says 'I need to eat'; one doctor says no

Feed the Choleh - everyone agrees.

Choleh says 'I don't need'; one doctor says he does

Feed the Choleh - everyone agrees.

Choleh says 'I need'; two doctors say he doesn't

Rav Yannai: Follow doctors (don't feed). Mar Bar Rav Ashi, Rach, Rambam, Mechaber: Feed the Choleh.

Two doctors say he needs to eat; majority say he doesn't

Ramban, Rosh, Mechaber: Feed him - safek nefashos lehakel. Rashi, Rambam: Follow majority.

Equal numbers of doctors on each side

Follow the more expert doctor (Ramban; Magen Avraham).

Non-doctor onlooker says it is life-threatening

Permitted to break Shabbos if a Jew; if no Jew expert, ask non-Jew to do Melacha (Mishnah Berurah).

Choleh himself is a doctor

Machlokes whether to attribute weight to his self-assessment.

Choleh says 'I need a specific medicine'; doctor disagrees

Follow the doctor regarding specific medicines.

p. 228Refuah — Medical Treatment

8. Yoledes - Woman in Labor

A Yoledes (woman in labor) has the halachic status of Choleh she'yesh boh sakana from a certain point in labor.

When Does Pikuach Nefesh Status Begin?

Stage of LaborStatus

Yoshev al hamishbar (sits in labor position)

Permitted to do Melachos - Abaye; Rif rules like this.

Blood flows

Permitted - Rav Huna (lenient version).

Needs friends to help her walk

Permitted - Rav Huna (another version).

Crying out in pain (before above stages)

Rambam: Permitted to light a candle at this point, even before the full onset.

Any of the above - whichever comes first

SA rules like Ramban: permitted at whichever stage occurs first.

Before any stage, if delay risks danger

Permitted; certainly permitted to travel to hospital early.

p. 229Refuah — Medical Treatment

Status After Birth

PeriodStatus

Days 1–3 after birth

Choleh she'yesh boh sakana - even if she says she doesn't need it.

Days 3–7

Choleh she'yesh boh sakana if she says she needs it. If she says she doesn't - forbidden.

Days 7–30

Choleh she'ein boh sakana - non-Jew should do any needed Melachos.

After 30 days

Healthy; normal halachos apply.

Counting the 3 days

MB: count m'eis l'eis (72 hours) - lenient for safek nefashos lehakel.

9. Saving a Non-Jew & Limiting Chillul Shabbos

Saving a Non-Jew on Shabbos

ScenarioRuling

Breaking Shabbos Issurei doraisa to save non-Jew (no enmity concern)

Forbidden (Rambam).

Issurei derabanan if enmity (eivah) concern

Permitted - most Poskim.

Issurei doraisa if enmity concern

Tzitz Eliezer: Permitted if the Melacha is she'ein sricha l'gufa. Rav Moshe: Permitted - genuine danger to Jewish people if Jewish doctors don't treat non-Jews.

Karaite (observes Shabbos)

Magen Avraham citing Knesses Gedolah: Permitted to break Shabbos.

Tinok shenishba

Permitted - treated like a Jew.

p. 230Refuah — Medical Treatment

Eighth-Month Baby

  • Based on Rishonim: Permitted to break Shabbos only if hair and nails fully developed.
  • Contemporary ruling: Obligatory to perform Melachos for any premature baby - modern medicine can save them.

Putting Oneself in a Situation of Danger

  • Forbidden to place oneself in a situation where one will definitely need to do Melachos on Shabbos (Baal HaMeor; Mechaber).
  • Baal HaMeor: Forbidden only within 3 days of Shabbos; permitted more than 3 days before. Permitted within 3 days for a Mitzva.
  • Biur Halacha: Many Rishonim disagree - forbidden any day of the week. Conclusion: be strict.
  • Rav Moshe: Even if one unjustifiably placed himself in danger - still obligated to break Shabbos to save him.

Returning After Saving a Life (Hitiru Sofan Mishum Haschalasan)

  • If the rescuer is still needed at his original place (e.g., Hatzala): Permitted to do Issurei doraisa (drive) to return.
  • If not needed: Most Poskim permit Issurei derabanan (e.g., ask non-Jew to drive) but not doraisa.
  • Rav Moshe Feinstein: Permits Issurei doraisa if he expected to complete the task and return within Shabbos.
  • Rav Tzvi Pesach Frank (and most Poskim): Does not permit Issurei doraisa to return unless he may be needed for further pikuach nefesh.
p. 231Refuah — Medical Treatment

Quick Summary: What Is Permitted for Each Category

CategoryWhat a Jew May DoWhat a Non-Jew May Do

Totally healthy

Consume Maachal briyim freely. Non-Maachal-briyim: Machlokes (MA strict; Mechaber lenient).

N/A

Baal meichush

Consume Maachal briyim. Non-Maachal-briyim for eating only: Machlokes (Elyah Rabbah strict).

N/A

Choleh she'ein boh sakana

Medicine (minhag). Issur derabanan with shinui (Ramban/MB). Issur doraisa with shinui if no non-Jew (SA HaRav; Rav Auerbach).

Melacha doraisa (everyone agrees).

Sakanas eiver

All Issurei derabanan (Ran, Ramban).

Melacha doraisa.

Choleh she'yesh boh sakana

All Issurei doraisa - obligatory. With shinui where possible without delay (Rama/Ramban). Without shinui permitted (Rambam/Mechaber).

Melacha doraisa (better that Jew does it - MB/Rambam; unless non-Jew more reliable - Rama).

Core Principle

When in any doubt about pikuach nefesh - act immediately. Safek nefashos lehakel. One who is zealous is praiseworthy; one who delays because of over-caution is to be rebuked (Rambam, Hilchos Shabbos 2:3).

When in any doubt about pikuach nefesh - act immediately. Safek nefashos lehakel. One who is zealous is praiseworthy; one who delays because of over-caution is to be rebuked (Rambam, Hilchos Shabbos 2:3).

Kosher U'Matir

Kosher U'Matir

Kosher U'Matir

p. 232Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying

1. Background: The Melacha of Kosher

Source in the Mishkan

Thread ends were knotted to hold stitching in place; seam ends were knotted to prevent unraveling.

Melacha of Matir

Untying is the corresponding melacha (mirror of Kosher).

2. Machlokes Rishonim: What Makes a Knot Forbidden?

Two Approaches

Rashi, Rosh, Tur

Duration the knot is intended to last

Temporal intent

Rif, Rambam

Type of knot (craftsman vs. simple) + whether it is made to last

Knot quality + permanence

3. Determining the Duration of a Knot: Taz vs. Biur Halacha

AuthorityPositionPractical Effect

Taz (Siman 317:1)

Follows the person's specific intent - when do you plan to untie it?

Even a normally permanent knot is permitted if you plan to untie it that day.

Biur Halacha (Siman 317:1)

Follows the normal/standard duration for that type of knot

Even if you plan to untie it today, a normally permanent knot remains assur mid'oraisa.

p. 235Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying

4. Mechaber and Rama - Halacha L'Maaseh

Mechaber (SA 317:1)

Rules like Rif/Rambam: only a permanent kesher uman is assur mid'oraisa.

Rama

Combines both opinions (strict on each point): • A permanent knot = assur mid'oraisa even if not a kesher uman (Rashi). • A kesher uman made to untie that day = assur mid'rabanan (Rif/Rambam). • Two opinions cited: knot permitted if < 1 week OR only if untied same day - halacha is to be strict: only permitted if untied same day.

p. 236Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying

5. Kesher Al Gabai Kesher (Double Knot) and Related

Type of Knot/BowStatusSource

Kesher al gabai kesher (knot on knot)

Assur even if meant to be untied same day - may be a kesher uman (Rama)

Shiltei Giburim; Rama

Kesher v'aniva (knot + bow on top)

Permitted if intended to be untied that day

p. 237Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying

Inadvertent kesher al gabai kesher: MB - may untie only if causing pain. Chazon Ish - may untie even without pain (since the strict minhag only applies to deliberate knots).

6. Twist-Ties, Ropes, and Cutting

Twisting into a rope (Rambam)

Making threads into a rope is a tolda of Kosher; undoing it is a tolda of Matir - even without an actual knot, if it creates a very tight binding.

Twist-tie (Rav S.Z. Auerbach)

Twisting more than once and leaving closed for more than one day is forbidden. Twisting once only = permitted.

Cutting a permitted knot

Permitted (equivalent to untying). Should not be done in front of an am ha'aretz.

Cutting a forbidden knot

Forbidden.

Knots on choslos (vessel wrapping)

Permitted to untie or cut - these are not made-to-last knots (Mishnah Berurah).

p. 238Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying

7. Melacha of Matir - Untying

AuthorityPositionCondition

Rach

Chayav only if untying in order to re-tie (matir al menas likshor)

Must have intent to re-tie

Tosefos

Uncertain

-

Rashi

Chayav even if not al menas likshor

No condition required

Biur Halacha

Assur mid'oraisa to untie any otherwise-forbidden knot if there is any positive benefit to the untying

Positive benefit required (e.g. to open a vessel)

Poskim: It is always permitted to untie any knot that was made inadvertently - whether made on Shabbos or on a weekday.

8. Tying for the Sake of a Mitzva

The Question

May one tie a knot that is normally forbidden (assur mid'rabanan) if doing so is needed for a mitzva?

Rambam / Tur / Mechaber

Permitted to tie a normally assur mid'rabanan knot for the sake of a mitzva.

Rashi / Tosefos / Bartenura

Strict - not permitted even for a mitzva.

Mishnah Berurah

Implies to be strict. Exception: fixing a broken eruv on Shabbos to prevent the public from sinning (mitzva d'rabbim).

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Lenient for a mitzva d'rabbim (e.g. lights in a shul so the tzibbur can daven/learn).

Rav Elyashiv

Strict even for a mitzva d'rabbim.

Melacha doraisa for mitzva

Generally forbidden. In the Beis HaMikdash only: even doraisa permitted to fix instruments (Rambam).

p. 239Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying

Shvus d'shvus: Asking a non-Jew (shvus #1) to do an issur derabanan (shvus #2) is permitted for a mitzva, great need, or miksas choli - but that is amira l'akum, not Kosher itself.
