p. 241Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing

1. Background: The Melacha of Tofer

Source in the Mishkan

The ten panels of the bottom wool covering were sewn together. Alternatively (Yerushalmi): sewing was needed to repair torn coverings.

Core definition

Weaving/sewing together parts of fabric into one combined unit.

Koraya - the mirror melacha

Tearing apart what was sewn together. Discussed in Sections 4–7 below.

2. Minimum Requirements for a Chiyuv

ActStatusAuthority / Notes

Two needle penetrations (tekifus) with a knot

Assur mid'oraisa - Tofer

The knot need not be a lasting one. If it is a lasting knot, also transgresses Kosher.

Two tekifus with a lasting knot

Assur mid'oraisa - Tofer AND Kosher

Transgresses two melachos

Three tekifus - even without any knot

Assur mid'oraisa

All opinions

Two tekifus without any knot

Assur mid'rabanan

Korban Nesanel; Mishnah Berurah

Combining two objects by pinning, gluing, or any means

Included in Tofer (mid'oraisa)

Rambam, per Rav Dovid Ribiat - Tofer = unifying any two separate objects into one entity

p. 242Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing

3. Tofer L'Zman - Is Temporary Sewing Permitted?

The Question: Just as a temporary knot (Kosher l'zman) is permitted, is a temporary act of sewing (Tofer l'zman) also permitted?

AuthorityPositionNotes

Mordechi

Strict - no heter for temporary Tofer

Mechaber rules like Mordechi (SA 340:6–7)

Ravya

Lenient - temporary Tofer is permitted, just like temporary Kosher

Minhag followed this (Darchei Moshe)

Mechaber (SA 340)

Strict - rules like Mordechi; does not cite Ravya

Rama (SA 340:7)

Appears strict (like Mordechi)

Chazon Ish: Rama is strict

Rama (SA 317:3)

Permits relying on Ravya - not in front of amei ha'aretz

Rav S.Z. Auerbach: Rama is lenient

Tehilla L'David / Rav Elyashiv

Strict for temporary Tofer; lenient for temporary Koraya (tearing)

Hybrid position

Beis Yosef (SA 317)

Permits relying on Ravya - but not in front of amei ha'aretz

Darchei Moshe HaAruch agrees

p. 243Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing

Bottom line: The Poskim dispute the Rama's position. L'maaseh, one should not rely on the leniency in front of amei ha'aretz. The Minhag was to follow the Ravya.

Tightening a Loosened Stitch (SA 340:6)

Pulling a thread to tighten a loosened stitch

Assur mid'oraisa (Mordechi; Mechaber) - because of Tofer. If there is also a knot, transgresses mid'oraisa even more clearly.

Garment designed to be tightened (visible gathers)

Permitted - it is recognizable that this is how the garment is designed; does not appear as tightening a thread (Mordechi).

Two stitches (no knot)

Assur mid'oraisa to tighten - Pri Megadim: becomes very tight even without a knot.

Diaper tabs (sticking to itself)

Permitted - no Issur Tofer when part of one item sticks to itself (Rav Moshe Feinstein, Igros Moshe OC 2:84).

p. 244Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing

4. Various Ways of Combining Objects - Practical Halacha

Item / ActionStatusReason / Details

Buttoning a garment

PERMITTED

Two reasons: (1) Buttons are designed to be fastened and unfastened - like opening/closing a door. (2) Tofer requires items unified to the point of needing tearing to separate; a button does not achieve this.

Safety pins

PERMITTED (majority)

Similar to a button - does not unify items the way sewing does. Chazon Ish, Rav Moshe, Rav Auerbach, Minchas Yitzchak all permit. Some disagree. Certainly permitted if used for less than one day.

Velcro / zippers

PERMITTED

Designed to be fastened and unfastened - universally permitted.

Magnets

Generally PERMITTED

Comparable to velcro. Some question this. Rav Ribiat: do not leave magnets attached long-term.

Tape / adhesive stickers

FORBIDDEN

Forbidden to use tape, to tape two sheets of paper, to tape a note to the wall, or to use adhesive note-pads (not designed to remove and reattach like velcro).

Tape / stickers for less than one day

Disputed

Depends on the above machlokes regarding Tofer l'zman.

Band-aid on skin

PERMITTED

Inherently temporary in nature.

Sticking both ends of a band-aid together (> 1 day)

Disputed

Some forbid if intended for more than one day.

Peeling protective backing from a band-aid

Disputed

Rav Auerbach / Rav Karelitz: lenient. Rav Elyashiv: strict.

p. 245Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing

5. The Melacha of Koraya - Definition

Basic definition

Tearing apart what was sewn/joined together - the mirror melacha of Tofer.

Rambam (Shabbos 10:11)

Sticking together pieces of paper or skin = tolda of Tofer. Tearing them apart = Koraya.

What requires Koraya?

Tearing apart items that were previously combined into one unit.

p. 246Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing

Does Koraya Apply to Paper and Skin?

AuthorityPositionBasis

Shulchan Aruch HaRav (340:17a)

Koraya only applies to materials that were originally made of separate pieces that were combined. Paper and skin - never separate sections - are NOT subject to Koraya.

Logical derivation from Tofer/Koraya relationship

Biur Halacha (340:13)

Disagrees - tearing skin IS Koraya, per the Yerushalmi.

Yerushalmi

Rambam (Shabbos 23:6)

Tearing paper = forbidden due to Tikkun Maneh (a form of Makeh V'Patish) - does NOT mention Koraya.

Gemara, Beitzah

p. 247Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing

The Question: Is Koraya mid'oraisa only when tearing in order to sew back (al menas litfor), or even for any constructive purpose? Authority

Notes

Gemara (Shabbos 105b)

One who tears as an act of mourning or out of anger is chayav - even without intent to re-sew.

Constructive tearing = chayav even without litfor

Constructive tearing = chayav even without litfor

Rashi (105b)

Tearing as an act of mourning = Melacha she'ein tzricha l'gufo - not mid'oraisa.

Tosefos (105b)

Tearing for mourning = she'tzricha l'gufo (chayav). Tearing out of anger = she'ein tzricha l'gufo.

Any constructive tearing = assur mid'oraisa, even without intent to re-sew.

Main practical ruling

Main practical ruling

Biur Halacha - further refinement

Koraya requires intent to use both parts of the torn item. If only one part is used and the other discarded - no Koraya. But the usable part triggers Makeh V'Patish.

Explains why tearing paper for roasting fish is not Koraya

7. Koraya of Vessels and Packaging

Breaking a barrel (Mishna 146a)

Permitted - Rashi: destructive act. Tosefos: barrel is unstable, liable to fall apart on its own; breaking it is not real Soser. Ran: small vessel - only mid'rabanan; permitted for Shabbos need.

Permitted - Rashi: destructive act. Tosefos: barrel is unstable, liable to fall apart on its own; breaking it is not real Soser. Ran: small vessel - only mid'rabanan; permitted for Shabbos need.

Tearing skin covering of a barrel

Permitted - Rav Moshe Feinstein: Koraya only applies when the torn item will visibly be sewn up again. If there is no visible evidence of constructive use, it is permitted.

Permitted - Rav Moshe Feinstein: Koraya only applies when the torn item will visibly be sewn up again. If there is no visible evidence of constructive use, it is permitted.

Choslos (date-leaf fruit wrapping)

Permitted to cut open - Mechaber: treated like peels.

Permitted to cut open - Mechaber: treated like peels.

Food packets discarded after use

Permitted - Rav Moshe: wrapping designed only for that one use = treated like a peel; no Issur.

Permitted - Rav Moshe: wrapping designed only for that one use = treated like a peel; no Issur.

Food packets that are reused

Forbidden to tear - the peel-analogy does not apply.

Forbidden to tear - the peel-analogy does not apply.

Rav Moshe's Gezeira: Despite the above heteirim, Rav Moshe issued a general prohibition against opening packets, vessels, and boxes on Shabbos. This ruling is not universally followed. The Poskim recommend opening all such items before Shabbos to avoid the issue entirely.

Chazon Ish: Strict - some Poskim say: immediately discard the packet after opening to satisfy the Chazon Ish's concern.

p. 249Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing

8. Separating Stuck Pages

Pages stuck together inadvertently (food, substance)

Permitted to separate - Magen Avraham: kal v'chomer from the fact that intentionally tied temporary knots may be untied.

Pages stuck together with writing on the edges

Forbidden - tearing erases writing (Mochek).

Pages stuck together at binding (never separated at production)

Forbidden - tearing them open = Makeh V'Patish (fixing/completing the item).

p. 250–251Memachek — Smoothing

Memachek

1. Foundations - Definition of Memachek

Memachek ('smoothing') is one of the 39 Melachos. Its origin in the Mishkan was smoothing the hides used in construction.

Memachek vs. Gozez - What's the Difference?

ViewDistinction Between Memachek & Gozez

Rambam (Shabbos 11:5, 9:7)

Gozez = removing hair/wool for the sake of the hair/wool itself. Memachek = removing hair for the sake of the skin - to smooth it.

Sidrei Tahara (citing Rash)

The method differs: Gozez = cutting. Memachek = scraping.

Can Memachek Apply to a Living Animal?

The Rambam implies Memachek only applies post-mortem. However, Tosefos (Shabbos 73b) disagrees: Rabbeinu Tam held that milking an animal is Memachek (because the nipples are smoothed). Tosefos did not accept that application but agreed Memachek can in principle occur on a living animal.

Surfaces Beyond Animal Hides

SourceSourceApplication

Gemara Shabbos 75b (Rashi)

Gemara Shabbos 75b (Rashi)

Smoothing the ground between pillars of a building = Memachek.

Rambam / Tosefos (Shabbos 75b)

Rambam / Tosefos (Shabbos 75b)

Rubbing the leather stretched over pillars to smooth it = Memachek.

Gemara Shabbos 74b; Chayei Adam

Gemara Shabbos 74b; Chayei Adam

Removing hairs from a bird's spine is Memachek only if intent is for the skin. If for the hair - not Memachek.

Key Principle

One is only liable for Memachek when the intent is for the sake of the surface being smoothed - not for the material being removed.

One is only liable for Memachek when the intent is for the sake of the surface being smoothed - not for the material being removed.

p. 252Memachek — Smoothing

2. Memarayach - Smoothing Soft Substances

Memarayach is the Tolda (sub-category) of Memachek that applies to soft and pliable substances - as opposed to the Av Melacha which involves hard surfaces. The Mishna (Shabbos 146a) establishes that smearing wax into a barrel opening is Assur midoraisa.

Three Levels of Substance Consistency

TypeStatusExamples

Pliant solid substances (hard enough to hold shape)

Assur midoraisa

Wax, solid soap, chapstick, solid lipstick, solid deodorant, tar, congealed fat, dough, Silly Putty.

Dense semi-solids (thick but spreadable)

Assur miderabanan

Facial/hand creams, petroleum jelly, skin cream, toothpaste.

Viscous liquids (flows freely)

Generally permitted (some Poskim strict if it lathers)

Liquid soap (most Poskim permit; Rav Berkovits and Rav Moshe are strict), baby oil, olive oil.

p. 253Memachek — Smoothing

Key Practical Cases

CaseRuling

Pressing/shaping soft wax drippings

Assur midoraisa (also Muktza).

Melting bottom of wax candle to stick to holder

Assur midoraisa - even on Yom Tov.

Chapstick for chapped lips

Assur midoraisa (also possible Issur refuah).

Solid lipstick

Assur midoraisa (also Tzovaya).

Solid deodorant sticks

Assur midoraisa.

Washing with solid soap

Assur midoraisa - all contemporary Ashkenazic Poskim. Sefardim: Ohr Letsion forbids; Rav Ovadiah permits (praiseworthy to be strict).

Facial/hand creams, petroleum jelly

Assur miderabanan.

Toothpaste

Assur miderabanan (Rav Moshe; Mishnah Berurah; accepted minhag). Sefardim: Ohr Letsion forbids; Rav Ovadiah permits if needed for health.

Medicinal cream on infant's rash

Permitted - may press it on (not smear) if the child is a Choleh she'ein bo sakana. Also permitted under a diaper, spread by the baby's movement.

Liquid soap

Most Poskim permit (incl. Rav Elyashiv). Rav Moshe and Rav Berkovits are strict. Can be diluted with water on one's hand to satisfy the strict view.

Baby oil / olive oil

Permitted.

Stepping on saliva on the ground

Permitted - intent is for it to be absorbed, not smoothed. If one intends to smooth it: forbidden.

Heating wax candle to stick to holder

Forbidden (Be'er Heitev). Some forbid even touching wax lest one smooth it.

p. 254Memachek — Smoothing

3. Memachek B'Ochlin - Smoothing Foods

The Rishonim and Acharonim debate whether Memachek applies to foods at all, and if so, to what degree.

StatusConditionsSource / Basis

Assur midoraisa

Smoothing food for a non-food purpose (e.g., plugging a crack with chewing gum or sticky candy).

The food is being used as a building material - full Memachek applies.

Assur miderabanan

Food that is inedible without being smoothed.

Magen Avraham (SA 321, sk 24); Mordechai.

Permitted

Food is edible without smoothing; intent is simply to spread it to all areas.

Rama (SA 321:19); Magen Avraham; Biur Halacha.

Permitted, but praiseworthy to be strict

Food is edible without smoothing; intent is aesthetic (to make it thin or decorative).

Mordechai; Rama: 'Hamachmir tavo alav bracha.' Biur Halacha: this only applies when intent is for aesthetic thinning, not spreading.

Practical Cases

CaseRuling

Plugging a crack with chewing gum or sticky candy

Assur midoraisa - used as a building material, not food.

Spreading icing on a cake (to cover it, not to decorate)

Permitted.

Smearing icing decoratively / to achieve a smooth aesthetic effect

Praiseworthy to be strict (tavo alav bracha). Not strictly forbidden.

Smoothing egg salad for aesthetic purposes

Praiseworthy to avoid.

Mashing banana into a decorative shape

Praiseworthy to avoid. (Note: Chazon Ish forbids mashing banana altogether due to Tochein; most Poskim permit but are lechatchila strict.)

Spreading butter / jam on bread

Permitted - intent is to spread it, not to smooth for aesthetic thinning.

Bottom Line

The key questions: (1) Is the substance solid, semi-solid, or liquid? (2) Is the intent to smooth a surface, or merely to spread/cover? (3) Is the food inedible without being smoothed, or is the smoothing purely aesthetic?

p. 257Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

Boneh, Soser V'Makeh V'Patish

PART A: BONEH

1. Background & Shiur

Source in the Mishkan

The walls of the Mishkan were formed by assembling specially designed wooden planks. Assembling them = the Melacha of Boneh.

Shiur for chiyuv

Kol shehu - the minimum possible amount (Mishna, Shabbos 102b). Even a tiny act of building creates chiyuv, as long as it can last.

Examples of Boneh

Filling in a hole in a dirt floor, leveling the ground, making a wall.

p. 258Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

2. Building a Wall - Machlokes Rishonim

AuthorityBottom stone (no cement)Top layer (no cement)

Rashi + Tosefos

CHAYAV - no cement needed; straightening into place suffices

CHAYAV - stable even without cement

Ramban

Not assur mid'oraisa

Not assur mid'oraisa

Rambam

Not Boneh doraisa - would be Makeh V'Patish

Not chayav unless cement under it

3. Mosif Al HaBinyan - Adding to an Existing Building

Permanent addition

FORBIDDEN - Mosif al habinyan; appears as adding a foreign object to the structure.

Bolt/peg inserted temporarily (condition 1)

Must be planned before Shabbos to insert. Normally removed and replaced.

Bolt/peg inserted temporarily (condition 2)

May not be intended to remain permanently. If permanent: must be attached by string/rope.

Foreign material inserted (e.g. clothing)

PERMITTED even without pre-planning - not the normal function of the window.

p. 259Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

4. Mechitsa Arai - Temporary Walls

AuthorityMechitsa for Tznius/KavodMechitsa Hamateres (enables carrying etc.)

Rashi

PERMITTED

PERMITTED

Tosefos

PERMITTED

FORBIDDEN (mid'rabanan)

Mechaber / Rama (SA 315:1)

PERMITTED

FORBIDDEN

Chazon Ish

FORBIDDEN if hung permanently

-

Permitted: curtain in front of a door (tznius); Paroches of an Aron Kodesh; wall to block sun/wind/candles. Forbidden: Mechitsa hamateres; wall for marital purposes in front of a candle (Rama).

p. 260Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

5. Unblocking a Drain or Toilet on Shabbos

Gemara (Kesubos 60a)

Assur mid'oraisa to unblock a pipe normally; permitted with a shinui (unusual manner) in private, in a case of loss.

Shevisas HaShabbos

Unblocking normally = Boneh - makes the pipe usable again.

Be'er Moshe

Severely blocked pipe = assur mid'oraisa. Toilet/sink: a minor blockage is not significant - permitted even normally and even with a plunger.

Chelkas Yaakov

Unblocking a drain = issur derabanan of Tikkun Maneh - permitted for kavod habriyos.

Rav Moshe Feinstein

Strict: only permits if the drain clogs very commonly. If totally blocked - ask a non-Jew in great need.

Bottom line: Many poskim permit unblocking a toilet/sink in a time of need. Rav Moshe is strict.

p. 261Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

PART B: BINYAN B'KEILIM

6. The Core Machlokes: Ein vs. Yesh Binyan B'Keilim

The Question: Does the Melacha of Boneh apply to assembling vessels (keilim), or only to structures attached to the ground?

AuthorityPositionBasis / Limits

Rashi

EIN binyan b'keilim - Boneh never applies to any kli (under 40 seah)

Only building houses/shelters = Boneh; kli > 40 seah IS subject to Boneh

Tosefos

YESH binyan b'keilim - building a new kli can be Boneh mid'oraisa

Only reassembling (not building anew) = Ein binyan. Applies only to 'binyan gamur'

Halacha

Follows Tosefos - Ein binyan b'keilim applies only to minor/reassembly

Building a kli anew or in a very firm manner = Yesh binyan b'keilim

The 40-seah rule: All agree that a kli holding 40+ seah is not considered a 'kli' for halacha - full Issur Boneh doraisa applies to it (Rashi; Eruvin 34b).

p. 262Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

7. The Three Levels of Tightness in Assembling a Kli

Derech Rafui

Weak/loose connection. Kol Bo: parts move in the hole. Smag (halacha): easy to separate the parts - even tight grooves if easily pressed apart.

Derech Mehudak

Firm/moderate connection. Smag: strength or expertise needed to separate. Magen Avraham: screwing = takua. Taz: screwing = mehudak.

Derech Takua

Very strong, peg-like connection - parts are fully locked into place.

Halacha by Level of Tightness

Normal derech of this kliAssembling b'derech rafuiAssembling b'derech mehudakAssembling b'derech takua

Normally rafui

PERMITTED (all)

-

-

Normally mehudak

PERMITTED for Shabbos need (MB) Chazon Ish: always permitted

FORBIDDEN unless sorech gadol (SA HaRav)

-

Normally takua

FORBIDDEN (Hagahos Ashri; MB) PERMITTED (Rosh; Chazon Ish)

FORBIDDEN

ASSUR MID'ORAISA

p. 263Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

Key practical rule: Screwing the lid of a baby bottle or kli = PERMITTED. The Chazon Ish and Rav Karelitz: opening/closing is the kli's regular shimush - not Boneh at all.

Lego: Rafui (Rav Auerbach). Permitted for children. Adults - forbidden (may be building a new structure). High-chair tray with easy-press groove = rafui = permitted.

Breaking a stable kli < 40 seah

Rashi/Gra: permitted. Tosefos/MB: forbidden.

Depends on core machlokes

Machloket: is the cap already a complete kli?

p. 264Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

Rav Moshe's Gezeira: Despite the above heteirim, Rav Moshe issued a general prohibition against opening all packets/vessels/boxes on Shabbos. Not universally followed. Best practice: open everything before Shabbos.

p. 265Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

PART C: OHEL

10. Ohel - Building a Shelter

Ohel kavua (permanent shelter)

ASSUR MID'ORAISA - Rambam

Ohel arai (temporary shelter) - making both shelter + walls

ASSUR MID'RABANAN - Gezeira lest one make Ohel kavua (Rambam)

Adding to an existing Ohel arai

PERMITTED - Tosefes Ohel arai (Rambam; SA 315:2)

Making shelter alone - purpose is shade

FORBIDDEN even without walls (or walls pre-made) - Rosh; Mechaber

Making shelter alone - no shade purpose, no use for air below

PERMITTED - all agree (Ran; SA 315:7; MB)

Making shelter alone - air below has a use but purpose is not shade

DISPUTED: Tosefos permits if no walls/walls pre-made; Rashba forbids; BH strict except shaas hadchak

p. 267Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

Unfolding an Existing Ohel

ActionStatusReason / Authority

Opening a folded chair

PERMITTED

Rashi: no addition made. Rach: not made for air below. MB rules like Rashi.

Upturning a bed to its legs

PERMITTED

Same - Rashi; Rach; MB

Opening a chupa (connected to poles from Erev Shabbos)

PERMITTED - MB rules like Rashi

Even if made for air underneath - Magen Avraham; MB

p. 268Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

Tosefes Ohel Arai - Adding to an Existing Shelter

Condition for Tosefes Ohel

Roof already open a tefach before Shabbos, OR attached to poles/frame by strings.

Stroller roof (attached to frame)

PERMITTED to open - Tosefes Ohel arai

Rain cover attached to stroller

PERMITTED if attached from before Shabbos - or even unattached if already open a tefach

Spreading a Tallis (threads pre-attached)

PERMITTED - pulling threads = adding to Ohel, not building it (Gemara 138a)

Kilat Chattanim

PERMITTED to open/close if roof < 1 tefach and designed for this use (SA 315:11)

The Rif's three-part stringency: (1) Ohel with roof ≥ 1 tefach = assur mid'oraisa even if temporary. (2) Roof < 1 tefach = still assur mid'rabanan. (3) Pre-attached string only helps if roof < 1 tefach. The Mechaber follows the Rif.

1. Tzovaya (Dyeing)

A. Tzovaya L'Zman - Temporary DyeingA. Tzovaya L'Zman - Temporary Dyeing

Category

Ruling

Permanent coloring

Assur mid'oraisa

Temporary coloring (fades on its own, short time)

Assur mid'rabanan

If color is easily removed

Assur mid'rabanan

Color intended to be temporary - machlokes

Smag: assur mid'oraisa. Rambam / Mechaber: assur mid'rabanan. Halacha follows Rambam.

No Tzovaya mid'oraisa on human skin

Because color is not absorbed - only issur derabanan for cosmetics

Cases

Cases

Cosmetics (rouge, lipstick, eyeshadow)

Assur mid'rabanan - temporary effect

Talcum powder on skin

Machlokes: Rav Moshe & Rav Scheinberg - muttar; RSZ Auerbach & Rav Wosner - assur mid'rabanan

Water paint on glass/metal

Assur mid'rabanan - easily wiped

Crayon on formica/metal

Assur mid'rabanan

p. 276Various — Part 1
B. Tzovaya b'Ochlin - Staining with Food / Wiping StainsB. Tzovaya b'Ochlin - Staining with Food / Wiping Stains

Opinion

Position

Yeraim

Assur mid'rabanan to wipe a stain with cloth (psik reisha d'loh nichah leih); forbids covering wound with clothing

Radbaz / Agur

Permitted - Derech lichluch (abnormal way)

Magen Avraham

Rules like Yeraim; same-color cloth is certainly forbidden

Mishnah Berurah / Elyah Rabbah

Ideally follow Yeraim; avoid same-color cloth; wash blood off first if possible

Shemiras Shabbos / Rav Ribiat

Permitted to use disposable paper towel or tissue

Rav Berkovits

Permits rag used specifically for stains; not a regular hand towel

C. Common Modern Tzovaya QuestionsC. Common Modern Tzovaya Questions

Case

Ruling

Color-changing thermometer

RSZ Auerbach: lenient in case of need (very temporary, nothing new added). If letters appear - depends on whether outline was pre-existing.

Photochromic (darkening) glasses

Most Poskim permit: part of normal function, very temporary, possibly indirect (gramma factor)

Sunbathing / getting a tan

Shemiras Shabbos: permitted; Minchas Yitzchak: forbidden. Walking in sun without intent - permitted to all.

Colored toilet disinfectant

Tzitz Eliezer, Ohr L'Tzion, Rav Ovadia: lenient (psik reisha d'loh nichah leih + eino miskayem + gramma). Rav Auerbach, Rav Wosner, Orchos Shabbos: remove before Shabbos. If not removed - kavod habrios considerations apply.

Removing nail polish

Permitted unless intending to re-polish immediately after

2. Netilas Neshama - Killing, Wounding, and Causing Bleeding

A. Killing Animals - Practical HalachaA. Killing Animals - Practical Halacha

Type of Animal

Halacha

Poisonous / life-threatening (e.g., rabid dog, poisonous snake, scorpion)

Permitted to kill - even if not presently chasing

Causes significant pain but not life-threatening, presently pursuing

Permitted to kill

Causes significant pain, not pursuing

Only permitted to step on inconspicuously

Causes some pain (e.g., non-poisonous hornet)

Forbidden to kill outright; permitted to trap or step on

General insect infestation

Forbidden to spray/sprinkle poison. Permitted to spray perimeter if in kitchen.

Lice

SA: permitted (do not reproduce normally). Modern lice do reproduce - Rav Dessler & RSZ Auerbach: permit; Rav Elyashiv: strict (permits if causing pain to child).

B. Causing Bleeding - Halacha L'MaasehB. Causing Bleeding - Halacha L'Maaseh

Principle

Detail

Which melacha?

Rashi/Tosefos: Netilas Neshama. Rambam: Dosh. Halacha follows Rashi/Tosefos.

Chiyuv requires

Constructive purpose (e.g., feeding animal, weakening it, Rambam: even anger)

Hitting with anger

Rambam: assur mid'oraisa. Raavad: assur mid'rabanan.

Psik reisha - no benefit from bleeding

Assur mid'rabanan

Cases

Cases

Removing scab likely to bleed

Forbidden

Forbidden (almost certainly bleeds). In great pain - ask non-Jew.

Removing splinter (may cause some blood)

Permitted - blood is undesired (at worst derabanan); Chazal permit for pain

Blood test on Shabbos

Assur mid'oraisa; only permitted for pikuach nefesh

3. Tzod (Trapping)

Confining an animal

A. Mino Nitzod vs. Ein B'Mino NitzodA. Mino Nitzod vs. Ein B'Mino Nitzod

Category

Examples / Halacha

Mino nitzod (commonly trapped)

Rabbits (fur/food), parrots (pets). Trapping = issur d'oraisa with narrow confinement.

Ein b'mino nitzod (not commonly confined)

Flies. Trapping = assur mid'rabanan only.

Honey bees - machlokes

Beis Yosef: Mino nitzod. Most Poskim: Ein b'mino nitzod (beekeeper fosters, not truly traps).

B. Levels of Confinement

B. Levels of Confinement

Narrow confinement

Assur mid'oraisa

Loose confinement

Assur mid'rabanan

Further confining already-loosely-confined animal

Permitted as long as does not reach narrow confinement

Adequacy of confinement

Must match the animal - a dog's cage is inadequate for a lion; high walls trap dogs but not birds

p. 280Various — Part 1
C. Trapping Flies - Halacha L'MaasehC. Trapping Flies - Halacha L'Maaseh

Case

Ruling

Intentionally trapping a fly

Assur mid'rabanan (fly = ein b'mino nitzod)

Closing small box with fly inside

Tur: permits (hard to catch fly even from small box). Sefer HaTerumah: forbids. Mishnah Berurah: strict like Sefer HaTerumah.

Closing large box with fly inside

All agree: permitted (too loose to be meaningful confinement)

Unsure if fly is in box (safek psik reisha)

Taz: permits. Mishnah Berurah: permits (only d'rabanan concern). Chazon Ish: strict.

D. Trapping Harmful Animals - Halacha L'Maaseh

D. Trapping Harmful Animals - Halacha L'Maaseh

Category

Ruling

Life-threatening animals

Permitted to trap (and kill - see Section 2A)

Animals causing considerable pain

Permitted to trap

Animals causing some pain, on person's body

Permitted to hold and throw; forbidden to trap if not on body

Insects causing discomfort / preventing sleep

Rav Karelitz: permitted to trap. RSZ Auerbach: forbidden. Ask a Rav.

Ruling

Opening/closing book with writing on edge

Permitted - kreivah/richuk of existing letters is not koseiv

Assur mid'rabanan (Maharam MiRottenberg). Adult should not give child such food.

Tearing letters on food and eating them

More serious - letters can never be rejoined

Cutting letters on a packet

Subject to discussion - practical rule: cut between letters where possible

Discussed in shiurim

Rabbinic extensions related to Koseiv

7. Hachana (Preparation)

Preparing on Shabbos for after Shabbos

A. Core RulesA. Core Rules

Hachana is forbidden because it constitutes unnecessary tircha on Shabbos for a weekday purpose.

The issur applies equally to preparing on Shabbos for after Shabbos, on Yom Tov Rishon for Yom Tov Sheini, and on Shabbos for Yom Tov.

Actions that have a benefit for Shabbos itself are permitted even if they also benefit after Shabbos.

Hachana is forbidden because it constitutes unnecessary tircha on Shabbos for a weekday purpose.

The issur applies equally to preparing on Shabbos for after Shabbos, on Yom Tov Rishon for Yom Tov Sheini, and on Shabbos for Yom Tov.

Actions that have a benefit for Shabbos itself are permitted even if they also benefit after Shabbos.

Case

Ruling

Making bed for kavod Shabbos

Permitted - benefit for Shabbos

Washing dishes to be used later on Shabbos

Permitted

Washing dishes (not needed again on Shabbos)

Many Poskim permit if it would be unpleasant to leave dirty dishes visible

Washing dishes primarily to avoid post-Shabbos cleanup

Forbidden

Washing ten dishes when only one is needed

Permitted

Soaking dishes on Shabbos

Discussed separately - depends on circumstances

B. Avsha Milsa - Activating Noisy Appliances Before ShabbosB. Avsha Milsa - Activating Noisy Appliances Before Shabbos

Issur: Causing noisy vessels (e.g., washing machine, dryer, dishwasher) to operate on Shabbos.

Issur: Causing noisy vessels (e.g., washing machine, dryer, dishwasher) to operate on Shabbos.

The concern: people will think the melacha was done on Shabbos.

Case

Ruling

Washing machine / dryer / dishwasher set to run on Shabbos

Forbidden. Rav Ben-Tzion Abba Shaul: forbidden even by Mechaber's standard.

9. Molid Reyach

Creating a New Fragrance on Shabbos

Core Halacha - Molid ReyachCore Halacha - Molid Reyach

Chazal forbade adding new smells to objects or people on Shabbos.

Chazal forbade adding new smells to objects or people on Shabbos.

Question

Positions

Does issur apply to body?

Taz, Shulchan Aruch HaRav, Kaf HaChaim: strict. Chacham Zvi, Ginas Veradim, Mishnah Berurah: lenient.

Unintentional molid reyach

Rama: strict. Maharshal / Taz: lenient. Mishnah Berurah: strict except time of great need.

Cases

Cases

Deodorant / perfume on body

Lenient Poskim (Mishnah Berurah camp): permitted; strict Poskim: forbidden

Insect spray on clothing

Orchos Shabbos: lenient - molid reyach applies only to pleasant smells

Air freshener

Permitted - no issur molid reyach in the air

Colored toilet disinfectant (smell aspect)

Rav Karelitz: lenient - intent is to remove bad smell (Sheilas Yaavetz)

10. Rechitsa

10. Rechitsa

Washing on Shabbos

A. The Fundamental Gezeira

A. The Fundamental Gezeira

Chazal forbade bathing with hot water on Shabbos due to concerns about bathhouse attendants heating water on Shabbos.

Two categories apply, each with different leniencies.

Chazal forbade bathing with hot water on Shabbos due to concerns about bathhouse attendants heating water on Shabbos.

Two categories apply, each with different leniencies.

Water Type

What is Permitted

Mayim she'huchmu m'Erev Shabbos (heated before Shabbos)

Permitted: hands, face, feet. Also individual limbs - as long as not majority of body in one session.

Mayim she'huchmu b'Shabbos (heated on Shabbos, even permissibly)

Generally forbidden. Exception: situation of pain - entire body permitted.

Heated on Erev Shabbos but completed on Shabbos

Status disputed by Acharonim - discussed extensively in shiurim

B. Special Cases

B. Special Cases

Case

Ruling

Washing a young child with hot water on Shabbos

Subject to discussion - health considerations may apply

Using hot water in the Mikveh on Shabbos

Discussed in dedicated shiur - see Rechitsa Shiur 3

Cold shower / bath / swimming

Generally permitted - Rechitsa gezeira applies only to hot water

1. Oneg Shabbos and Kavod Shabbos1. Oneg Shabbos and Kavod Shabbos

Status of the Obligation

Status of the Obligation

Authority / Position

Ruling

Oneg & Kavod Shabbos - general

Divrei Kabbala (from Yeshaya 58:13) - not Torah-level, but treated with great seriousness. Divrei Sofrim are more severe than Divrei Torah (Shaar Hatsion).

Ramban

Oneg Shabbos may be a Mitzva doraisa - derived from "Shabbos Shabbason / mikra kodesh" in the Torah

Sefer HaChinuch / Beis Yosef

Miderabanan

Fasting on Shabbos

Forbidden - mevatel Oneg Shabbos. Even for one hour if intent is to fast. Certainly forbidden until chatzos.

Counting Toward Shabbos - Zachor

Counting Toward Shabbos - Zachor

Zachor es Yom HaShabbos

Mitzva to count each day from Shabbos (e.g., "today is the first day from Shabbos"). Fulfilled by mentioning the day before Shir Shel Yom.

Buying Food for Shabbos

Buying Food for Shabbos

Ideal practice (Shammai's approach)

Buy food earlier in the week if it will be well-preserved by Shabbos and may not be available later. If food is definitely available Erev Shabbos, buying then is more clearly l'kavod Shabbos.

Hillel's approach

Waited until Erev Shabbos out of bitachon - only appropriate for one on that level. For everyone else, Shammai's approach is correct.

p. 298Various — Part 2

2. Takanas Ezra - Laundry on Thursday

Core HalachaCore Halacha

The Takana

Ezra decreed that laundry should be done on Thursday, so that one enters Shabbos with clean clothing.

Opinion

Position

Magen Avraham

Equally acceptable to do laundry on any earlier day of the week

Elyah Rabbah

Davka on Thursday

General rule

Many Poskim: one does not have to wash all clothing unless it is dirty

Applies Nowadays?

Applies Nowadays?

Most Poskim

Yes - applies even though laundry is done far quicker than in the times of the takana

Rav Ovadia Yosef

Does not apply nowadays

Thursday Night

Thursday Night

Rav Karelitz

Takana applies to Thursday night as well

Rav Abba Shaul

Does not apply Thursday night. Also: applies only if one does not have a dryer (even with a machine). In time of need, may do laundry Erev Shabbos without a dryer.

p. 299Various — Part 2

3. Erev Shabbos Preparations

Getting Up Early / General PreparationsGetting Up Early / General Preparations

Obligation

One should get up early to begin preparations. Everyone must do some preparations - even talmidei chachamim, even menial tasks, for the sake of Shabbos.

Challah

Challah

Traditional practice

Women would make their own challah on Erev Shabbos. Biur Halacha: one should not mevatel this minhag.

Nowadays (bakery challah)

Rav Abba Shaul: minhag does not apply with same severity. Rav Elyashiv: does not apply if one prefers the bakery challah.

What to Eat on Shabbos

What to Eat on Shabbos

Chashuv food

Eating chashuv (impressive) food fulfils Oneg and Kavod Shabbos, but there is no obligation if one does not enjoy it

Hot food

One should not avoid hot food unless it is harmful

Fish

Inyan to eat fish; but if one does not enjoy it, no need to eat it

Two tavshilin

Inyan to have two cooked dishes at each seudah

Personal Preparation - Washing and Grooming

Personal Preparation - Washing and Grooming

Washing

Mitzva to wash face, hands, and feet with hot water on Erev Shabbos. Tur: ideally wash whole body. Praiseworthy to go to mikveh.

Nails

Mitzva to cut nails on Erev Shabbos (not Sunday - superstition concern). Various minhagim on which fingers to start with.

Hair

If hair is long, should cut it on Erev Shabbos

p. 300Various — Part 2

4. Travelling and Eating on Erev Shabbos

CaseRuling

Travelling on Erev Shabbos

Permitted, but should try to arrive at destination at least one hour before Shabbos starts

Big seudah on Erev Shabbos

Forbidden unless Seudas Mitzva b'zman (e.g., bris). Even then, ideally begin before chatzos.

Eating until Shabbos

Permitted, but a mitzva not to be kovaya seudah - should not set a regular meal

Erev Shabbos that is Erev Yom Tov - Seudah Shlishis

Ideally begin before nine and a half hours into the halachic day

Doing melachah after Mincha Ketanah

Forbidden unless l'sorekh Shabbos

Store owner

Should close at least one hour before Shabbos begins

p. 301Various — Part 2

5. Tosefes Shabbos

Adding time to Shabbos

Is There a Chiyuv?Is There a Chiyuv?

Opinion

Position

Rov Rishonim

Mitzva doraisa to begin Shabbos before it technically starts - halacha follows this view

Rambam

No mitzva doraisa of Tosefes Shabbos

Beis Yosef (understanding Rambam)

Not even a mitzva derabanan

Gra (understanding Rambam)

There is a mitzva derabanan

When Must One Begin Tosefes Shabbos?

When Must One Begin Tosefes Shabbos?

Rabbeinu Tam / Mechaber approach

Issur melacha begins long after first shekiah (bein hashmashos is ~1 hour after first shekiah). Tosefes Shabbos is before first shekiah.

Mishnah Berurah

Must begin Tosefes Shabbos before the first shekiah

Some Rishonim

Chiyuv is only a kol shehu (tiny amount) before Shabbos begins

Most Rishonim

A significant amount of time before Shabbos begins

How to Accept Tosefes Shabbos

How to Accept Tosefes Shabbos

Many Rishonim

Suffices to lifrosh mimelacha - stop melacha - with kavannah to fulfil the mitzva

Some Rishonim / Mishnah Berurah

Must verbally acknowledge Shabbos

Practical ruling

Ideally verbally acknowledge Shabbos (Rav Elyashiv, Rav Wosner also). M'ikar hadin: lifrosh mimelacha suffices.

If davening Mincha close to shekiah

Should lifrosh mimelacha before Mincha if no time to verbally bring in Shabbos

Tosefes Shabbos of the Tzibbur

Tosefes Shabbos of the Tzibbur

If majority of shul accepted Shabbos

Minority may not do melacha, but may still daven Mincha

Multiple shuls in neighborhood

Bound by the latest shul, not by majority

One shul in one's nusach

Rav Elyashiv: bound by that shul. Rav Abba Shaul: unsure.

Family / Wife

Family / Wife

When husband accepts Shabbos

Poskim dispute whether family must stop melacha. Permitted to do issurei derabanan in bein hashmashos unless tzibbur already accepted.

Tosefes Shabbos at end of Shabbos

Obligation exists but no need to have kavannah. Piskei Teshuvos: praiseworthy to intend to fulfil the mitzva.

p. 302–303Various — Part 2

6. Hadlakas Neiros

Shabbos candles

The ChiyuvThe Chiyuv

Nature of obligation

Obligatory. Three reasons: (1) Kavod Shabbos, (2) Oneg Shabbos, (3) Shalom Bayis. All three apply in different ways.

Where to light

Must eat where one lights. If very unpleasant to eat there, may eat elsewhere.

How Many Neiros?

How Many Neiros?

Basic obligation

One ner. Accepted halacha: two neiros.

Various minhagim

Some add more (e.g., one per child). A woman may light per her minhag; husband should ideally pay but is not obligated.

The Penalty (Knas)

The Penalty (Knas)

Forgot to light

Must add one additional ner every Shabbos from then on

When knas applies

Machlokes in various cases - ask a Rav for specific situations

Who Lights?

Who Lights?

Primary responsibility

The woman. Good for the man to be involved.

Man living alone

Must light neiros

Wife not home

Machlokes whether man should light, or a girl above Bas Mitzvah

Some minhagim

All girls in the home light with a bracha

Blind woman

May light with a bracha. If married, husband should ideally light and say the bracha.

What to Light With

What to Light With

Ideal oil

Olive oil (Mechaber). Some Poskim: regular candles even more ideal (no shema yateh concern).

Electric lights

If cannot light a flame: may use electric lights with a bracha (most Poskim). Rav Auerbach: battery-powered flashlight if possible. Rav Elyashiv: electric or fluorescent bulbs acceptable.

The Bracha - Light First or Bracha First?

The Bracha - Light First or Bracha First?

Mechaber

Say bracha first, then light

Rama / Ashkenaz minhag

Light first (covering eyes), then say bracha

Rav Ovadia Yosef

All Sefardim should say bracha first, even if minhag was otherwise

Rav Abba Shaul

May follow one's minhag; if no minhag - bracha first

Men

Never mekabel Shabbos with the hadlaka regardless of order

Mekabeles Shabbos with the Bracha

Mekabeles Shabbos with the Bracha

Behag

Woman is mekabeles Shabbos with hadlaka

Rosh / Mechaber

Woman is NOT mekabeles Shabbos with hadlaka

Ashkenaz minhag (Rama)

Woman IS mekabeles Shabbos with the bracha

Special Cases - Away from Home

Special Cases - Away from Home

Case

Ruling

Man away from home (wife lights at home)

Fulfils obligation through wife's lighting, unless he has his own room where he stays and there is sufficient light so he won't stumble.

Different time zones from wife

Poskim dispute whether still exempted

Wife away from home (husband home)

Same exemption - husband fulfils through wife's lighting

Both husband and wife away from home

Husband is NOT exempted from his obligation

Guests

Guests

Guest without own room, wife not lighting at home

Must mishtatef b'prutah if eating own food in host's home

Guest eating host's food

Machlokes whether exempted or must mishtatef b'prutah

Kavua - definition (Rav Elyashiv)

30 days

Multiple People Lighting in Same Place

Multiple People Lighting in Same Place

Mechaber

Second person cannot say bracha

Rama / Ashkenaz minhag

Second person says a bracha

Electric lights present

Shvus Yitzchak: second woman cannot say bracha (adds no light). Acharonim debate cases where ner adds very little light.

Electric Lights Already On

Electric Lights Already On

Accepted minhag

Light neiros with bracha even when electric lights are on

Ideal practice (Rav Elyashiv, Rav Berkovits)

Turn on electric lights immediately before lighting neiros so bracha covers both

Lighting in a bedroom

Must ensure that without the neiros the room would be dark enough to risk stumbling

Hotel / Hospital

Hotel / Hospital

Hotel - cannot light in makom achila or bedroom

Cannot say bracha. May light electric light in bedroom and say bracha on that.

Bathroom light

Poskim debate if bracha may be said

Woman in hospital

Technically need not light if husband lights at home and some light in her room. But many Poskim: should light. Cannot say bracha unless in makom achila or bedroom.

Bachurim in Yeshiva

Bachurim in Yeshiva

Obligation

Poskim dispute if bachur needs to mishtatef and if he can light with bracha in his bedroom

p. 304–307Various — Part 2

7. Kiddush

Friday night and Shabbos morning

The ObligationThe Obligation

Doraisa component

Mitzva doraisa to mention (verbally sanctify) Shabbos at its onset - "Zachor es Yom HaShabbos"

Kiddush on wine

Rishonim and Acharonim dispute whether kiddush on wine is doraisa. Most Poskim hold it is miderabanan.

Man motsi wife who has not davened Maariv

Generally no problem - most Poskim permit

Timing

Timing

When to make Kiddush

Ideally as soon as he arrives home, unless not hungry

Eating before Kiddush

Forbidden to eat or drink anything before Kiddush

Children above chinuch before Kiddush

Most Poskim: permitted to eat/drink for health. Debate if permitted for other food.

Covering the Challah

Covering the Challah

Must cover challah

Yes - at all Shabbos meals (some lenient for Seudah Shlishis)

One sitting at different table

Poskim debate if must cover challah if not drinking the wine

Mezonos at Kiddush

Poskim debate if must cover mezonos

The Position During Kiddush

The Position During Kiddush

Sitting vs. standing

Different minhagim. Various hiddurim for holding the Kiddush cup.

Netilas Yadayim - before or after Kiddush?

Mechaber: wash after Kiddush (if washed first, make Kiddush on bread). Rama / common Ashkenaz minhag: wash first. Mishnah Berurah: follows Mechaber, but bdi eved if washed first - may make Kiddush on wine. Everyone but Mekadesh may wash first even per Mechaber.

The Kiddush Cup

The Kiddush Cup

Condition of cup

Must be whole and unblemished. Should use a nice cup.

No proper cup available

May use a disposable cup. If none - use the bottle.

Size

Must hold at least a reviis. Be strict for shiur of 137 cubic centimeters for night Kiddush.

Filling the cup

Should be filled to the brim. If not possible, may add foreign matter.

p. 308–309Various — Part 2
Wine and AlternativesWine and Alternatives

Type

Ruling

Wine vs. grape juice

Ideally use wine. If one prefers grape juice - permitted. Rav Elyashiv: grape juice that can never become wine is pasul for Kiddush; most Poskim disagree.

Red vs. white wine

Mechaber: permitted to use white, but red is preferable unless one prefers white. Ramban: white is pasul bdi eved.

Cooked wine

Mechaber: permitted, uncooked is preferable. Machlokes Rishonim.

Chamar Medinah - for Shabbos Morning Kiddush

Chamar Medinah - for Shabbos Morning Kiddush

Night Kiddush - no wine available

Make Kiddush on bread (not chamar medinah). May make on bread even if prefers bread over wine.

Morning Kiddush - no wine

Use chamar medinah (e.g., whisky). May NOT make on bread in the morning.

What qualifies as chamar medinah?

Beer, orange juice, whisky: generally yes. Coffee/tea: machlokes. Soda: machlokes. Chazon Ish: nothing qualifies nowadays.

Drinking the Wine

Drinking the Wine

Mekadesh should drink

A maleh lugmav (majority of a reviis)

If only another person drank maleh lugmav

Rishonim dispute. Mechaber: good to be strict but yotsi bdi eved.

Combined drinking

If multiple people combined to drink a maleh lugmav together - all are yotsi

Kiddush b'Makom Seudah

Kiddush b'Makom Seudah

Ideal

Meal must be eaten in same place as Kiddush was made

Leaving the house between Kiddush and meal

Should not leave. Bdi eved - fulfils obligation.

Hefsek between Kiddush and meal

Ideally eat immediately. Hefsekim for sake of the meal are not a problem.

Had to leave after Kiddush before eating

Does not need to make Kiddush again when he returns

What Constitutes a Seudah?

What Constitutes a Seudah?

Praiseworthy

Eat bread after Kiddush - fulfils all opinions

Accepted minhag

Mezonos after Kiddush

Maaseh kedeirah

Acceptable

Rice

Poskim debate

Fruit

Generally insufficient. If weak with no chameshes haminim food - may eat fruit.

Morning Kiddush - maleh lugmav

In need, Mekadesh may drink a reviis instead. Others need only a reviis. If necessary even Mekadesh can drink only a reviis.

Saying Kiddush Oneself vs. Hearing It

Saying Kiddush Oneself vs. Hearing It

Ideal

One person says for all - "b'rov am hadras Melech"

Listener's requirements

Must have daas to be exempted. Acharonim debate if must also say Amen bdi eved - seems yotsi regardless.

Mekadesh already fulfilled his chiyuv

Can still motsi others through arvus

One who has not accepted Shabbos motsi others

Rav Auerbach: lenient only in shaas hadchak

Morning Kiddush

Morning Kiddush

Nature of obligation

Miderabanan

Content

Ikar Kiddush is the blessing on wine. Different customs on which pesukim to add.

Standing vs. sitting

Most common minhag: sit. Some stand.

Woman before davening - obligated?

Poskim debate

Sick person permitted to eat before davening

Must make Kiddush first

p. 310–312Various — Part 2

8. Shabbos Meals

Three meals on Shabbos

The ChiyuvThe Chiyuv

Who is obligated

Men and women - three meals with bread on Shabbos

If cannot eat bread

Exempt from bread but must still eat meals

Amount of bread

Acharonim debate: more than a kebeitzah, or a kezayis

Pas kisnin

Debate on how much pas kisnin to eat to say Hamotsi and Birchas Hamazon

Times of the Three Meals

Times of the Three Meals

Meal

Time

Friday night meal

Can eat until dawn; ideally begin soon after nightfall. May begin from after plag hamincha; some Poskim: eat kezayis of bread after nightfall.

Shabbos morning meal

Most important meal. Should not overeat if it will prevent eating seudah shlishis. Aruch Hashulchan: before chatzos; most Poskim do not hold this strictly.

Seudah Shlishis

Must eat after time of Mincha (some Poskim lenient). Ideally pray Mincha first. Should begin before it gets too late. Preferable to eat meat or fish rather than fruit.

Melaveh Malka

Melaveh Malka

Obligation

Mitzva to eat a meal after Shabbos (Melaveh Malka). Most Poskim: women also obligated.

What to eat

Ideally bread. If unable: mezonos or fruit.

Eats kezayis of bread during seudah shlishis after nightfall

Some Poskim: fulfils Melaveh Malka. Others: requires a separate meal.

Minhag

Keep Shabbos clothes until after Melaveh Malka

p. 313–314Various — Part 2

Two loaves at Shabbos meals

9. Lechem Mishneh

Two loaves at Shabbos meals

The Obligation

The Obligation

Magen Avraham

Chiyuv miderabanan

Taz

Chiyuv midoraisa

Breaking the Loaf

Breaking the Loaf

Rashi, Rambam, Tur

Break only one loaf (Mechaber rules this way; Minhag follows Mechaber)

Rashba / Maharshal, Shelah, Gra

Must break both loaves

Which Loaf to Break?

Which Loaf to Break?

Friday night

Mechaber: break the lower loaf

All other meals (Shabbos day, Yom Tov night)

Rama: break the higher loaf

Bach

Always break the higher loaf

Magen Avraham

Put the loaf to break on top during Kiddush, then place it lower for Hamotsi

Taz

Hold lower loaf closer to one's body

Making a roshem (mark) before cutting

Poskim dispute whether this is better

How large a piece to break

Mitzva to break a large piece that will suffice for the entire meal

If One Does Not Have Two Whole Loaves

If One Does Not Have Two Whole Loaves

Have one whole and one broken

Use one whole + one broken loaf

Only broken loaves

Use two broken loaves

Loaf that broke in two

Connect with toothpick (not visible) - considered shalem. Cannot do with three pieces.

Sliced bread in a closed bag

NOT considered whole

Special Cases

Special Cases

Loaf one is generally strict not to eat from

Permitted to use for lechem mishneh

10. Havdala

Separating Shabbos from the weekday

Is Havdala Doraisa or Derabanan?Is Havdala Doraisa or Derabanan?

Machlokes Rishonim

Some: doraisa. Others: derabanan. Chazal fixed Havdala both in Shemoneh Esrei ("Atah chonantanu") and on a cup of wine.

Forgot "Atah chonantanu"

Does not need to repeat the Shemoneh Esrei

Who is Obligated?

Who is Obligated?

Person

Ruling

Women

Most Rishonim: obligated. Mechaber: brings both opinions; ikar is obligated. Rama/Taz: should not make Havdala for themselves. Bach/Magen Avraham/Mishnah Berurah: women may make Havdala for themselves.

Man making Havdala for woman (already fulfilled his own)

Ideally should not. In time of need: permitted.

Woman making Havdala for man

Ideally should not. In time of need: permitted.

Children (above chinuch)

Must hear Havdala (may eat first). Debate if child who went to sleep before end of Shabbos must hear next day.

Man motsi child in Havdala

Even if already fulfilled his own chiyuv

Child motsi adult

Only if adult said "hamavdil" and child has not. If child also said "hamavdil" - machlokes.

Blind person

Obligated in Havdala but cannot say bracha on fire for himself

Onein

May not hear Havdala. After burial - must hear Havdala unless after sunset on Tuesday.

Eating and Drinking Before Havdala

Eating and Drinking Before Havdala

After shekiah

Forbidden to eat or drink anything (except water) before making Havdala

Began eating bread before shekiah

May continue eating and drinking until he bentches

Began drinking before shekiah

Must stop at shekiah

Began eating mezonos before shekiah

Poskim debate if may continue

Doing Melacha Before Havdala

Doing Melacha Before Havdala

After nightfall without Havdala

Forbidden (machlokes if rabbinic or has Torah source)

How to permit Melacha

"Baruch hamavdil bein kodesh lechol", "Atah chonantanu" in Shemoneh Esrei, or Havdala on wine - all permit Melacha

Before Kedusha in Maariv

Ideal not to do Melacha until after Kedusha of Maariv

Asking others to do Melacha

Permitted even before Havdala

Lighting candles

One opinion permits without Havdala; Rama is strict

Zmanim of Havdala

Zmanim of Havdala

If did not make Havdala on Motsei Shabbos

Rama: may make until (not including) Tuesday night. Sefardi Poskim: debate.

Making Havdala before nightfall (onnes)

Mechaber: permits. Mishnah Berurah: only if cannot make it by Tuesday night.

Making Havdala before Maariv

Ideally daven Maariv first. In time of need: Havdala first.

p. 317–318Various — Part 2
The Havdala ProcedureThe Havdala Procedure

Element

Halacha

Cup of wine

Should overflow out of the cup. Various minhagim on standing vs. sitting.

Drinking the Havdala Wine

Drinking the Havdala Wine

Amount to drink

Must drink a maleh lugmav; ideally drink a reviis

Who drinks

Only one person should drink. If enough wine, others may drink the rest.

Women

Ideally do not drink the wine. If no man available - a woman should drink.

Besamim

Besamim

Why we smell besamim

To alleviate the loss of the neshama yeseirah at the end of Shabbos

Ashkenazim

Always say "borei minei besamim." Ideally use a spice with that bracha.

Sefardim

Say the fitting bracha for the specific spice. Use a hadas.

Fruit with pleasant smell

May use. Should wait until after making Havdala before smelling.

Havdala Candle (Ner)

Havdala Candle (Ner)

Mitzva

Mitzva to say bracha on a ner on Motsei Shabbos. May say until alos hashachar.

Women

Mishnah Berurah: not obligated. Many Poskim: may say the bracha. Debate.

Blind person

Cannot say bracha on the ner. Poskim unsure if can motsi others.

Type of ner

Ideally multi-wicked candle. May use a single flame. Must be lit in a permitted way, for the sake of giving light.

Electric bulb

Poskim debate if bracha may be said

Proximity

Must be close enough to potentially derive benefit from the ner

Bracha before or after benefit

Machlokes. Some do both (say bracha and then benefit, and then benefit again) to fulfil both opinions.

p. 319–320Various — Part 2

11. Kabbalas Shabbos and Tefila

Kabbalas ShabbosKabbalas Shabbos

Purpose

Minhag to say Kabbalas Shabbos as Shabbos enters - primary purpose is Kavod Shabbos

When Shabbos is brought in

"Boi b'kallah" (Lecha Dodi) brings in Shabbos, as does Barechu

Tefila Notes

Tefila Notes

Bracha before Krias Shema (Friday night)

Different ending. Bdi eved - yotsi if said weekday bracha.

"Veshamru" before Shemoneh Esrei

Most communities say it. Ashkenazim in Eretz Yisrael: do not say it, based on Gra.

Me'eyn Sheva (Magen Avos)

Me'eyn Sheva (Magen Avos)

When said

Friday night, after Shemoneh Esrei

Purpose

Said for those who arrive late to shul - condensed form of the Shabbos Amidah

Shabbos Shacharis Additions

Shabbos Shacharis Additions

Additions to Shacharis

Various additions to the Shabbos Shacharis service - discussed in shiurim

Chazzan repeating Shemoneh Esrei

Practical notes discussed in shiurim (including situation where person should say Shabbos Shemoneh Esrei himself)
